I could see him who was transferred by the servant of servants from the Arno to the Bacchiglione, where he left his weak nerves.

I would say more: But the coming and the speech cannot be longer, because I see fresh smoke rising from the sand there.

People are coming with whom I must not be. May my Treasure be commended to you, in whom I still live, and I ask no more."

Then he turned, and seemed to be one of those who run to Verona for the green flag across the countryside; and he seemed to be one of these

the winners, not the loser.

Inferno · Canto XVI

I was already in a place where the roar of the water falling in the other circle could be heard, like the roar of beehives,

when three shadows, running together, departed from a herd that was passing under the rain of bitter torment.

They came toward us, each crying: "Stop, you who by your dress seem to be one of our depraved land."

Alas, what wounds I saw in their limbs, recent and old, ignited by the flames! It pains me even less that I remember them.

At their cries, my Teacher listened; he turned his face toward me, and said, "Now wait, these must be courteous.

And if it were not for the fire that shoots from the nature of the place, I would say that haste would have been better for you than for them."

As soon as we stopped, they began their old verse again; and when they reached us, all three of them made a circle.

As champions do, naked and oiled, assessing their capture and their advantage, before they are beaten and stung by one another,

thus wheeling, each directed his gaze toward me, so that his neck made a continuous journey in opposition to his feet.

And "If the misery of this place alone makes us and our prayers scornful," one began, "and his stained and scorched appearance,

may our fame incline your mind to tell us who you are, who so safely trample your living feet through Hell.

This one, whose footprints you see me treading in, though he goes naked and hairless, was of greater rank than you believe:

he was the grandson of good Gualdrada; Guido Guerra was named, and in his life he accomplished much with his wit and his sword.

The other, who treads the sand near me, is Tegghiaio Aldobrandi, whose voice should have been welcome in the world above.

And I, who am placed on the cross with them, was Jacopo Rusticucci, and certainly my fierce wife harms me more than anything else."

If I had been covered by the fire, I would have thrown myself among them, and I believe the doctor would have suffered it;

but because I would have burned and cooked myself, fear overcame my good desire that made me greedy to embrace them.

Then I began: "Not disdain, but grief, your condition has fixed within me, so much so that it is late to be completely shed,

as soon as this my lord spoke words to me that made me think that such people as you are, came.

I am from your land, and I have always fondly remembered and listened to your work and your honored names.

I leave the dolorous and go for the sweet apples promised to me by the true leader; but I must first return to the center."

"If your soul long guides your limbs," he replied, "and if your fame shines after you,

courtesy and valor, say if it remains in our city as it is wont, or if it has entirely departed;

for Guglielmo Borsiere, who grieves with us for a little while and goes there with his companions, greatly grieves us with his words."

"The new people and the sudden gains have generated pride and excess in you, Florence, so that you already weep for it."

So I cried with my face raised; and the three, who took this for an answer, looked at each other as one looks at the truth.

"If at other times it costs you so little," they all replied, "to please others, happy are you if you speak thus at your own pleasure!

Therefore, if you escape from these dark places and return to see the beautiful stars, when it will do you good to say 'I was,'

make sure you speak of us to the people." Then they broke the wheel, and their nimble legs seemed to flee like wings.

An amen could not have been said so quickly as they had disappeared; so the master thought he should leave.

I followed him, and we had gone but a little while before the sound of the water was so close that we could hardly have heard each other.

Just as that river that first flows eastward from Monte Viso, from the left slope of the Apennines,

called Acquacheta above, before it descends into its shallow bed, and at Forlì is empty of that name,

reverberates there above San Benedetto de l'Alpe, falling into a ravine where it should have been a refuge for a thousand;

so, down a steep bank, we found that tinted water resounding so that in a few hours it would have offended the ear.

I had a rope tied around me, and with it I sometimes thought of seizing the leopard with the painted skin.

After I had completely untied it, as the leader had commanded me, I handed it to him, coiled and tied.

Whereupon he turned to the right side, and, some distance from the bank, threw her down into that deep ravine.

'It must be,' I said to myself, 'that something new should respond to the new signal that the Master so follows with his eye.'

Ah, how cautious men must be when approaching those who do not merely see the work, but gaze with their understanding into their thoughts!

He said to me: 'Soon will come from above that which I await and which your thoughts dream; soon it must be revealed to your face.'

A man must always close his lips as far as he can against that truth that has the face of a lie, because without guilt it brings shame;

but here I cannot keep silent; And by the notes of this comedy, reader, I swear to you, if they are not empty of long-lasting grace,

that through that thick, dark air I saw a figure coming, noting, upward, marvelous to every sure heart,

just as one returns who sometimes goes down to loosen the anchor that catches hold of a rock or something else that is locked in the sea,

that stretches upward and contracts at the foot.

Inferno · Canto XVII

"Behold the beast with the sharp tail, which passes over mountains and breaks walls and weapons! Behold the one who stinks up the whole world!"

So my leader began to speak to me, and motioned for her to come to shore, near the edge of the marble walkways.

And that filthy image of deceit came, and reached the head and torso, but did not draw its tail to the bank.

His face was that of a just man, so benign was his skin on the outside, and all the rest of his trunk was that of a serpent;

he had two hairy paws down to his armpits; his back, his chest, and both sides were painted with knots and bucklers.

With more colors, subdued and overlapping, never did Tartars or Turks make cloths, nor were such cloths imposed on Arachne.

As sometimes the boats stand on the shore, some of which are in the water and some on land, and as there among the greedy Germans

the beaver settles down to wage war, so the foul beast stood on the edge that is of stone and encloses the sand.

In the void its entire tail wriggled, twisting upward the venomous fork that armed its tip like a scorpion.

The leader said: "Now we must turn our path a little toward that wicked beast that lies there."

So we descended to the right breast, and took ten steps on the edge, to get away from the sand and the flame.

And when we reached it, a little further on I saw people sitting on the sand near the empty place.

There the Master said to me, "So that you may gain full experience of this circle, go and see their course.

Let your conversation be brief there; while you return, I will speak with this one, so that she may grant us her strong shoulders."

So again, all alone, I went up to the outermost head of that seventh circle, where the sad people sat.

Out of their eyes, grief was bursting forth; here and there they helped with their hands, sometimes the vapors, sometimes the hot ground.

Dogs do the same in summer, now with their muzzles, now with their feet, when they are bitten by fleas, flies, or horseflies.

When I looked into the faces of certain eyes, into which the painful fire falls, I recognized none; but I noticed

that from the neck of each hung a pouch that had a certain color and a certain mark, and from there it seemed as if their eyes were feeding.

And as I looked among them, I saw in a yellow pouch a blue one that had the face and demeanor of a lion.

Then, as my gaze continued along the curro, I saw another one as red as blood, revealing a goose whiter than butter.

And one, whose white pouch was marked by the mark of a fat blue sow, said to me: "What are you doing in this pit?

Now go away; And since you are still alive, know that my neighbor Vitaliano will sit here on my left side.

With these Florentines I am from Padua: often they deafen my ears, shouting: 'Let the sovereign knight come,

who will bring the pouch with three goats!'" Here he distorted his mouth and stuck out his tongue, like an ox licking its nose.

And I, fearing lest any longer lingering anger him who had warned me to linger a little longer, turned back from the weary souls.

I found my leader, who had already mounted the fierce animal's back, and said to me: "Now be strong and bold.

Now we descend such stairs; go first, for I want to be in the middle, so that the tail cannot do any harm."

Like one who has the fear of quartan fever so close that his nails are already pale and tremble all over even looking at the shade,

such I became at the words uttered; but his threats made me ashamed, which make a strong servant before a good lord.

I sat on those great shoulders; I wanted to say, but the voice did not come as I thought: "See, you embrace me."

But he, who had once remembered something else, as soon as I mounted, wrapped his arms around me and supported me;

and said: "Gerion, move now: the wheels are wide, and the descent is short; think of the new burden you have."

As the little ship moves backward from its place, so he moved away from there; And then, when he felt himself completely at ease,

where his chest was, he turned his tail, and, outstretched, moved it like an eel, and with his claws gathered the air to himself.

I do not believe there was greater fear when Phaeton abandoned the reins, whereupon the sky, as it still seems, was scorched;

nor when wretched Icarus felt his loins being plucked by the heated wax, his father crying to him, "You are on an evil path!"

than mine was, when I saw that I was in the air on every side, and I saw every sight extinguished except that of the beast.

She goes slowly, slowly, rolling and descending, but I do not notice it except that it blows in my face and from beneath.

I already heard the whirlpool making a horrible roar beneath us on the right hand, causing me to lean my head downward with my eyes.

Then I was more timid at the sound, because I saw fires and heard cries; whereupon I cowered all over, trembling.

And then I saw, for I could not see it in front, the descending and circling of the great evils that were approaching from various sides.

Like the falcon that has been on its wings for a long time, which, without seeing either bird or feather, makes the falconer say, "Alas, you are falling!"

descends wearily from where it moves swiftly, through a hundred circles, and stands far from its master, disdainful and wicked;

So Geryon placed us at the bottom, at the foot of the towering rock, and, having unloaded our persons,

he vanished as if from a rope.

Inferno · Canto XVIII

A place in hell is called Malebolge, all made of iron-colored stone, like the circle that surrounds it.

In the straight middle of the evil field there is a very large and deep well, the location of which I will describe.

The belt that remains is therefore round between the well and the foot of the high hard bank, and has divided the bottom into ten valleys.

Which, where the castles are surrounded by more and more ditches to guard the walls, the part where they are stands out,

they created such an image there; and as in such fortresses there are little bridges from their thresholds to the outer bank,

so from the bottom of the rock rocks moved which cut back the banks and ditches up to the well which cuts them off and collects them.

In this place, shaken by Gerïon's back, we found ourselves; and the poet kept to the left, and I moved behind.

On the right hand I saw new pity, new torment and new whippersnappers, with whom the first bedlam was complete.

In the background the sinners were naked; from the middle here they come towards our face, from there with us, but with greater steps,

as the Romans for the very army, in the year of the jubilee, over the bridge they have to pass the cultured people,

that on one side they all face the castle and go to Santo Pietro, on the other side they go towards the mountain.

From here, from there, up the gloomy rock I saw horned demons with great whips, cruelly beating them from behind.

Alas, how did they raise their anger at the first blows! no one was already waiting for the second ones or the third ones.

While I was going, my eyes were met in one; and I immediately said: "I'm not tired of seeing this man."

So I imagine my feet fixed; and the sweet leader remained with me, and I consented that I should go a little further behind.

And that whipped man believed himself to be hidden by lowering his face; but it was of little use to him, that I said: "O you who cast the eye to the ground,

if the factions you carry are not false, Venedico is you Caccianemico. But what brings you to such pungent sauces?

And he to me: «I don't want to say it; but force me to use your clear speech, which reminds me of the ancient world.

I was the one whom Ghisolabella led to fulfill the Marquis's desire, as if the dirty story were to be heard.

And not even I cry Bolognese here; Indeed, this place is so full of them that many languages are not yet learned

to say 'sipa' between Savena and Reno; and if you want faith or testimony of this, bring to mind our stingy breast."

Thus speaking, he struck a demon with his scourge, and said: «Away, ruffian! here they are not minting females."

I reached myself with my escort; then with a few steps we reached a rock on the bank.

We went up very lightly; and turning to the right up its sliver, we departed from those eternal circles.

When we were there where he was wandering below to give way to the lashed ones, the leader said: "Be careful, and let him fight.

the sight in you of these other ill-born ones, whose faces you have not yet seen because they have gone together with us."

From the old bridge we watched the trail that came toward us from the other side, which the whip similarly drives away.

And the good master, without my asking, said to me: "Look at that great one who comes, and in grief he seems not to shed tears:

How royal he still retains! He is Jason, who by heart and wisdom deprived the Colchians of the ram.

He passed through the island of Lemnos after the bold, merciless women had put all their males to death.

There with signs and ornate words he deceived Hypsipyle, the maiden who had previously deceived all the others.

He leaves her there, pregnant, alone; such a crime condemns him to such torment; and even Medea is being avenged.

With him goes whoever deceives in such a way; and let this be enough to know of the first valley and of those who bite into it."

We were already there where the narrow path intersects with the second bank, and makes it abutment to another arch.

Then we heard people crouching in the other pit, snorting with their muzzles and beating themselves with their palms.

The banks were covered with mold, from the breath from below that clings there, which spars with their eyes and noses.

The bottom is so dark that there is not enough room for us to see without climbing to the ridge of the arch, where the cliff towers highest.

There we came; and then down in the ditch I saw people immersed in dung that seemed to have been stirred by human waste.

And while I was searching down there with my eyes, I saw someone with a head so filthy with shit that it didn't seem like he was a layman or a clergyman.

He scolded me: "Why are you so eager to look at me more than at the other ugly ones?" And I to him: "Because, if I remember correctly,

I've already seen you with dry hair, and you're Alessio Interminei from Lucca: therefore I eye you more than all the others."

And he then, beating his head: "Down here, I've been overwhelmed by the flattery that never tired my tongue."

After this, the guide said to me, "Make sure you push your face a little further forward, so that your eyes can clearly see the face

of that filthy, disheveled servant girl who scratches herself there with her filthy nails, now crouching, now standing.

It is Thais, the whore who answered her lover when he said, 'Have I great thanks from you?': 'Indeed, marvelous ones!'

And from there let our sights be satiated."

Inferno · Canto XIX

O Simon Magus, O wretched followers who, while the things of God, which should be the brides of goodness, you rapacious men

pervert for gold and silver, now the trumpet must sound for you, since you are in the third ditch.

We had already, at the next tomb, climbed the cliff to that part that drops precisely over the middle of the ditch.

O supreme wisdom, how much art you display in heaven, on earth, and in the evil world, and how justly your virtue is distributed!

I saw the livid stone full of holes along the sides and bottom, all of the same width, and each was round.

They did not seem to me less wide or larger than those in my beautiful St. John, made for the place of the baptizers;

One of which, not many years ago, I broke for one who was drowning inside: and let this be a seal that all men may deceive.

Out of the mouth of each one the feet and legs of a sinner were surpassing the bulk, while the other was inside.

The soles of all were both on fire, so that the joints flickered so violently that, when broken, they were twisted and strange.

As the flame of greasy things is wont to move only along the outermost skin, so it was there from the heels to the toes.

"Master, who is he who writhes more than his other companions," I said, "and whom the redder flame sucks?"

And he to me: "If you want me to carry you down there along that bank that lies lowest, you will learn from him about himself and his wrongs."

And I: "As much as it pleases you is beautiful to me: you are lord, and you know that I do not depart from your will, and you know what is being kept silent."

Then we came to the fourth bank; we turned and descended with a weary hand down there into the perforated and shaky depth.

The good Master did not yet release me from his hip, so he reached the breach of him who was weeping with his leg.

"O whoever you are who holds the height below, sad soul stuck like a stake," I began to say, "if you can, speak."

I stood like the friar who confesses the perfidious assassin, who, once he is dead, recalls him so that death may cease.

And he cried: "Are you already standing there, are you already standing there, Boniface? The writing lied to me by several years.

Are you so soon satiated with that possession that you did not fear to deceive the beautiful lady, and then to torture her?"

I became like those who stand, not understanding what is answered them, almost scorned, and do not know how to answer.

Then Virgil said: "Tell him quickly: 'I am not he, I am not he you believe'"; and I answered as I was commanded.

At this the spirit all writhed its feet; then, sighing and with a tearful voice, it said to me: "Then what do you ask of me?

If you care so much to know who I am that you have run up the bank, know that I was clothed in the great cloak;

and truly I was the bear's son, so eager to outdo the bear cubs that I put it here and there in my purse.

Beneath my head are the others who preceded me, simony-playing, flattened through the cracks in the stone.

Down there, too, will I fall when he comes whom I thought you were, when I asked the sudden question.

But the time has already passed since my feet were worn and I have been so upside down that he will not stand firm with red feet.

For after him will come, from the west, a lawless shepherd of fouler deeds, one who must cover both him and me.

There will be a new Jason, of whom we read in the Maccabees; and as his king was soft to him, so will he be who rules France."

I do not know if I was too foolish here, for I answered him in this meter: "Now tell me, alas: how much treasure did Our Lord demand from Saint Peter, first that he should place the keys in his power? Certainly he asked nothing more than 'Come back to me.'

Neither Peter nor the others took gold or silver from Matthias, when he was drawn to the place where his wicked soul perished.

Therefore, stay, for you are well punished; and guard carefully the ill-gotten coin that made you fight against the bold Charles.

And if it were not that the reverence for the supreme keys you held in the joyful life still forbids me,

I would use even more serious words; for your greed saddens the world, trampling on the good and raising up the wicked.

The Evangelist became aware of you shepherds when he saw her who sits upon the waters whoring with kings;

she who was born with seven heads, and from ten horns was given power, until virtue pleased her husband.

You have made yourselves gods of gold and silver; and what difference do you have to the idolaters, except that he is one, and you worship a hundred?

Alas, Constantine, how much evil was the mother, not of your conversion, but of that dowry that your first rich father took from you!

And while I sang to him these notes, whether anger or conscience was biting him, he pushed hard with both feet.

I believe it pleased my leader, for with such contented lips he always awaited the sound of the true words expressed.

Therefore he took me in both arms; and after he had me entirely up to his chest, he remounted the path from which he had descended.

He did not tire of having me close to him, so he carried me to the summit of the arch that spans the fourth to the fifth bank.

There he gently unloaded his burden, gentle because of the rugged and steep rock that would be a difficult passage for goats.

Then another valley was revealed to me.

Inferno · Canto XX

Of a new pain I must make verses and provide material for the twentieth canto of the first song, which is about the drowned.

I was already fully prepared to gaze into the exposed depths, which were bathed in anguished weeping;

and I saw people coming through the circular valley, silent and weeping, at the pace that the Letanian women take in this world.

As my gaze descended lower among them, each one appeared to be miraculously swept away between the chin and the beginning of the chest,

for their faces had turned from their backs, and they had to go backward, because forward vision was taken from them.

Perhaps by force of speech someone had already been completely swept away in this way; but I did not see it, nor do I believe it is.

If God allow you, reader, to reap the fruit of your lesson, now consider for yourself how I could keep my face dry,

when I saw our image so twisted nearby that the tears from my eyes wet the crack of my buttocks.

Truly I wept, leaning against one of the rocks of the hard crag, so that my escort said to me: "Are you also one of the other fools?

Here pity lives when it is truly dead; who is more wicked than he who yields to divine judgment?

Lift up your head, lift up, and see for whom the earth opened to the eyes of the Thebans; for they all cried out: "Where are you falling,

Amphiaraus? Why do you abandon the war?" And they did not stop from rushing down the valley to Minos, who seizes everyone.

Look at what he has made of his shoulders; Because he wanted to see too far ahead, he looks behind and takes a backward path.

See Tiresias, who changed his appearance when he became a female from a male, his entire limbs changing;

and first, then, the two coiled serpents had to beat him back with the rod, so that he could regain his masculine feathers.

Aronta is the one who leans against his belly, who in the mountains of Luni, where the Carrarese who dwells below hoes,

had a cave among the white marbles for his home; so that his vision was not cut off from gazing at the stars and the sea.

And she who covers the breasts, which you do not see, with her loose tresses, and has every hairy skin there,

was Manto, who searched through many lands; then she settled where I was born; So I'm pleased you'll listen to me a little.

After her father departed from life and the city of Baco became a slave, this city has long been wandering the world.

Up in beautiful Italy lies a lake, at the foot of the Alps that enclose Germany above Tiralli, which is called Benaco.

From a thousand springs, I believe, and more between Garda and Val Camonica and Pennino it is bathed by the water that stagnates in the said lake.

It is a place in the middle where the shepherd from Trento, the one from Brescia, and the one from Verona could mark, if he took that path.

Peschiera sits, a beautiful and strong fortress to face the people of Brescia and Bergamo, where the shore slopes furthest around.

There must fall everything that cannot stay in the lap of Benaco and become a river down through green pastures.

As soon as the water begins to flow, it is no longer called Benaco, but Mencio, all the way to Governolo, where it flows into the Po.

It has not run far when it finds a shallow river, which extends and makes it marshy; and in summer it is sometimes miserable.

Then, passing by, the cruel virgin saw land, in the middle of the marsh, uncultivated and bare of inhabitants.

There, to escape all human company, she stayed with her servants to practice her crafts, and lived, and left her empty body there.

Then the men who were scattered around gathered at that place, which was fortified by the marsh it had on all sides.

They built the city on those dead bones; and for her who first chose the place, they called it Mantua without any other name.

Already its people were more densely packed within, before the madness of Casalodi and Pinamonte received deception.

Therefore I warn you that, if you ever hear my city originated otherwise, let no lie be defrauded of the truth."

And I: "Master, your arguments are so certain to me and so reliably hold my trust, that the others would be like dead coals to me.

But tell me, among the people who proceed, if you see any worthy of note; for only to that does my mind return."

Then he said to me: "He who from his cheek thrusts his beard over his brown shoulders was—when Greece was empty of men,

so that barely any remained in the cradles—an augur, and with Calchas in Aulis gave the moment to cut the first rope.

He was called Eurypylus, and so my lofty tragedy sings it somewhere: you know it well, for you know it all.

That other one, whose flanks are so small, was Michele Scotto, who truly knew the game of magical tricks.

See Guido Bonatti; see Asdente, who now wishes to have understood the leather and the string, but too late regrets it.

See the sad women who abandoned the needle, the shuttle, and the spindle, and became divine; they cast spells with herbs and with images.

But come now, for it already holds the boundary of both hemispheres and touches the wave beneath Sobilia, Cain and the thorns;

and already last night the moon was round: you must remember well, for it never harmed you in the deep forest."

So he spoke to me, and we went together.

Inferno · Canto XXI

Thus from bridge to bridge, speaking nothing else than my comedy cares to sing, we went; and we were reaching the summit, when

we stopped to see the other fissure of Malebolge and the other vain laments; and I saw it marvelously dark.

As in the Venetians' arsenal, the tenacious pitch boils in winter to re-bond their unhealthy vessels,

since they cannot sail—in its stead, one makes his own new vessel and another repairs the ribs of what has made many voyages;

one re-rigs from the prow and another from the stern; another makes oars and another turns rigging; another refloats the rigging and the jib—

such, not by fire but by divine art, a thick pitch was boiling down there, which made the bank slippery on every side.

I saw her, but I never saw in her anything but the bubbles that the boiling raised, swelling all over, and sitting compressed.

While I was gazing down there, my leader, saying, "Look, look!", drew me toward him from the place where I was standing.

Then I turned like a man who is slow to see what he must flee from and who is suddenly struck by fear,

who, just to see, does not delay his departure: and I saw a black devil coming behind us, running up the cliff.

Ah, how fierce he was in his aspect! and how fierce he seemed to me in his demeanor, with outstretched wings and light on his feet!

His shoulder, which was sharp and proud, was burdened with both hips by a sinner, and he had seized the sinew of his feet.

From our bridge he said: "O Malebranche, behold one of the elders of Santa Zita! Put him down, for I'm returning by hip

to that land, which is well supplied with them: every man there is a barrator, except Bonturo; with the no, for money, one goes there."

He threw him down there, and turned over the hard rock; and never was a mastiff released with such haste to pursue the thief.

He dove, and came back up reeling; but the demons who had covered the bridge cried out: "The Holy Face has no place here!

One swims here differently than in the Serchio! So, if you don't want us to scratch you, don't overdo it on the pitch."

Then, biting him with more than a hundred hooks, they said: "You must dance here covered, so that, if you can, you can stealthily grab hold of us."

Just as the cooks make their vassals dip the meat in the middle of the cauldron with hooks, so that it doesn't roam.

The good master said to me: "So that it doesn't seem like you're there, crouch down behind a ledge, so that it has some shield for you;

and don't be afraid of any offense that may be done to me, for I know all things, because I've been in a similar fight before."

Then he passed beyond the top of the bridge; and when he reached the sixth bank, he needed to have a firm front.

With the fury and tempest that dogs unleash on a poor man who suddenly asks where he's stopping,

they emerged from under the little bridge and turned all their hooks against him; but he shouted: "Let none of you be cruel!

Before your hooks catch me, let one of you step forward and hear me, and then take counsel about hooking me."

They all shouted: "Go, Malacoda!"; whereupon one moved—and the others stood still—and came to him, saying: "What brings him?"

"Do you think, Malacoda, you see me come here," said my master, "safe from all your shields,

without divine will and opportune fate? Let me go, for in heaven it is willed that I show others this wild path."

Then his pride fell so low that he let the hook fall at his feet, and said to the others, "Now let him not be wounded."

And my leader to me, "O you who sit crouching among the splinters of the bridge, now return to me in safety."

So I moved and came quickly to him; and all the devils came forward, so that I feared he was keeping his pact;

so I saw the infantrymen who were leaving Caprona under pact fear, seeing themselves among so many enemies.

I approached my leader with my whole body, and did not turn my eyes from their appearance, which was not good.

They lowered their gaffs and said to one another, "Do you want me to touch him on the rump?" And they answered, "Yes, see that I touch him."

But the demon who was holding conversation with my leader turned quickly and said, "Stop, stop, Scarmiglione!"

Then he said to us, "It is impossible to go further along this rock, because the sixth arch lies completely broken at the bottom.

And if it pleases you to go forward, go up through this cave; nearby is another rock that makes a way.

Yesterday, more than five hours later than this eighth, one thousand two hundred and sixty-six years completed since the road was broken here.

I'm sending some of my men over there to see if any of them are showing themselves; go with them, for they won't be guilty.

"Go ahead, Alichino and Calcabrina," he began to say, "and you, Cagnazzo; and Barbariccia lead the ten.

Let Libicocco come further on, and Draghignazzo, bloody Ciriatto, and Graffiacane, and Farfarello, and mad Rubicante.

Seek around for the boiling bread; may these be safe as far as the other rock that entirely extends above the lairs."

"Ah, master, what is this I see?" I said. "Ah, let us go alone without an escort, if you know how to go; for I ask none of it.

If you are as alert as you are, do you not see that they are gnashing their teeth and threatening us with grief with their brows?

And he to me: "I do not want you to be afraid; let them gnash to their heart's content, for they do this for the sake of their suffering souls."

They turned along the left bank; but first each had clenched his tongue between his teeth, toward their leader, as a sign;

and he had made a trumpet out of his ass.

Inferno · Canto XXII

I have already seen knights move camp, and begin a battle, and make their display, and sometimes set out for their own escape;

I have seen runners through your land, O Aretines, and I have seen gualdane go, strike tournaments, and jousts run;

sometimes with trumpets, sometimes with bells, with drums, and with signals from the castle, and with local and foreign things;

nor have I ever seen knights move with such different tunes, nor foot soldiers, nor ships, under the sign of land or star.

We were traveling with the ten demons. Ah, fierce company! But in the church with the saints, and in the tavern with the gluttons.

My attention was only on the pitch, to see every aspect of the pit and of the people who were burning within.

Like dolphins, when they signal to sailors with the arch of their backs that they are prepared to save their ship,

sometimes, to alleviate the pain, one of the sinners showed his back and hid it in less time than a flash of lightning.

And as frogs stand at the edge of a ditch with their snouts out, so that they hide their feet and other fat,

so stood the sinners on every side; but as Barbariccia approached, so they retreated beneath the boiling water.

I saw, and it terrifies my heart, one waiting like this, as it happens that one frog remains and the other escapes;

and Graffiacan, who was closest to him, grabbed his matted locks and pulled him up, so that he looked like an otter to me.

I already knew the names of all of them, so I noted them when they were chosen, and after they were called, I listened how.

"O Rubicante, make sure you get your claws on him, so that you flay him!" cried all the accursed ones together.

And I: "My Master, make sure, if you can, that you know who is the wretch who has fallen into the hands of his adversaries."

My leader approached him beside him and asked him where he was from, and he replied: "I was born in the kingdom of Navarre.

My mother placed me as the servant of a lord, who had borne me to a scoundrel, a destroyer of himself and his things.

Then I was in the household of good King Tebaldo; there I began to practice barratry, for which I am answering in this heat."

And Ciriatto, whose mouth had a tusk sticking out from every side like a pig's, made him feel how one was being torn.

The mouse had come among the evil cats; but Barbariccia closed it in with her arms and said: "Stand aside, while I fork him."

And he turned his face to my master. "Ask," he said, "if you want to learn more from him, before someone else undoes him."

The leader then: "Now tell me: among the other villains, do you know any who are Latin under the pitch?" And he: "I left,

a short while ago, from one who was nearby. Would that I were still covered with him, for I would fear neither claw nor hook!"

And Libicocco said: "We have suffered too much," and seized his arm with his grappling hook, so that, tearing, he bore a fragment.

Draghignazzo also tried to grab them by the legs; whereupon their decurion turned around with an ill-tempered attitude.

When they had somewhat reconciled themselves, my leader, who was still gazing at his wound, asked him without hesitation:

"Who was he whose bad luck, you say, you took to get to shore?" And he replied: "It was Friar Gomita,

the one from Gallura, a vessel of every deception, who had his lord's enemies in his hands, and did so much to them that everyone praises him for it.

He took money and left them on the plain, as he says; and in other offices he was also a barrater, not a small one, but a sovereign one.

He associates with Don Michel Zanche of Logodoro; and their tongues never tire of speaking of Sardinia.

Oh, look at the other one gnashing his teeth; I would say so too, but I fear he is preparing to scratch my itch."

And the great commander, turning to Farfarello, who was rolling his eyes to strike, said: "Come over there, you wicked bird!"

"If you want to see or hear," the frightened man began again, "Tuscans or Lombards, I will make some of us come;

but let the Malebranche remain a little quiet, so that they do not fear their vengeance; and I, sitting in this very place,

for one that I am, will make seven of us come when I whistle, as is our custom when someone comes out."

At this word, Cagnazzo raised his muzzle, shaking his head, and said: "Hear the mischief he has devised to throw himself down!"

Whereupon he, who had snares in abundance, replied: "I am too malicious when I bring about my greatest sadness."

Alichin did not hold back and, in opposition to the others, said to him: "If you dive, I will not gallop after you,

but I will beat my wings on the pitch. Let go of your neck, and let the bank be a shield, to see if you alone are worth more than us."

O you who read, you will hear a new game: each turned his eyes to the other side, the first one, who was more reluctant to do so.

The Navarrese took his time well; he planted his feet on the ground, and in a moment leaped and freed himself from their purpose.

At this each was remorseful for his guilt, but he who was the cause of the defect most; therefore he moved and cried: "You have arrived!"

But it was of little avail, for the wings could not advance against the fear; the one went under, and the other, flying, raised his chest high.

Just as the duck suddenly dives when the falcon approaches, and he returns up, angry and broken.

Calcabrina, enraged by the joke, followed him flying, eager that he would survive by having the fight;

and when the barrater disappeared, he turned his talons on his companion and was caught with him above the ditch.

But the other sparrowhawk was a good hawk in clawing at him, and both fell into the middle of the boiling pond.

The hot snatcher was quick; but there was no way to rise, so entangled were his wings.

Barbariccia, grieving with the rest of his men, sent four of them flying from the other side with all their gaffs, and very quickly

they descended to the post, this way and that; they aimed their hooks at the encrusted men, who were already baked inside by the crust.

And we left them thus encumbered.

Inferno · Canto XXIII

Silent, alone, without company, we went, one ahead and the other behind, as Minor Friars go along the road.

My thoughts were turned to Aesop's fable because of the present brawl, where he spoke of the frog and the mouse;

for "now" and "now" are no more alike than the one with the other, if one carefully matches the beginning and the end with a fixed mind.

And as one thought bursts from another, so another was born from that, which doubled my initial fear.

I thought thus: "These are mocked by us with such harm and mockery that I believe it does them much harm.

If anger is combined with ill will, they will come after us more cruelly than a dog pursues the burden he seizes."

I already felt my hair stand on end with fear and stood intently behind, when I said: "Master, if you do not hide

you and me quickly, I fear the Malebranche. We already have them behind us; I imagine them so that I already feel them."

And he: "If I were made of leaded glass, I would not draw your external image to me sooner than I imprint the one within.

Just now your thoughts came among mine, with a similar attitude and a similar face, so that I formed a single counsel between us.

If it is that the right slope is so low that we can descend into the other ditch, we will flee the imagined chase."

He had not yet finished explaining this counsel, when I saw them coming with outstretched wings not far away, wanting to catch us.

My Leader seized me suddenly, like a mother who wakes at the sound and sees the flames burning near her,

who takes her son and flees and does not stop, caring more for him than for herself, so much so that she wears only a single shirt;

and down from the neck of the hard bank he fell supine to the sloping rock that blocks one side of the other pit.

Never did water run so quickly through a gutter to turn the wheel of a mill on the ground, when it approaches closest to the paddles,

as my Master did across that ledge, carrying me on his breast, as his son, not as a companion.

Hardly had his feet reached the bed of the bottom when they were on the hill above us; But there was no suspicion there:

since the high Providence that chose to place them as ministers of the fifth grave took away from them all the power to depart from there.

Down there we found a painted people walking around with very slow steps, weeping and looking tired and defeated.

They wore cloaks with hoods lowered before their eyes, made of the same cloth that is made for monks in Cluj.

On the outside they are gilded, so dazzling; but inside they are all lead, and so heavy that Federigo covered them with straw.

Oh eternally wearisome cloak! We still turned to the left with them, intent on the sad weeping;

but because of their weight, those weary people came so slowly that we were new in company with every movement of our hips.

Wherefore I to my leader: "See that you find someone who is known by deed or name, and, as you go, move your eyes around."

And someone who heard the Tuscan word shouted behind us: "Hold your feet, you who run so fast through the dark air!

Perhaps you will get from me what you ask." At which the leader turned and said: "Wait, and then proceed at his pace."

I stopped, and saw two men show great haste, with their faces, to be with me; but their burden and the narrow path delayed them.

When they arrived, they looked at me askance for a long time without saying a word; then they turned and said to each other:

"This one seems alive by the movement of his throat; and if they are dead, by what privilege are they uncovered from the heavy stole?"

Then they said to me: "O Tuscan, who have come to the college of sad hypocrites, do not scorn to say who you are."

And I to them: "I was born and raised beside the beautiful Arno River in the great village, and I am with the body I have always had.

But who are you, in whom distills as much pain as I see down your cheeks? And what pain is in you that sparkles so?"

And one answered me: "The orange capes are made of lead so thick that the weights make their scales creak so.

We were joyful friars, and Bolognese; I Catalano and these Loderingo called, and taken together from your city

as a solitary man is usually taken, to preserve his peace; and we were such, that it still appears around Gardingo."

I began: "O brothers, your woes . . ." But I said no more, for my eye caught sight of one crucified on the ground with three stakes.

When he saw me, he distorted himself completely, blowing his beard with sighs; and the Catalan friar, who noticed this,

said to me: "That impaled man you see advised the Pharisees that it was best to subject a man to martyrdom for the people.

He is crossed, naked, in the street, as you see, and it is necessary that he feel the burden of whoever passes first.

And so his father-in-law toils in this ditch, and the others from the council that was a bad seed for the Jews."

Then I saw Virgil marvel at him who was stretched out on the cross so vilely in eternal exile.

Then he addressed the friar with this voice: "Do not be displeased, if you may, to tell us if on the right hand there lies a passage

through which we can both escape, without forcing the black angels to come and separate us from this depth."

Then he replied: "A rock is nearer than you expect, which moves from the great circle and crosses all the wild valleys,

except that in this one it is broken and does not cover it. You will be able to climb over the ruin that lies on the hillside and overhangs the bottom."

The leader stood a moment with his head bowed; then he said: "He who hooks the sinners here told us little of the matter."

And the friar: "I have already heard in Bologna that the devil has many vices, among which I heard that he is a liar and the father of lies."

The leader followed with long strides, his face somewhat troubled by anger; so I left the encumbered ones

following the ranks of the dear trees.

Inferno · Canto XXIV

In that part of the young year when the sun tempers his hair under Aquarius and the nights are already drawing to midday,

when the frost on the ground resembles the image of its white sister, but lasts only a short time to temper its feathers,

the peasant whose possessions are lacking rises and looks and sees the countryside all white; whereupon he beats his hip,

returns home and laments here and there, like a wretch who doesn't know what to do; then he returns and regains hope,

seeing the world have changed face in a short time, he takes his crook and drives the sheep out to pasture.

So the master made me dismayed when I saw his brow so troubled, and so quickly the plaster came to the misfortune;

For, as we reached the ruined bridge, my guide turned to me with that gentle expression I first saw at the foot of the mountain.

He opened his arms, after deliberating some deliberate plan, first carefully surveying the ruin, and grasped me.

And like one who works and estimates, who always seems to be making provision beforehand, so, lifting me up toward the top

of a cliff, he noticed another sliver, saying: "Then grab hold of that one; but try first if it's one that can support you."

It was not a path to be clad in a cloak, for we, he lightly and I pushed, could barely climb from buttock to buttock.

And if it were not that the slope of that precipice was shorter than that of the other, I do not know about him, but I would be well beaten.

But because Malebolge slopes all the way toward the door of the lowest well, the position of each valley dictates

that one slope rises and the other descends; we finally reached the point where the last stone drops away.

The breath had drained from my lungs so much when I was up that I could go no further; rather, I sat down at the first moment of arrival.

"Now you must undress yourself," said the master; "for, sitting on feathers, one gains no fame, nor under a blanket;

without which, he who consumes his life leaves such a trace of himself on earth as smoke in the air and foam in the water.

So rise; conquer your anguish with the spirit that conquers every battle, if it does not collapse with its heavy body.

A longer stairway must be climbed; It is not enough to have left these people. If you understand me, now make it avail you."

Then I rose, showing myself to be more supplied with breath than I felt, and said: "Go, for I am strong and bold."

Up the cliff we took the path, which was rocky, narrow, and difficult, and much steeper than before.

Talking, I went on so as not to appear faint; whereupon a voice came from the other ditch, inappropriate in its form.

I do not know what it said, although I was already on the back of the arch that passes there; but the speaker seemed to be moving to go.

I was turned downward, but my living eyes could not reach the bottom because of the darkness; so I said: "Master, make sure you reach

the other ridge and let us dismount the wall; for, as I hear from here and understand not, so I see below and imagine nothing."

"I give you no other answer," he said, "than to do it; for the honest question must be followed by deeds in silence."

We descended the bridge from the head where it joins the eighth bank, and then the pit was clear to me:

and I saw within it a terrible throng of serpents, and of such a variety that memory still drains my blood.

Let Libya boast no more of its sand; for if it produces chelydri, jacula, and phareas, and cencri with amphibena,

nor has it ever shown so many pestilences nor so many evils with all Ethiopia nor with all that lies above the Red Sea.

Among this cruel and most sad multitude, naked and frightened people ran, without hope of a hole or heliotrope:

they had tied their hands behind them with serpents; They stuck their tails and heads into the reins, and were entwined in front.

And behold, a serpent pounced on one who was on our shore and pierced him where the neck joins the shoulders.

Neither O nor I was ever written so quickly, as it flared up and burned, and as it fell it must have turned to ashes;

and after it was thus destroyed on the ground, the dust gathered itself and returned to the same place at once.

Thus it is confessed by the great sages that the phoenix dies and is then reborn when it approaches its five hundredth year;

it feeds on neither grass nor grain during its life, but only on incense, tears, and amomum, and nard and myrrh are its last swaddling clothes.

And as he who falls, and knows not how, by the force of a demon that drags him to the ground, or by some other oppression that binds man,

when he rises, looking around, completely bewildered by the great anguish he has suffered, and sighing as he gazes:

such was the sinner when he rose afterward. Oh, how severe is the power of God, that rains down such blows in vengeance!

The leader then asked him who he was; to which he replied: "I rained from Tuscany, not long ago, into this wild ravine.

I liked a bestial life, not a human one, like the mule I was; I am Vanni Fucci, a beast, and Pistoia was my worthy lair."

And I to the leader: "Tell him not to move, and ask what sin drove him down here; for I saw him as a man of blood and wrath."

And the sinner, who understood, did not feign guilt, but turned his mind and face toward me, and painted himself with sad shame;

then he said: "It grieves me more that you have caught me in the misery where you see me, than when I was taken from the other life.

I cannot deny what you ask; I am so low because I was a thief in the sacristy of the beautiful furnishings,

and it was falsely placed there by others. But lest you enjoy such a sight, if you ever find yourself outside the dark places,

open your ears to my announcement, and listen. Pistoia first grows thin of the Neri; then Florence renews its people and ways.

Mars draws vapor from the Val di Magra, which is shrouded in turbid clouds; and with a fierce and bitter storm

over Campo Piceno will be fought; whereupon he will suddenly shatter the fog, so that every Bianco will be wounded.

And I have said it so that it may grieve you!

Inferno · Canto XXV

At the end of his words, the thief raised his hands with both fingers, shouting: "Take them away, God, for I will strike them at you!"

From then on, the snakes were my friends, for one then coiled around his neck, as if to say, "I do not want you to say any more!"

and another around his arms, and bound him again, reinforcing itself so tightly that it could not even break with them.

Ah, Pistoia, Pistoia, why do you not decide to burn yourself to ashes so that you no longer endure, since your seed is left over in evil deeds?

Through all the dark circles of Hell, I have not seen a spirit so proud in God, not that which fell from the walls of Thebes.

He fled so quickly that he no longer spoke a word; And I saw a centaur, full of rage, come calling: "Where is he, where is the wild one?"

I do not believe Maremma has as many as he had snakes on his rump, up to where our lips begin.

Across his shoulders, behind the cup, a drake lay with outstretched wings; and it sets fire to anyone who stumbles upon it.

My master said: "This is Cacus, who, beneath the rock of Mount Aventine, often made a pool of blood.

He does not travel with his brothers on the same road, because of the fraudulent theft he committed of the great herd he had nearby;

so as to cease his sinister works under the mace of Hercules, who perhaps gave him a hundred, and he did not feel the ten."

While he was speaking thus, and it passed, three spirits came beneath us, of whom neither I nor my leader was aware,

except when they cried out, "Who are you?"; whereupon our conversation paused, and we only heard from them afterwards.

I did not recognize them; but it happened, as is often the case with some chance, that one had to name another,

saying, "Cianfa, where has he remained?"; whereupon I, to make the leader attentive, placed my finger from my chin to my nose.

If you are now, reader, slow to believe what I am about to say, it will not be surprising, for I, who saw it, can barely consent.

As I held my eyebrows raised, a serpent with six feet darted forward before one of them and clung to him entirely.

It wrapped its middle feet around his belly and grasped his arms with its forefeet; then it bit them on both cheeks;

it stretched its hind legs to his thighs, and placed its tail between them, and stretched it up behind him through his reins.

Never had an ivy clung so tightly to a tree as the horrible beast entwined its own limbs around another.

Then they clung as if they were made of hot wax, and their colors mingled, neither of them seemed what they were:

as from the heat, through the papyrus above, a brown color that is not yet black proceeds, and the white fades.

The other two looked at him, and each cried out: "Alas, Agnel, how you are changing! See that you are now neither two nor one."

The two heads had already become one, when two figures appeared, mixed in one face, where two were lost.

Two arms were made of four strips; the thighs with the legs, the belly, and the chest became limbs never before seen.

Every former aspect there was hollow: two and none seemed the perverse image; and such a soul went with slow pace.

As a lizard under the great lash of the canicular days, changing into silk, seems like lightning if it crosses the path,

so it seemed, coming toward the heights of the other two, a small burning serpent, livid and black as a grain of pepper;

and that part from which our nourishment is first taken, it pierced one of them; then it fell down stretched before him.

The pierced man looked at him, but said nothing; rather, with his feet still, he yawned as if sleep or fever were assailing him.

He looked at the serpent and at it; One from the wound and the other from the mouth smoked strongly, and the smoke collided.

Let Lucan be silent now, where it is his turn to speak of wretched Sabellus and Nasidius, and listen to what is now being spewed.

Let Ovid be silent about Cadmus and Arethusa, for if he turns the former into a serpent and the latter into a fountain in his poetry, I do not envy him;

for never did he change two natures face to face so that both forms were ready to change their material.

Together they responded to such standards that the serpent cleft its tail into a fork, and the wounded man closed his tracks together.

The legs and thighs stuck together so tightly that the joint soon made no visible mark.

The figure that was lost there was taking away its cleft tail, and its skin became soft, and that on the other side hard.

I saw the arms enter through the armpits, and the two feet of the beast, which were short, lengthen as much as they shortened those.

Then the hind feet, twisted together, became the limb that hides the man, and the wretched man had two of his own.

While the smoke veiled both of them with a new color, and generated hair on one side and peeled it off on the other,

one rose and the other fell down, not however turning away the impious lamps, under which each changed faces.

The one who was upright, he pulled toward the temples, and from the excessive matter that came there, the ears emerged from the hollow cheeks;

The one who did not run backward and retained that excess, gave a nose to the face and thickened the lips as was appropriate.

The one who was lying thrusts his muzzle forward, and draws his ears back into his head like a snail's horns;

and the tongue, which had been united and ready to speak before, splits, and the forked one closes in the other; and the smoke remains.

The soul, which had become a wild beast, hissing, flees through the valley, and the other, speaking after him, spits.

Then he turned his new back on him and said to the other: "I want Buoso to run, as I have done, crawling along this path."

Thus I saw the seventh ballast change and transmute; and here excuse me for the novelty if my pen abhors flower.

And although my eyes were somewhat confused and my mind dismayed, they could not flee so closed

that I did not clearly see Puccio Sciancato; and he was the only one, of the three companions who came before, who had not changed;

the other was the one for whom you, Gaville, lament.

Inferno · Canto XXVI

Rejoice, Florence, since you are so great that you beat your wings on land and sea, and your name is spread throughout Hell!

Among the thieves I found five of your citizens, who bring shame to me, and you do not rise to great honor.

But if one dreams of truth near the dawn, you will soon hear of what Prato, like no other, longs for you.

And if it were already, it would not be soon. So it would be, for it must be! For it will weigh more heavily on me as I grow older.

We departed, and up the steps that the first ones had built for us to descend, my leader remounted and led me;

and continuing along the lonely path, among the splinters and crags of the cliff, my foot could not move without a hand.

Then I grieved, and now I grieve again when I direct my mind to what I saw, and I rein in my genius more than I am accustomed,

so that it does not run unless virtue guides it; so that, if a good star or something better has given me happiness, I may not envy it myself.

As the peasant who rests on the hill, at the time when he who illuminates the world keeps his face least hidden from us,

like the fly yields to the mosquito, sees fireflies down the valley, perhaps there where the grape harvest and the plow are carried out:

The eighth pit shone with so many flames, as I perceived as soon as I was there where the bottom appeared.

And as he who avenged himself on the bears saw Elijah's chariot depart, when the horses rose erect to heaven,

that he could not follow it with his eyes so far as to see anything but the flame alone, like a little cloud, rising upward:

so each one moves through the ravine of the moat, for none reveals the theft, and every flame steals a sinner.

I stood on the bridge, so high up to see, that if I had not caught a rock, I would have fallen down without being struck.

And the leader, who saw me so eagerly awaited, said: "The spirits are within the fires; each one swathes himself with that which is burned."

"My Master," I replied, "for hearing you I am more certain; But I had already foreseen that it was so, and already I wanted to say to you:

Who is in that fire that is so divided above, that it seems to rise from the pyre where Eteocles was placed with his brother?

He answered me: "In there Ulysses and Diomedes are tormented, and together they go to vengeance as to wrath;

and within their flame the ambush of the horse that made the gate through which the noble seed of the Romans issued is lamented.

Within it is lamented the art for which, dead, Deidamia still mourns Achilles, and the punishment of the Palladium is borne there."

"If they can speak within those sparks," I said, "Master, I beg you very much, and I beg you again, that the prayer may be worth a thousand,

that you do not deny me the waiting until the horned flame comes here. See that I bend toward it with desire!"

And he to me: "Your prayer is worthy of much praise, and therefore I accept it; but be careful that your tongue be restrained.

Leave me to speak, for I have understood what you want; for they would be shy, because they are Greeks, perhaps of your words."

After the flame had reached the place and time that seemed right to my leader, I heard him speak in this way:

"O you who are two within one fire, if I deserved you while I lived, if I deserved you much or little

when I wrote those lofty verses in the world, do not move; but let one of you say where, through him, lost, he went to die."

The greatest horn of the ancient flame began to quiver, murmuring, like one weary of the wind;

then, waving its tip here and there, as if it were a speaking tongue, it uttered a voice and said: "When

I departed from Circe, who took me away for more than a year near Gaeta, before Aeneas had named her so,

neither the sweetness of a son, nor the pity of an aged father, nor the due love that should have made Penelope happy,

could overcome within me the ardor I had to become experienced in the world, in human vices and in valor;

but I set out on the high open sea, alone with a ship and that little companion from whom I was not deserted.

From one shore to the other I saw as far as Spain, as far as Morocco, and the island of Sardinia, and the others that the sea bathes around.

My companions and I were old and slow when we reached that narrow mouth where Hercules marked his sights

so that man might go no further. On my right hand I left Sibilia, on the other I had already left Setta.

"O brothers," I said, "who through a hundred thousand perils have reached the West, to this so brief vigil

of our senses that remains, do not deny the experience, behind the sun, of the unpeopled world.

Consider your lineage: you were not made to live like brutes, but to pursue virtue and knowledge."

With this brief oration I made my companions so keen on the journey that I could hardly have held them back.

And turning our stern toward the morning, we made wings of our oars for our mad flight, always gaining on the left side.

Night already saw all the stars of the other pole, and ours so low that it did not rise above the sea floor.

Five times the light from beneath the moon had been rekindled and as many times extinguished, since we had entered the high pass,

when a mountain appeared, dark with distance, and it seemed to me as high as any I had ever seen.

We rejoiced, and soon we cried again; for from the new land a whirlwind arose and struck the first corner of the ship.

Three times it made it whirl with all the waters; at the fourth, raise the stern and go down the prow, as pleased another,

until the sea closed over us."

Inferno · Canto XXVII

The flame was already raised high and quiet, so as to say no more, and was already departing from us with the sweet poet's permission,

when another, coming after it, made us turn our eyes to its summit because of a confused sound issuing from it.

Just as the Sicilian ox, which first bellowed with the weeping of him, and that was right, who had tempered it with his file,

bellowed with the voice of the afflicted, so that, though it was made of brass, it still seemed pierced by pain;

so, because it had no path or opening from the beginning in the fire, the wretched words were converted into its own language.

But after they had reached the summit, giving it that flicker that the tongue had given in its passage,

we heard: "O you to whom I direct my voice and who just now spoke Lombard, saying 'Go to Istria, I no longer incite you,'

because I have arrived perhaps somewhat late, do not be sorry to stay and speak to me; see that it does not bother me, and I burn!

If you have just now fallen into this blind world from that sweet Latin land from which I bear all my guilt,

tell me whether the Romagnuoli have peace or war; for I was from the mountains there between Orbino and the yoke from which the Tiber breaks loose."

I was still down there, attentive and bent, when my leader touched me from the side, saying: "You speak; this one is Latin."

And I, who already had my answer ready, began to speak without hesitation: "O soul who are hidden down there,

Your Romagna is not, and never was, without war in the hearts of its tyrants; but I have now left none there in the open.

Ravenna remains as it has been for many years: the eagle of Polenta broods there, so that it covers Cervia with its wings.

The land that once endured the long trial and a bloody heap of Frenchmen is found under green claws.

And the old and the new mastiff from Verrucchio, who made Montagna the bad government, there where they are wont to suck their teeth.

The cities of Lamone and Santerno are led by the lion from the white nest, who changes sides from summer to winter.

And that one whose flank the Wise bathes, as it is between the plain and the mountain, lives between tyranny and freedom.

Now who are you? I beg you to tell us. Do not be more harsh than others have been, if your name may stand firm in the world."

After the fire had roared somewhat in its own way, the sharp point moved from one side to the other, and then uttered this breath:

"If I believed that my answer was to one who would never return to the world, this flame would have remained without further shocks;

but since no one has ever returned alive from this depth, if I hear the truth, without fear of infamy I answer you.

I was a man of arms, and then I was a Cordelier, believing, thus girded, to make amends; And certainly my belief would have been complete,

if it were not for the high priest, whom woe betide!, who remitted me to my first sins; and how and why, I want him to understand.

While I was formed from the bones and flesh my mother gave me, my actions were not those of a lion, but of a fox.

I knew all the devices and the hidden ways, and I practiced their art so that the sound came out to the ends of the earth.

When I saw myself reaching that stage of my life where everyone should lower their sails and gather their rigging,

what had once pleased me now displeased me, and I repented and confessed; alas, wretched man! and it would have been useful.

The prince of the new Pharisees, having war near the Lateran, and not with Saracens or Jews,

since every one of his enemies was Christian, and no one had been to conquer Acre or a merchant in the land of the Sultan,

he looked neither for high office nor holy orders, nor for me that noose that used to make his girdles leaner.

But just as Constantine asked Sylvester from within Syracuse to cure his leprosy, so he asked me for a teacher

to cure his proud fever. He asked me for advice, and I remained silent because his words seemed intoxicated.

And then he said again: "Do not suspect your heart; I absolve you now, and you teach me to do as you cast Penestrino to the ground.

I can lock and unlock heaven, as you know; therefore there are two keys that my predecessor did not cherish."

Then the grave arguments drove me to the place where silence seemed to me the worst, and I said: "Father, since you wash me

of that sin into which I must now fall, a long promise with short waiting will make you triumph on the high throne."

Francis came then, after I was dead, for me; But one of the black cherubim said to him: "Do not carry it; do not wrong me.

He must come down among my wretched ones because he gave the deceitful advice, for which I have been torn to pieces until now;

for one cannot absolve one who does not repent, nor can one repent and will at the same time because of the contradiction that does not allow it."

Oh, how sad I am! How I roused myself when he seized me, saying: "Perhaps you did not think I was a logician!"

He carried me to Minos; and he twisted his tail eight times around his hard back; and after he bit it in great rage,

he said: "This is one of the culprits of the dead fire." Therefore, where you see me, I am lost, and, going thus clad, I am resentful.

When he had thus completed his speech, the flame departed in pain, twisting and flapping its sharp horn.

We passed on, my guide and I, over the cliff to the other arch that covers the ditch where the penalty is paid

to those who by betting acquire burdens.

Inferno · Canto XXVIII

Who could ever, even in simple words, fully describe the blood and wounds I just saw, if I had to recount them many times?

Every tongue would certainly faint at our discourse and at the minds that have so little scope for comprehending it.

If all the people who once, in the fortunate land of Apulia, grieved for their blood, were to gather together

for the Trojans and for the long war that made such noble spoils of the rings, as Livy, who is not mistaken, writes

with the one who felt the pain of blows from opposing Robert Guiscard; and the other whose bones still gather

at Ceperan, there where every Apulian was a liar, and there at Tagliacozzo, where old Alardo conquered without weapons;

and whichever member he showed pierced or severed, the manner of the filthy ninth pit would be nothing to equal.

Now I see, by half-lost or lull, as I saw one, so unperforated, torn from the chin to the point where it gulps.

Between his legs hung his guts; his breastbone seemed to be the sad sack that makes shit from what is swallowed.

While I was absorbed in seeing him, he looked at me and with his hands opened his chest, saying: "Now see how I am tearing myself apart!

See how crippled is Muhammad! Before me goes Ali weeping, his face cleft from chin to forelock.

And all the others you see here, sowers of scandal and schism, are alive outside, and therefore are cleft like this.

There is a devil behind us who tortures us so cruelly, putting each of this lot to the edge of the sword,

when we have turned the painful path; for the wounds are closed before anyone else returns before them.

But who are you who muses on the rock, perhaps to delay going to the punishment that is judged on your accusations?"

"Neither death has reached him yet, nor does guilt lead him," my master replied, "to torment him; but to give him full experience,

I, who am dead, must lead him through hell down here, from circle to circle; and this is true, as I speak to you."

More than a hundred, when they heard it, stopped in the ditch to gaze at me in wonder, forgetting their torment.

"Now tell Brother Dolcin, you who will perhaps soon see the sun, to arm himself if he doesn't want to follow me here soon,

so that a crush of snow doesn't bring victory to the Noarese, which otherwise would be impossible to achieve."

After he had suspended one foot from his feet to leave, Muhammad spoke these words to me; then he laid him down to the ground to depart.

Another, whose throat had been pierced and whose nose was cut off below the eyebrows, and who had always had only one ear,

stood gazing in wonder with the others, and before them opened his reed, which was red on every side,

and said: "O you, whom no guilt condemns, and whom I saw up in Latin land, if too much resemblance does not deceive me,

remember Pier da Medicina, if you ever return to see the sweet plain that slopes from Vercelli to Marcabò.

And let the two best men from Fano, Messer Guido and also Angiolello, know that, if their foresight here is not in vain,

they will be thrown from their vessel and beaten near the Cattolica for the treachery of a cruel tyrant.

Between the islands of Cyprus and Maiolica, Neptune never saw such a great crime, not by pirates, not by Argolic people.

That traitor who sees only with one, and holds the land he would like to see here with me to be empty,

will bring them to parley with him; then he will ensure that in the wind of Focara they will have no need of vows or prayers."

And I to him: "Show me and declare, if you want me to bring news of you, who is the one with the bitter sight."

Then he placed his hand on the jaw of one of his companions and opened his mouth, crying: "This is he, and he does not speak.

This one, driven away, submerged Caesar's doubts, declaring that the prepared man always suffered with loss for waiting."

Oh, how terrified did Curio, who was so bold to speak, seem with his tongue cut out in his throat!

And one who had both hands severed, raising the stumps into the dark air, so that the blood stained his face,

cried: "You will also remember Mosca, who said, alas!, 'He has done something,' which was a bad seed for the Tuscan people."

And I added: "And death to your lineage"; whereupon he, piling grief upon grief, departed like a sad and mad person.

But I remained to gaze at the flock, and I saw something I would be afraid, without further proof, to tell alone;

except that conscience assures me of the good company that frees man under the hauberk of feeling pure.

I saw indeed, and it seems I still see it, a headless bust walking as the others of the sad flock went;

and it held the severed head by its locks, weighing it in its hand like a lantern; and it looked at us and said: "Oh me!"

It made a lamp of itself, and there were two in one and one in two; how it can be, he who governs himself knows.

When he was right at the foot of the bridge, he raised his arm high, his whole head high, to draw nearer to his words,

which were: "Now see the grievous punishment, you who, breathing your last, go gazing upon the dead: see if any is as great as this.

And that you may bring news of me, know that I am Bertram of Bornio, he who gave the young king his misfortunes.

I made the father and the son rebellious within themselves; Ahithophel no longer made Absalom and David with his wicked goads.

Because I separated people so closely joined, I have separated my brain, alas!, from its origin, which is in this stump.

Thus the counterpass is observed in me."

Inferno · Canto XXIX

The multitude of people and the diverse wounds had so intoxicated my eyes that I longed to stand there and weep.

But Virgil said to me: "Why are you still gazing? Why does your gaze only suffocate down there among the sad, broken shades?

You have not done so to the other pits; consider, if you believe in counting them, that the valley extends twenty-two miles.

And already the moon is beneath our feet; the time granted us is now short, and there is more to see than you see."

"If you had," I replied afterwards, "attended to the reason why I was gazing, perhaps you would have also excused me from standing."

My leader was going away, and I was following him, already making his reply, and adding: "In that cave

where I was now keeping my eyes so intently fixed, I believe a spirit of my blood is weeping for the sin that costs so much down there."

Then the master said: "Do not let your thoughts wander from here onward upon him. Attend to something else, and let him remain there;

for I saw him at the foot of the little bridge point to you and threaten you forcefully with his finger, and I heard him named Geri del Bello.

You were then so completely obstructed by him who once held Altaforte that you did not look away, so he had withdrawn."

"O my leader, the violent death that is not yet avenged," I said, "by anyone who is a partner in the shame,

made him disdainful; where he went away without speaking to me, as I judge: and in this he has made me more pious toward himself."

So we spoke until we reached the first place that the other valley shows from the cliff, if there were more light, all the way down.

When we were above the last cloister of Malebolge, so that its lay brothers could appear to our sight,

various laments shot at me, arrows that had been barbed with pity; so I covered my ears with my hands.

What a pain it would be if the sick of the hospitals of Valdichiana between July and September, and of Maremma and Sardinia,

were all in one ditch, such was it here, and such a stench came from it as is usual to come from rotten limbs.

We descended to the last shore of the long cliff, still on the left; and then my vision was more vivid

down toward the bottom, where the minister of the high Lord, infallible justice, punishes the perpetrators she records here.

I do not believe that the people in Aegina were more afflicted by the sight of sadness, when the air was so filled with malice

that all the animals, even the smallest worm, fell, and then the ancient people, as the poets hold firmly,

refreshed themselves with ant seed; for it was to behold in that dark valley the spirits languishing on various shovels.

One lay on each other's stomachs, one on each other's shoulders, and one crawled along the grim path.

Step by step we went without speaking, looking and listening to the sick, who could not lift their bodies.

I saw two sitting leaning against each other, as one leans against a pan to warm oneself, spotted from head to foot with skulls;

and I never saw a witch being used on a boy waited on by his master, nor on one who is unwilling to keep awake,

as each one often bit his nails in the great rage of the itch, which has no further relief;

and the nails tore away the scab, like a knife to the scales of a roach or any other fish that has larger scales.

"O you who unravel yourself with your fingers," my leader began to one of them, "and who sometimes make pincers of them,

tell me if there is any Latin among those who are here, if your nails are eternally sufficient for this work."

"We are Latins, whom you see both so ruined here," one replied, weeping; "but who are you who asked about us?"

And the leader said: "I am one who descends with this living being from ledge to ledge, and I intend to show him Hell."

Then the common support broke; and each one, trembling, turned to me, along with others who heard him in return.

The good Master gathered himself completely to me, saying: "Tell them what you wish." And I began, after he turned:

"If your memory is not stolen from human minds in the first world, but lives under many suns,

tell me who you are and of what people; let not the shameful and irksome pain of revealing yourselves to me frighten you."

"I was from Arezzo, and Albero of Siena," one replied, "had me put to the fire; but that for which I died does not bring me here.

True it is that I said to him, speaking in jest, 'I could rise through the air by flight'; and he, who had little desire and little sense,

wanted me to show him the art; and only because I did not make him Daedalus, he had me burned by one who had him for a son.

But to the lowest pit of the ten, Minos, who is not permitted to fail, condemned me for the alchemy I practiced in the world.

And I said to the poet: "Now were there ever people as vain as the Sienese? Certainly not the French so vain!"

Then the other leper, who heard me, replied to my words: "Take with me Stricca, who knew how to spend wisely,

and Niccolò, who first discovered the rich habit of carnations in the garden where such seed grows;

and take with me the company in which Caccia d'Ascian dispersed his vineyard and his great estate, and Abbagliato poured out his wisdom.
