But so that you may know who supports you against the Sienese, sharpen your eye toward me, so that my face may answer you clearly:

then you will see that I am the shade of Capocchio, who falsified metals with alchemy; and you must remember, if you look carefully,

how I was by nature a good ape.

Inferno · Canto XXX

While Juno was enraged by Semele's anger against the Theban bloodline, as she repeatedly demonstrated,

Athahamas became so mad that, seeing his wife and two sons laden in each hand,

he cried out, "Let's spread the nets so I can catch the lioness and the cubs at the pass." Then he stretched out his merciless claws,

grabbing one, whose name was Learchus, and rolling him around, struck him against a rock; and she drowned herself with the other burden.

And when fortune brought low the Trojans' courage, who dared everything, so that the king and his kingdom were destroyed,

Hecuba, sad, wretched, and wicked, after she saw Polyxena dead, and her Polydorus on the seashore,

the woeful Hecuba, aware of her grief, barked like a mad dog; so much did the pain twist her mind.

But neither Theban nor Trojan furies were ever seen in anyone so cruel, not stinging beasts, not even human limbs,

as I saw in two pale, naked shadows, who ran biting like a pig when it opens its sty.

One reached Capocchio and bit him in the crook of his neck, so that, pulling, it made his belly scrape against the firm bottom.

And the Aretine, who remained, trembling, said to me: "That elf is Gianni Schicchi, and he goes about in a rage treating others like this."

"Oh," I said to him, "if the other doesn't set his teeth on you, don't be hard pressed to say who he is before he escapes from here."

And he to me: "That is the ancient soul of wicked Myrrha, who, outside of rightful love, became her father's friend.

She thus came to sin with him, falsifying herself in another's form, as the other who goes there sustained,

to win the lady of the herd, falsifying in himself Buoso Donati, making a will and giving form to the will."

And after the two madmen had passed, on whom I had fixed my gaze, I turned it to look at the other ill-born.

I saw one, fashioned in the guise of a lute, provided he had his groin severed by the other who has forked the man.

The heavy dropsy, which so disintegrates the limbs with poorly converted humor that the face no longer corresponds to the belly,

made him keep his lips open like the stinging man who, because of thirst, turns one chin toward the other upward.

"O you who are without any pain, and I know not why, in the wretched world," he said to us, "look and attend

to the misery of Master Adam; I had, in my lifetime, enough of what I wanted, and now, alas!, I long for a drop of water.

The streams that flow down from the green Casentine hills to the Arno, making their channels cold and soft,

are always before me, and not in vain, for their image dries me more than the pain that tears my face.

The rigid justice that searches me draws its reason from the place where I sinned to further put my sighs to flight.

There is Romena, where I counterfeited the Baptist's sealed bond; for which I left my body burned above.

But if I could see here the sad soul of Guido or Alessandro or their brother, I would not give up my sight for Fonte Branda.

There's one inside already, if the angry shades wandering around speak truth; but what good is it to me, my limbs tied?

If I were even so light that I could walk an ounce in a hundred years, I would already be on the path,

looking for him among these unsightly people, even though it winds eleven miles, and is not less than a half a mile across.

I am among such a family for them; they persuaded me to strike the florins that had three carats of dirt."

And I to him: "Who are those two wretches who smoke like wet hands in winter, lying close to your right borders?"

"I found them here—and then they did not give—," he replied, "when I rained in this ravine, and I do not believe they give forever.

One is the false one who accused Joseph; the other is the false Greek Sinon of Troy: because of a sharp fever they cast such leptus."

And one of them, who perhaps grew weary of being called so obscure, struck him on the black stomach with his fist.

She sounded like a drum; and Master Adam struck him in the face with his arm, which seemed no less hard,

saying to him: "Although I am deprived of movement by my heavy limbs, I have my arm free for such a task."

To which he replied: "When you went to the fire, you did not have it so ready; but you had it so much more when you were coining."

And the dropsical man: "You speak true of this: but you were not such a true witness when you were asked for the truth in Troy."

"If I spoke falsely, and you falsified the coin," said Sinon; "and I am here for one fault, and you for more than any other demon!"

"Remember, perjurer, the horse," replied he whose stomach was swollen; "and be guilty that the whole world knows it!"

"And be guilty of the thirst that cracks your tongue," said the Greek, "and the putrid water that so closes your belly before your eyes!"

Then the coiner: "Thus your mouth is torn open for your own misfortune, as it is wont; for if I am thirsty and humor fills me,

you are burning and your head aches, and to lick the mirror of Narcissus, you would not want to say many words."

I was completely absorbed in listening to them when the master said to me: "Now look, I'm almost going to fight with you!"

When I heard him speak to me angrily, I turned toward him with such shame that it still swirls in my memory.

As is he who dreams of his own harm, who in dreaming desires to dream, so that he longs for what is, as if it were not,

such I became, unable to speak, who wanted to excuse myself, and excused myself all the time, and did not believe I could do it.

"Less shame washes away a greater fault," said the master, "than yours has ever been; therefore, it frees you from all sadness.

And make sure that I am always at your side, if it ever happens that fortune finds you where there are people in similar plight:

for to want to hear this is a base desire."

Inferno · Canto XXXI

The same tongue first bit me, so that it stained both cheeks, and then restored the medicine;

so I hear that the spear of Achilles and his father was accustomed to be the cause first of bad and then of good.

We turned our backs on the wretched valley along the bank that surrounds it, crossing it without any conversation.

There it was less than night and less than day, so that my vision went little ahead; but I heard a loud horn sound,

so loud that it would have made every thunder hoarse, which, following its path against itself, directed my eyes all to one place.

After the painful defeat, when Charlemagne lost the holy deed, Roland did not sound so terribly.

I turned my head there a short time before I seemed to see many high towers; whereupon I: "Master, tell me, what land is this?"

And he to me: "Because you wander through the darkness too far away, it happens that in your imagination you abhor it.

You will see clearly, if you connect there, how far the sense is deceived; therefore, prick yourself a little more."

Then he took me gently by the hand and said: "Before we go further, so that the matter may seem less strange to you,

know that they are not towers, but giants, and they are in the well around the edge, from the navel down, all of them."

As when the fog dissipates, the gaze gradually figures out what the vapor that crowds the air conceals,

so piercing the thick, dark air, drawing ever closer to the edge, error flees from me and fear grows in me;

For, just as Montereggio is crowned with towers on its circular walls, so the shore that surrounds the well

the horrible giants towered halfway up their bodies, whom Jove from heaven still threatens when he thunders.

And I could already see the face, shoulders, chest, and a large part of the belly of some, and down along the sides both arms.

Nature, indeed, when she abandoned the art of such animals, did well to remove such executioners from Mars.

And if she does not repent of elephants and whales, he who looks subtly holds her more just and more discreet;

for where the reason of the mind is joined to evil will and power, no people can protect it.

His face seemed to me long and thick like the pine tree of St. Peter's in Rome, and the other bones were in proportion to it;

so that the bank, which was a loincloth from the middle down, showed so much of it above that it reached the mane.

Three Frisians had ill-conceived boasting; for I could see thirty great spans of it from the place down where a man buckles his cloak.

"Raphèl never amècche zabì almi," began to shout the fierce mouth, to which sweeter psalms were not fitting.

And my leader turned to him: "Foolish soul, hold on to your horn, and with it vent yourself when anger or other passion touches you!

Search around your neck, and you will find the rope that holds it, O confused soul, and see him who binds your great chest."

Then he said to me: "He accuses himself; this is Nimbrotto, for whose evil brow even language is not used in the world.

Let us leave him alone and not speak in vain; for every language is to him as his is to others, which is known to no one."

We then took a longer journey, turning to the left; and at the shot of one crossbow we found the other much more ferocious and larger.

Whoever was the master who bound him, I cannot say, but he had the other in front and the right arm behind him

bound with a chain that bound him from the neck down, so that it wound around his exposed body up to the fifth circle.

"This proud man wanted to test his power against supreme Jove," said my leader, "whence he has such merit.

His name is Phialtes, and he performed great tests when the giants struck fear into the gods; the arms he wielded he never moves."

And I to him: "If it can be, I would have my eyes experience the boundless Briareus."

To which he replied: "You will see Antaeus near here, speaking and unbound, who will place us at the bottom of all evil.

The one you wish to see is much further away, bound and made like this one, except that his face appears more ferocious."

Never before had there been an earthquake so violent that it shook a tower as quickly as Phialtes was able to shake himself.

Then I feared death more than ever, and there was no need for anything more than the learned, if I had not seen the twists.

We then proceeded further and came to Antaeus, who, a full five years old, without his head, emerged from the cave.

"O you who in the fortunate valley that Scipio made the heir of glory, when Hannibal and his men turned their backs,

have already brought a thousand lions as prey, and who, had you been at the high war of your brothers, still seem to believe

that the sons of earth would have conquered: put them down, and do not be disgusted, where Cocytus locks in the cold.

Do not make us go to Tityus or Typhus: he can give what is desired here; therefore, bend down and do not twist your snout.

He can still restore your fame in the world, that he lives, and still awaits a long life if grace does not call him to himself before its time."

So said the master; and he quickly stretched out his hands and took hold of my leader, where Hercules already felt a great grip.

Virgil, when he felt himself taken, said to me: "Come here, so that I may take you"; then he made it so that he and I were one bundle.

As it seems to gaze upon the Carisenda beneath the slope, when a cloud passes over it so that it leans against it:

Such seemed Anteus to me, who was watching to see him bend, and there was a time when I would have liked to go another way.

But lightly at the depth that devours Lucifer and Judas, he wedded us; nor, so bowed, did he dwell there,

and like a mast on a ship he rose.

Inferno · Canto XXXII

If I had harsh and hackneyed rhymes, as befits the sad hole over which all the other rocks thrust,

I would press the juice of my concept more fully; but since I do not have it, I do not lead myself to speak without fear;

for it is not an undertaking to be taken lightly to describe the depths of the entire universe, nor a tongue that calls for mother or father.

But may those women aid my verse who helped Amphion to enclose Thebes, so that the words may not differ from the facts.

O above all the ill-bred people who dwell in a place where speech is hard, better had you been sheep or goats here!

As we descended into the dark pit beneath the giant's much lowered feet, and I still gazed at the high wall,

I heard him say: "Watch your step; go, lest you trample with your feet the heads of the wretched, weary brothers."

So I turned and saw before me and beneath my feet a lake that, because of the cold, had the appearance of glass and not water.

Danoia in Osterlicchi did not cast such a thick veil over its course in winter, nor Tanaï there under the cold sky,

as it did here; that if Tambernicchi had fallen there, or Pietrapana, it would not have made a crack at the edge.

And as a frog croaks with its muzzle out of the water when it often dreams of gleaning the peasant,

livid, as far as where shame appears, the mournful shades were in the ice, setting their teeth to the note of a stork.

Each one kept their faces turned downward; from their mouths the cold, and from their eyes the sad heart seeks testimony between them.

When I had looked around a little, I turned to my feet and saw two so close together that their scalps were mingled together.

"Tell me, you who so tightly press your breasts," I said, "who are you?" And they bowed their necks; And then, when their faces were raised to me,

their eyes, which before were still soft inside, dripped onto their lips, and the frost constricted the tears between them and closed them again.

Never did wood bind them so tightly with wood; so that they, like two goats butting together, were overcome by such rage.

And one who had lost both ears to the cold, still with his face down, said: "Why do you look so much at us?

If you want to know who these two are, the valley where Bisenzo slopes is the birthplace of their father Alberto and of them.

From one body they emerged; and you will be able to search all of Caina, and you will find no shadow more worthy of being stuck in jelly:

not those whose chest and shadow were broken by a blow from Arthur's hand; not Focaccia; not this one who burdens me

with his head so that I can no longer see, and he was called Sassol Mascheroni; if you are Tuscan, you know well by now who he was.

And so that you do not engage me in further discourse, know that I was Camiscion de' Pazzi; and I await Carlin to exonerate me."

Then I saw a thousand cur-like faces made by the cold; from which I have a distaste, and always will have, for frozen puddles.

And while we were moving toward the center where all burdens gather, and I trembled in the eternal shade;

whether it was will or fate or fortune, I know not; but, walking among the heads, I struck one hard in the face with my foot.

Weeping, he scolded me: "Why do you trample me? If you do not come to increase the vengeance of Montaperti, why do you molest me?"

And I: "My Master, now wait here for me, so that I may escape from a doubt through this man; then, however you wish, you will hasten me."

The leader stopped, and I said to him who was still cursing harshly: "Who are you, who thus reproaches others?"

"Now who are you," he replied, "who go along the Antenora, striking others on the cheeks, so that, if I were alive, it would be too much?"

"I am alive, and it must be dear to you," was my reply. "If you demand fame, let me put your name among the other notes."

And he to me: "I desire the opposite. Get up from here and don't bother me anymore, for you know little how to flatter with this blade!"

Then I grabbed him by the scalp and said: "You must name yourself, or you mustn't have any hair left up here."

Whereupon he to me: "Because you take my hair off, I won't tell you who I am, nor will I show you, if you come upon my head a thousand times."

I already had his hair wrapped in my hand, and had pulled out more than a lock, he barking with his eyes cast down,

when another shouted: "What's the matter with you, Bocca? Isn't it enough for you to clank with your jaws if you don't bark? What devil touches you?

"Now," I said, "I don't want you to speak any more, wicked traitor; for to your shame I will bring true news of you."

"Go away," he replied, "and tell what you want; but don't be silent, if you leave here, about him who just now had such a ready tongue.

He weeps here for the silver of the French: 'I saw,' you might say, 'that one from Duera, where the sinners lie in wait.'

If you were asked, 'Who else was there?' you have beside you that one from Beccheria whose gorget Florence sawed off.

I believe Gianni de' Soldanier is further away with Ganellone and Tebaldello, who opened Faenza when they slept."

We had already departed from him when I saw two frozen in a hole, so that one head was a hat to the other;

and as bread is eaten by hunger, so the uppermost teeth were placed on the other, where the brain joins the nape of the neck.

Just as Tydeus gnawed at the temples of Menalippus in disdain, as he did the skull and the other things.

"O you who show by such a bestial sign hatred toward him whom you devour, tell me why," I said, "by this agreement,

that if you rightly weep for him, knowing who you are and his sin, I may still change you in the world above,

if that with which I speak does not dry up."

Inferno · Canto XXXIII

The sinner raised his mouth from the savage meal, wiping it on the hair of his head, which he had previously ravaged.

Then he began: "You want me to renew the desperate pain that already weighs on my heart, even thinking about it, before I speak of it.

But if my words are the seed that bears infamy to the traitor I gnaw at, you will see me speaking and weeping at the same time.

I do not know who you are, nor how you came down here; but you truly seem Florentine when I hear you.

You must know that I was Count Ugolino, and this is Archbishop Ruggieri: now I will tell you why I am such a neighbor.

That, as a result of his never-ending thoughts, trusting him, I was captured and then killed, is not necessary to say;

But what you cannot have understood, that is, how cruel my death was, you will hear, and you will know if he has wronged me.

A narrow opening within the Muda, which for me bears the title of hunger, and which must still be closed for others,

had already shown me through its opening many moons, when I had the bad dream that rent my veil of the future.

This one seemed to me a master and lord, chasing the wolf and cubs on the mountain where the Pisans cannot see Lucca.

With lean, eager dogs, Count Gualandi, Sismondi, and Lanfranchi had placed themselves before him.

In a short run, the father and sons seemed tired to me, and with their sharp paws I seemed to see them tearing their flanks.

When I awoke before the morning, I heard my children who were with me weeping in their sleep and asking for bread.

Cruel indeed you are, if you do not grieve already at the thought of what my heart was foretelling; and if you do not weep, why are you accustomed to weep?

They were already awake, and the hour was approaching when food was usually brought to us, and each one was in doubt because of his dream;

and I heard the door beneath the horrible tower being locked; so I looked into the faces of my children without saying a word.

I did not weep, so I was petrified within: they wept; and my little Anselm said: "You look so, father! What is the matter?"

Therefore I neither wept nor answered all that day nor the night after, until the next sun rose into the world.

When a little light had entered the painful prison, and I glimpsed my own face in four faces,

I bit both my hands in pain; and they, thinking I did it out of desire to eat, immediately rose

and said: "Father, it will be much less painful for us if you eat of us: you clothed this wretched flesh, and you strip it."

Then I calmed myself so as not to make them sadder; that day and the next we were all silent. Ah, hard earth, why did you not open?

After we had reached the fourth day, Gaddo threw himself at my feet, saying: "My father, why do you not help me?"

Here he died; And as you see me, I saw the three fall one by one between the fifth and sixth days; so I began,

already blind, to grope over each one, and called them for two days, after they were dead. Then, more than the pain, the fasting was powerful."

When he had said this, with his eyes averted, he took the wretched skull with his teeth, which were strong on the bone, like a dog's.

Ah Pisa, reproach of the people of the beautiful country where the "yes" sounds, since your neighbors are slow to punish you,

let Capraia and Gorgona move and hedge the Arno at its mouth, so that it drowns everyone in you!

For if Count Ugolino had a rumor of having betrayed you of your castles, you should not have placed your sons on such a cross.

The new age made innocent, new Thebes, Uguiccione and Brigata and the other two whom the song above calls.

We passed beyond, where the frost harshly swaddles another people, not turned downward, but completely thrown back.

Even weeping does not allow me to weep there, and the grief that finds a stumbling block in my eyes turns inward to increase my anguish;

for the first tears form a cluster, and like crystal visors, fill the entire cup beneath my brow.

And although, like a callus, the cold had obliterated every sensation in my face,

I already seemed to feel a slight wind; whereupon I said: "My Master, who is causing this? Is not every vapor extinguished down here?"

Whereupon he said to me: "You will soon be where your eye will answer you of this, seeing the reason why the breath rains down."

And one of the sad ones from the cold crust cried out to us: "O souls so cruel, whose last chance has been given to you,

remove the harsh veils from my face, so that I may vent the grief that impregnates my heart, a little, before the tears freeze."

So I said to him: "If you want me to remember you, tell me who you are, and if I do not free you, I must go to the bottom of the ice."

Then he replied: "I am Brother Alberigo; I am the one from the fruit of the bad garden, who here takes back a date for a fig."

"Oh," I said to him, "are you still dead?" And he to me: "How my body remains in the world above, I have no knowledge.

This Ptolemy has such an advantage that often the soul falls there before Atropos moves it.

And so that you may more willingly wipe the glazed tears from my face, know that, as soon as the soul betrays

as I did, its body is taken by a demon, who then governs it until its time is complete.

It falls into such a cistern; and perhaps it still appears to be the body above of the shade that winters here behind me.

You must know, if you come down just now: it is Ser Branca Doria, and many years have passed since he was thus locked up."

"I believe," I said to him, "that you deceive me; for Branca Doria has not died at all, and he eats and drinks and sleeps and wears clothes."

"Up in the ditch," he said, "of the Malebranche, where the tenacious pitch boils, Michel Zanche had not yet arrived,

when he left the devil in his place in his body, and a neighbor who committed the betrayal with him.

But now stretch out your hand; open my eyes." And I did not open them; and it was courtesy for him to be rude.

Ah, Genoese, men unlike every custom and full of every flaw, why are you not scattered throughout the world?

For with the worst spirit of Romagna I found one of you, whose soul, through his deed, is already bathed in Cocytus,

and in body he seems still alive above.

Inferno · Canto XXXIV

"The royal banner of hell bears toward us; therefore, look ahead," said my master, "if you discern it."

As when a heavy fog blows, or when our hemisphere grows dark, a mill seems far away that the wind turns,

I then seemed to see such a building; then, because of the wind, I shrank behind my leader, for there was no other cave there.

I was already there, and with fear I put it into my voice, where all the shadows were covered and showed through like straws in glass.

Others are lying; others stand erect, this one with her head, this one with her feet; another, like a bow, has her face turned to her feet.

When we had advanced so far that it pleased my Master to show me the creature who had the beautiful countenance,

he stepped before me and made me stand still, saying, "Behold, Dis, and behold the place where you must arm yourself with fortitude."

How I then became frozen and hoarse, ask not, reader, for I do not write it, for all speech would be insufficient.

I neither died nor remained alive; consider now, if you have any genius, what I became, deprived of both.

The Emperor of the woeful kingdom emerged from the middle of his chest from the ice; and I am more like a giant,

than giants do with his arms: see now how great must be that whole which is suited to such a part.

If he was once as beautiful as he is now ugly, and raised his brows against his Maker, all mourning must have come from him.

Oh, how great a marvel it seemed to me when I saw three faces on his head! One in front, and that was vermilion;

the other two were joined to it above the middle of each shoulder, and joined at the crest:

and the right one seemed between white and yellow; the left one was such to look at as come from where the Nile descends.

Under each one came two large wings, as befitted such a bird: I have never seen sea sails like them.

They had no feathers, but were like bats; and it fluttered so that three winds blew from it:

Then Cocytus froze completely. With six eyes he wept, and from three chins dripped tears and bloody drool.

From each mouth a sinner gnawed with his teeth, like a flax-brake, so that three of them were thus made to suffer.

To the one before him, biting was nothing compared to scratching, that sometimes his back was left completely stripped of skin.

"That soul up there who has the greatest pain," said the master, "is Judas Iscariot, who has his head inside and his legs outside.

Of the other two who have their heads underneath, the one who hangs from the black mug is Brutus: see how he writhes, and says nothing!

and the other is Cassius, who seems so limber. But night rises again, and now we must depart, for we have seen everything."

As it pleased him, I clasped his neck; and he took time and place, and when the wings were fully opened,

he took hold of the velvety ribs; from pile to pile he then descended down among the thick fur and the frozen crusts.

When we reached the point where the thigh turns, right on the thick of the hips, the leader, with difficulty and anguish,

turned his head to where his legs were, and clung to the hair like one who climbs, so that I thought I was returning to hell.

"Hold on tight, for by such stairs," said the master, panting like a weary man, "one must depart from so much evil."

Then he came out through a hole in a rock and placed me on the edge to sit down; then he offered me his careful step.

I raised my eyes and thought I saw Lucifer as I had left him, and I saw him holding his legs up;

and if I then became troubled, let the dull people think so, who do not see what point I had passed.

"Rise up," said the master, "on your feet: the road is long and the path is difficult, and already the sun returns at half-tester."

It was not a palace passage where we were, but a natural ravine that had poor ground and limited light.

"Before I tear myself from the abyss, my master," I said when I was upright, "speak to me a little to draw me from my error:

Where is the ice? And how is this stuck so upside down? And how, in so short an hour, has the sun made the journey from evening to morning?"

And he to me: "You still imagine yourself beyond the center, where I grasped the hair of the evil worm that pierces the world.

You were there as long as I descended; when I turned, you passed the point at which weights are lifted from all sides.

And you are now beneath the hemisphere that is opposite that which covers the great dry land, and beneath whose summit, consumed,

was the man who was born and lived without sin; you have your feet on a small sphere that forms the other face of the Giudecca.

Here it is morning, when over there it is evening; and this one, who made a ladder for us with his hair, is still fixed as before.

On this side he fell down from heaven; and the earth, which before leaned out from here, in fear of him made a veil of the sea,

and came to our hemisphere; and perhaps to flee him, that which appears from here left here an empty place, and ran back up."

There is a place down there from Beelzebub, as remote as the tomb extends, which is known not by sight, but by the sound

of a little stream that descends there through the hole in a rock, which it has gnawed, with its course that winds, and slopes slightly.

The leader and I entered by that hidden path to return to the bright world; and without caring for any rest,

we climbed up, he first and I second, until I saw some of the beautiful things that heaven bears, through a round hole.

And from there we emerged to see the stars again.

PURGATORIO
Purgatorio · Canto I

Now, to sail on better waters, the little vessel of my genius, which leaves behind such a cruel sea, raises its sails;

and I will sing of that second realm where the human spirit is purged and becomes worthy of ascending to heaven.

But here, O holy Muses, may dead poetry rise again; and here may Calïope rise a little,

continuing my song with that sound whose blow the wretched Magpies felt, so great that they despaired of forgiveness.

The sweet color of oriental sapphire, which gathered in the serene aspect of the center, pure to the first circle,

recommended delight in my eyes, as soon as I emerged from the dead air that had saddened my eyes and my breast.

The beautiful planet that encourages love made all the East smile, veiling the Pisces that were in its escort.

I turned to the right and fixed my attention on the other pole, and I saw four stars never seen except by the first people.

The sky seemed to rejoice in their flames: oh northern widowed place, since you are deprived of gazing at them!

As I withdrew from their gaze, turning a little to the other pole, where the Chariot had already disappeared,

I saw near me a single old man, worthy of such reverence in his appearance that no son more owes to a father.

He wore a long beard mixed with white hair, similar to his hair, from which a double stripe fell to his chest.

The rays of the four holy lights adorned his face with such brightness that I saw him as if the sun were before me.

"Who are you who have fled eternal prison against the blind river?" he said, moving those honest feathers.

"Who guided you, or who was your lamp, emerging from the profound night that always blackens the infernal valley?

Are the laws of the abyss thus broken? Or has a new counsel been changed in heaven, that, damned, you come to my caves?"

My guide then seized me, and with words and hands and reverent gestures he made my legs and my brow.

Then he replied: "I did not come from me: a lady descended from heaven, through whose prayers I helped him with my company.

But since it is your wish that our condition be explained more fully as it truly is, mine cannot be denied to you.

He never saw the last evening; but because of his madness he was so close to it that there was very little time to turn it around.

As I said, I was sent to him to save him; and there was no other way than this one I set out on.

I have shown him all the wicked people; and now I intend to show those spirits who purge themselves under your tutelage.

How I brought him would be long to tell you; power descends from above that helps me lead him to see and hear you.

Now may it please you to welcome his coming: he seeks freedom, which is so dear, as he knows who refuses life for it.

You know it, for death was not bitter for her in Utica, where you left the garment that on the great day will be so bright.

The eternal edicts are not ruined for us, for he lives and Minos does not bind me; but they are from the circle where are the chaste eyes

of your Marcia, who still in her sight begs you, oh holy breast, to keep her as yours: therefore, by her love, incline yourself to us.

Let us go through your seven kingdoms; I will bring thanks to her for you, if you deserve to be mentioned down there."

"Marcia pleased my eyes so much while I was there," he said then, "that I gave all the thanks she asked of me.

Now that she dwells beyond the evil river, she can no longer move me, by the law that was made when I left there.

But if a lady from heaven moves and governs you, as you say, there is no need for flattery: let it be enough that she asks me for her sake.

Go then, and have him girdled with a pure rush and wash his face so that all filth is wiped away;

for it would not be fitting, with your eye surprised by some mist, to go before the prime minister, who is one of those of Paradise.

This little island, from bottom to bottom, down there where the waves beat it, bears rushes on the soft mud:

no other plant that grows or hardens can live there, because it does not yield to blows.

Then let there be no income from here; the sun, which now rises, will show you how to take the mountain by an easier ascent.

So he disappeared; And I rose up without speaking, and drew back completely to my leader, and directed my eyes toward him.

He began: "Son, follow my steps: let us turn back, for from here this plain slopes to its low limits."

Dawn was conquering the morning hour that flees before, so that in the distance I recognized the trembling of the sea.

We were walking across the lonely plain like one returning to a lost path, which until it reaches it seems to him to be going in vain.

When we were there where the dew fights with the sun, because we are in a place where, in the breeze, it thins little,

my master gently placed both hands on the scattered grass; whereupon I, who was aware of his art,

turned my tearful cheeks toward him; There he made fully visible to me the color that hell hid from me.

Then we came to the desert shore, which never saw a man navigate its waters, who is then skilled in returning.

There he encircled me as pleased another: oh marvel! for as he chose the humble plant, so it was reborn

suddenly there from where he uprooted it.

Purgatorio · Canto II

The sun had already reached the horizon, whose meridian circle covers Jerusalem with its highest point;

and Night, which circles opposite him, issued from the Ganges with the Scales, which fall from her hand when she overwhelms;

so that the white and vermilion cheeks of beautiful Aurora, where I was, were turning orange through too much age.

We were still beside the sea, like people pondering their journey, who journey with their heart and their body.

And behold, as Mars, surprised by the morning, glows red through the thick vapors down in the west over the seabed.

So it appeared to me, if I still see it, a light coming across the sea so swiftly that its motion is matched by no flight.

From which, as I withdrew my eyes a little to ask my leader, I saw it again, brighter and larger.

Then on every side of it appeared to me something I knew not what white, and from beneath it, little by little, another emerged.

My master still said nothing, while the first white wings appeared; then, when he recognized the galley slave well,

he cried out: "Make sure, make sure your knees bend. Behold the angel of God: fold your hands; now you will see such officials.

See how he disdains human arguments, so that he wants no oar, nor any veil other than his own wings, between such distant shores.

See how he has them directed toward the sky, treating the air with his eternal feathers, which do not change like mortal hair."

Then, as the divine bird came closer and closer to us, it appeared brighter, so that the eye could not sustain it from close by,

but bent it downward; and it came to shore in a vessel so slender and light that the water swallowed nothing of it.

At the stern stood the celestial ferryman, one whose very description would make him blessed; and more than a hundred spirits sat within.

"In exitu Israel de Aegypto" they all sang together in one voice, along with all that is written of that psalm.

Then he made the sign of the holy cross over them, whereupon they all threw themselves onto the shore; and he departed, as quickly as he came.

The crowd that remained there seemed wild with the place, gazing around like one who tastes new things.

The sun, which had driven Capricorn from mid-heaven with its numerous arrows, was shooting down on all sides.

Then the new people raised their heads toward us, saying, "If you know, show us the way to the mountain."

And Virgil replied, "You perhaps think we are familiar with this place; but we are pilgrims like you.

A little while ago we came, a little ahead of you, by another road, which was so rough and steep that the ascent will now seem like fun to us."

The souls who, outside of me, realized by my expiration that I was still alive, grew pale in wonder.

And as a messenger bearing an olive branch draws people to hear news, and no one seems shy of following,

so all those fortunate souls fixed their gaze on my face, almost forgetting to go and make themselves beautiful.

I saw one of them draw forward to embrace me with such great affection that it moved me to do the same.

Oh, vain shadows, except in appearance! Three times I clasped my hands behind her, and as many times I returned with them to my breast.

I think I was filled with wonder; whereupon the shadow smiled and drew back, and I, following her, pushed on.

Softly she bade me pause; then I recognized who she was, and prayed that she would stop a moment to speak to me.

He answered me: "As I loved you in the mortal body, so I love you free: therefore I stop; but why are you going?"

"My Casella, to return once more to where I am, I make this journey," I said; "but how is so much time taken from you?"

And he to me: "No one has wronged me, if he who takes when and whom he pleases has so often denied me this passage;

for his will is made by just will: truly for three months he has taken away whoever he wished to enter, in complete peace.

So I, who was now turned toward the shore where the waters of the Tiber flow into the sea, was kindly received by him.

He now directs his wing to that mouth, because it always gathers there whoever does not descend toward Acheron.

And I: "If a new law does not take away your memory or the use of the amorous song that used to soothe all my pains,

may it please you to console my soul somewhat, which, with his person coming here, is so weary!"

"Love that speaks in my mind," he began then so sweetly that the sweetness still resounds within me.

My master and I and those people who were with him seemed so content, as if no one else had anything else in mind.

We were all fixed and attentive to his notes; and behold, the honest old man cried out: "What is this, slow spirits?

What negligence, what standing still is this? Run to the mountain and strip away the rock that God does not allow to be manifest to you."

As when, gathering grain or darnel, pigeons gathered together to feed, quiet, without showing their usual pride,

if something appears that makes them afraid, they suddenly abandon the bait, because they are assailed by greater care;

so I saw that fresh flock abandon their song and flee toward the hillside, like a man who goes without knowing where he ends;

nor was our departure any less sudden.

Purgatorio · Canto III

Although the sudden flight scattered those across the countryside, turning toward the mountain where reason searches us,

I clung to my faithful companion: and how would I have run without him? Who would have drawn me up the mountain?

He seemed to me to be remorseful within himself: O dignified and pure conscience, how bitter a bite is this small fault to you!

When his feet left the haste that disdains the integrity of every action, my mind, which before was restricted,

broadened its intent, as if it were dreaming, and I turned my gaze toward the hill that extends toward the highest heaven.

The sun, which blazed red behind me, was broken before the figure that had in me the support of its rays.

I turned aside, fearful of being abandoned, when I saw the dark earth alone before me;

and my comforter, "Why do you distrust?" began to say to me, all turned; "Do you not believe me with you, and that I will guide you?

Espers are already there where the body within which I cast a shadow is buried; Naples has it, and it is taken from Brandizio.

Now, if nothing shadows me, marvel no more than at the heavens, which one ray obstructs the other.

Virtue disposes such bodies to suffer torments, heat and cold, and, as she does, does not want them to reveal themselves to us.

Mad is he who hopes that our reason can travel the infinite path that one substance holds in three persons.

Be content, human people, with the quia; for, if you could have seen everything, there would have been no need to give birth to Mary;

and you saw such fruitless desires that their desire would have been satisfied, which is eternally given to them as mourning:

I speak of Aristotle and Plato and many others." And here he bowed his head and said no more, remaining troubled.

Meanwhile we reached the foot of the mountain; there we found the rock so steep that our legs would have been ready to enter the Arno.

Between Lerice and Turbia, the most deserted, the most broken ruin, is a stairway, towards it, easy and open.

"Now who knows on which side the hillside slopes," said my master, halting his pace, "so that he who goes without wings can ascend?"

And while he, keeping his face down, was examining his mind about the journey, and I was gazing up around the rock,

on the left hand a group of souls appeared to me, moving their feet toward us, and it seemed unseemly, so slowly they came.

"Raise," I said, "Master, your eyes: behold, from this side one who will give us counsel, if you cannot have it from yourself."

He then looked, and with a free expression replied: "Let us go there, for they come slowly; and you, steady your hope, sweet son."

That people were still far away—I say, after a thousand steps—as far as a good thrower could throw with his hand,

when they all pressed close to the hard rocks of the high bank, and stood firm and close together, as if one were standing to watch, in doubt.

"O well-finished ones, O already chosen spirits," Virgil began, "by that peace which I believe is awaited for you all,

tell us where the mountain lies, so that it may be possible to go up; for to waste time is most displeasing to those who know most."

As sheep come out of the fold one by one, two by three, and the others stand timidly, lowering their eyes and muzzles;

and what the first does, the others do, crowding close to it, if it stops, simple and quiet, and they know not why;

so I saw the head of that fortunate herd then move to come, modest in face and dignified in its gait.

When those in front saw the light broken on the ground on my right side, so that the shadow was between me and the cave,

they stopped and retreated a little, and all the others who were following, not knowing why, did the same.

"Without your asking, I confess to you that this is a human body you see, because the light of the sun is split on the earth.

Do not marvel, but believe that not without power from heaven does it seek to overcome this wall."

So said the master; and those worthy people: "Return," he said, "then enter forward," making a sign with the backs of their hands.

And one of them began: "Whoever you are, thus going, turn your face: consider if you ever saw me from there."

I turned toward him and looked steadily: he was blond and handsome and of gentle aspect, but one of his eyebrows had been split by a blow.

When I humbly regretted having ever seen him, he said, "Now see," and showed me a wound on his chest.

Then, smiling, he said, "I am Manfred, grandson of the Empress Constance; therefore, I beg you, when you return,

go to my beautiful daughter, mother of the honor of Sicily and Aragon, and tell her the truth, if anything else is said.

After I had broken my body with two mortal spears, I surrendered, weeping, to Him who willingly forgives.

Horrible were my sins; but infinite goodness has such wide arms that it takes all who turn to it.

If the shepherd of Cosenza, who was sent to hunt me down by Clement at that time, had read this face in God correctly,

my bones would still be at the top of the bridge near Benevento, under the guard of the heavy mora.

Now the rain bathes them and the wind moves them from outside the kingdom, almost along the Verde, where it transferred them with the light extinguished.

By their curse, eternal love is not lost so much that it cannot return, while hope has the flower of the green.

It is true that whoever dies in contumacy of Holy Church, even if he finally repents, must stay outside this bank,

for every thirty years he has been in his presumption, unless this decree is made shorter by good prayers.

See now if you can make me happy by revealing to my good Costanza how you saw me, and also this prohibition;

for here much is left for those over there."

Purgatorio · Canto IV

When, through delight or pain, which comprehends some of our virtues, the soul gathers itself to them,

it seems to no longer have any power; and this is contrary to the error that believes that one soul within us is enkindled above another.

And therefore, when one hears or sees something that holds the soul firmly turned toward itself, time passes and one does not notice it;

for one power is that which hears it, and another is that which holds the entire soul: this is as if bound, that is free.

Of this I had true experience, hearing that spirit and marveling; for the sun had risen a full fifty degrees,

and I had not noticed, when we came to where those souls cried out to us with one accord: "Here is your request."

A greater openness often imprudently penetrates the countryside with a forkful of its thorns when the grapes are turning brown,

than the path through which my leader ascended, and I behind him, alone, when the band departed from us.

One goes to Sanleo and descends to Noli, one climbs up to Bismantova and the Cacume with one's feet; but here one must fly;

I mean with nimble wings and with the plumes of great desire, following that guide who gave me hope and gave light.

We were climbing through the broken rock, and on each side the edge was tightening, and feet and hands wanted the ground below.

When we were on the highest edge of the high bank, on the exposed slope, "My Master," I said, "what way shall we go?"

And he to me: "Let no step of yours fall; just gain on the mountain behind me, until some wise escort appears."

The summit was so high that it surpassed the view, and the hillside far more superb than the line from the mid-quadrant to the center.

I was weary when I began: "O sweet father, turn and look how I remain alone, if I did not stop."

"My son," he said, "pull yourself up there," pointing to a ledge a little higher up that on that side completely encircles the hill.

His words so spurred me on that I forced myself to follow him, until the strap was under my feet.

We both sat down there, facing east from which we had ascended, for it is customary for others to look.

First I directed my eyes to the low shores; then I raised them to the sun, and marveled that from the left we were being struck.

The poet clearly perceived that I was standing completely stunned by the chariot of light, where it entered between us and the North Wind.

Whereupon he said to me: "If Castor and Pollux were in company with that mirror which conducts its light up and down,

you would see the red Zodiac still more closely revolving than the Bears, if it had not strayed from the old path.

How this is, if you wish to be able to think it through, gather yourself within yourself, imagine Zion with this mountain standing on the earth

so that both have a single horizon and different hemispheres; hence the road that Phaethon was unable to carve,

you will see how this one must go on one side, while that one on the other, if your mind pays close attention."

"Certainly, my master," I said, "I never saw clearly, as I discern, where my intelligence seemed to fail,

that the half-circle of the supernal motion, which is called the Equator in some art, and which always remains between the sun and the winter,

for the reason you say, departs from here toward the north, whence the Hebrews saw it toward the warm side.

But if it please you, I would willingly know how far we have to go; for the hill rises higher than my eyes can ascend."

And he to me: "This mountain is such that it is always heavy at the beginning from below; and the higher one goes, the less it hurts.

However, when it seems so sweet to you that going up becomes as easy as going down in a ship,

then you will be at the end of this path; there wait to rest your troubles. I answer no more, and this I know for a truth."

And as he had spoken his word, a voice nearby called out: "Perhaps you will be distressed to sit down first!"

At the sound of it, each of us turned, and we saw on our left a large rock, which neither he nor I had noticed before.

We drew near there; and there were people standing in the shade behind the rock, as a man resigns himself to sitting through laziness.

And one of them, who seemed weary to me, was sitting and embracing his knees, keeping his face low between them.

"O my sweet lord," I said, "behold him who shows himself more negligent than if sloth were his sister."

Then he turned to us and fixed his attention, moving his face just above his thigh, and said: "Now go up, you who are valiant!"

I recognized then who he was, and the anguish that still quickened my breath a little did not prevent me from going to him; and when

he had reached him, he barely raised his head, saying: "Have you seen how the sun drives its chariot on the left shoulder?"

His lazy gestures and terse words moved my lips a little to a smile; then I began: "Belacqua, I no longer grieve

about you; but tell me: why are you sitting here? Are you waiting for an escort, or have you simply returned to your usual way?"

And he: "O brother, what does it mean to go up? For the angel of God who sits at the gate would not let me go to torment.

First, heaven must surround me outside it as much as it did in life, because I delayed my good sighs at last,

if first prayer does not help me that rises from a heart that lives in grace. What is the other prayer worth, which is not heard in heaven?"

And already the poet was climbing ahead of me, and was saying: "Come now; see that the sun has touched noon, and Morocco is already covering the shore

with its foot the night."

Purgatorio · Canto V

I had already departed from those shades, and was following in the footsteps of my leader, when, behind me, pointing her finger,

one cried out: "See, the ray does not seem to shine from the left to him below, and he seems to be walking as if alive!"

I turned my eyes at the sound of this motto, and I saw them gaze in wonder only at me, only at me, and at the light that was broken.

"Why is your mind so entangled," said the master, "that you slacken your pace? What does that which is whispered there do to you?

Come behind me, and let the people speak: stand like a firm tower, whose top never falls because of the blowing of the winds;

For always the man in whom thought springs upon thought, stretches the limit of himself, because the ardour of one excites the other.

What could I say except, "I come"? I said it, somewhat with the discolored hue that sometimes makes a man worthy of pardon.

Meanwhile, along the hillside, people were coming a little ahead of us, singing "Miserere" verse by verse.

When they realized that my body did not allow the rays to pass through, they changed their song to a long, hoarse "Oh!";

and two of them, in the guise of messengers, ran to meet us and asked: "Let us know your condition."

And my master: "You can go and tell those who sent you that this man's body is true flesh.

If they stayed to see his shadow, as I believe, their answer is sufficient: let them do him honor, and it may be dear to them."

I have never seen burning vapors split the clear sky so quickly at first night, nor, at the setting sun, August clouds,

that these did not return up sooner; and, having arrived there, they turned toward us with the others, like a band that flows without restraint.

"These people who press toward us are many, and they come to pray to you," said the poet: "so go, and listen as you go."

"O soul who goes to be happy with those limbs with which you were born," they came crying, "quiet your pace a little.

See if you have ever seen any of us, so that you may bring news of him from there: ah, why do you go? ah, why do you not stop?

We were all already dead by force, and sinners until the last hour; there the light of heaven made us aware,

so that, repenting and forgiving, we left life at peace with God, who burns in us the desire to see Him."

And I: "Why do I gaze into your faces? I recognize no one; but if it pleases you what I can, well-born spirits,

you say, and I will do it for that peace which, following the feet of such a guide, I was made to seek from world to world."

And one began: "Everyone trusts in your kindness without swearing it, so long as their will is not repelled.

Therefore I, who speak alone before the others, beg you, if ever you see that land that lies between Romagna and that of Charles,

that you be courteous to me with your prayers in Fano, so that they may worship me well, so that I may purge the grave offenses.

Then I was; but the deep holes from which the blood flowed, where I sat, were made for me in the lap of the Antenori,

where I believed myself safest: he from Esti made it, who had me in anger far beyond my rightful purpose.

But if I had fled toward Mira, when I had overtaken Oriaco, I would still be where the breath is.

I ran to the marsh, and the reeds and the mire tangled me so that I fell; and there I saw my veins form a pool on the ground.

Then another said: "Ah, if that desire that draws you to the high mountain be fulfilled, aid mine with good pity!

I was from Montefeltro, I am Bonconte; Giovanna or anyone else cares nothing for me; therefore I go among them with low brow."

And I to him: "What force or what fortune led you so far away from Campaldino that your burial place was never known?"

"Oh!" he replied, "at the foot of the Casentino there crosses a stream called the Archiano, which rises above the Hermitage in the Apennines.

There where his word becomes vain, I arrived, pierced in the throat, fleeing on foot and bleeding across the plain.

There I lost my sight and speech; in the name of Mary I ended, and there I fell, and only my flesh remained.

I will speak the truth, and you will repeat it among the living: the angel of God took me, and he from hell cried out: "O you of heaven, why do you deprive me?

You take away the eternal from this one for a little tear that takes him from me; but I will take care of the other!"

You know well how in the air that moist vapor gathers, which returns to water, as soon as it rises where the cold catches it.

That evil will arrived, which only asks evil with the intellect, and moved the smoke and the wind by the power that nature gave it.

Then, as the day faded, the valley from Pratomagno to the great ridge was covered with mist; and the heavens above became intent,

so that the pregnant air turned to water; the rain fell, and into the ditches came what the earth could not bear;

and as it joined the great streams, it rushed toward the royal river so swiftly that nothing could hold it back.

The stout Archian found my frozen body at its mouth; and he pushed it into the Arno, and loosed from my breast the cross

that I made of myself when grief overcame me. He turned me over the banks and the bottom, then covered me with his prey and encircled me.

"Ah, when you have returned to the world and rested from your long journey," the third spirit continued the second,

"remember me, who am Pia; Siena made me, Maremma unmade me: he who had first ringed me with his jewel rose up,

and wedded me with his jewel.

Purgatorio · Canto VI

When the game of zara ends, the loser remains grieving, repeating the turns and learning sadly;

with the other, all the people go away; some go in front, some behind, and some to the side, he remembers;

he does not stop, and listens to this and that; to whom he extends his hand, he no longer presses; and thus he defends himself from the crowd.

Such was I in that dense crowd, turning my face to them, this way and that, and promising to free myself from it.

There was the Aretine who was killed by the fierce arms of Ghin di Tacco, and the other who drowned while running in pursuit.

There prayed with outstretched hands Federigo Novello, and the man from Pisa who made good Marzucco appear brave.

I saw Count Orso and his soul separated from his body by hatred and by rage, as he said, not by any sin committed.

Pierre da la Bróccia, I say; and here, while she is on this side, let the Lady of Brabant take care of herself, so that she may not be of a worse herd.

When I was freed from all those shades who only pray that others pray, so that they may hasten their becoming saints,

I began: "It seems that you deny me, O my light, expressed in some text that bends a heavenly decree;

and these people pray for this: would their hope then be vain, or is your saying not clear to me?"

And he to me: "My writing is plain; and their hope is not deceptive, if one looks carefully with a sound mind;

for the summit of judgment does not descend so that the fire of love may accomplish in one moment what must satisfy him who dwells here;

and where I fixed that point, no defect could be amended by praying, because the prayer was separated from God.

Truly, do not dwell on such a deep suspicion, unless she tells you, who is the light between truth and intellect.

I do not know if you understand: I speak of Beatrice; you will see her up there, on the summit of this mountain, smiling and happy."

And I: "Lord, let us go with greater haste, for I no longer tire myself as before, and now you see that the hill casts a shadow."

"With this day ahead," he replied, "we will go as far as we can now; But the fact is of another form than you indicate.

Before you are up there, you will see him return who already covers himself with the hillside, so that you do not break his rays.

But see there a soul who, standing all alone, looks toward us: it will show us the quickest path.

We came to her: O Lombard soul, how haughty and disdainful you stood, and how modest and slow in moving your eyes!

She said nothing to us, but let us go, looking only like a lion when he rests.

Yet Virgil drew near to her, begging her to show us the best way; and she did not answer his question,

but asked us about our country and our life; and the sweet leader began: "Mantua . . . ", and the shade, all alone within itself,

rose toward him from the place where it had been standing before, saying: "O Mantuan, I am Sordello of your land!"; and they embraced each other.

Ah, slave Italy, hostelry of sorrow, ship without a helmsman in a great storm, not a lady of provinces, but a brothel!

That gentle soul was so ready, only for the sweet sound of her homeland, to give her citizen a feast there;

and now within you your living are not free from war, and one gnaws at the other, those whom a wall and a ditch enclose.

Wretched one, search around your shores for your shores, and then look within yourself, to see if any part of you enjoys peace.

What good is it for Justinian to mend your bridle,
if the saddle is empty?
Without it there would be less shame.

Ah, people who should be devout and let Caesar sit in the saddle, if you understand well what God tells you,

see how this beast has become fallen from not being corrected by spurs, since you put your hand to the predella.

O German Albert, who abandons this one who has become untamed and savage, and should have straddled her saddle,

may a just judgment from the stars fall upon your blood, and be new and open, so that your successor will fear it!

You and your father have suffered, through greed for those who are there, the garden of the empire to be deserted.

Come and see the Montecchi and Cappelletti, the Monaldi and Filippeschi, a man without care: some already sad, and these with suspicions!

Come, cruel one, come, and see the pressure of your nobles, and heal their troubles; and you will see how dark Santafior is!

Come and see your Rome, which weeps, widowed and alone, and calls day and night: "My Caesar, why do you not accompany me?"

Come and see how much people love each other! And if no pity moves you for us, you will be ashamed of your fame.

And if I may, O supreme Jove, who was crucified on earth for us, are your just eyes turned elsewhere?

Or is it a preparation that you make in the abyss of your counsel for some good, completely separated from our awareness?

For all the cities of Italy are full of tyrants, and every peasant who takes sides becomes a Marcellus.

My Florence, you can be content with this digression that does not concern you, thanks to your people who argue.

Many have justice in their hearts, and shoot late so as not to come to the bow without counsel; but your people have it at the top of their mouths.

Many refuse the common burden; but your people eagerly respond without calling, and cry: "I will undertake it!"

Now be happy, for you have good sources: you are rich, you are peaceful, and you are wise! If I speak the truth, the effect does not hide it.

Athens and Lacedaemon, who made the ancient laws and were so civilized, made a small sign of good living

toward you, who make such subtle provisions that in mid-November what you spin in October does not arrive.

How many times, in the time you remember, have you changed law, currency, office, and custom, and renewed your limbs!

And if you remember well and see the light, you will see yourself like that sick woman who cannot find rest on her feathers,

but by turning her pain shields herself.

Purgatorio · Canto VII

After the honorable and joyful greetings had been repeated three and four times, Sordel drew back and said: "Who are you?"

"Before the souls worthy of ascending to God were directed to this mountain, my bones were buried by Octavian.

I am Virgil; and for no other crime did I lose heaven than for not having faith." Thus then my guide replied.

As is he who suddenly sees something before him that marvels, who believes and does not, saying: "She is . . . is not . . . »,

such seemed he; and then he lowered his brows, and humbly returned to him, and embraced him there where the lesser one clings.

"O glory of Latin," he said, "through whom our language showed what it could, O eternal treasure of the place from which I was,

What merit or what grace does it show me? If I am worthy of hearing your words, tell me if it comes from hell, and from what cloister."

"Through all the circles of the woeful kingdom," he replied, "I have come here; heaven's power moved me, and with it I come.

Not by doing, but by not doing, have I lost sight of the high Sun you desire and which was too late for me to recognize.

There is a place down there, not sad with torment, but only with darkness, where the laments do not sound like wails, but are sighs.

There I am with the innocent children bitten by the teeth of death before they were freed from human sin;

There I am with those who did not clothe themselves with the three holy virtues, and without vice recognized the others and followed them all.

But if you know and can, give us some clue as to how we can come more quickly to where purgatory has its rightful beginning."

He replied: "There is no certain place; I am permitted to go up and around; as far as I can go, I will guide you.

But you see now how day is fading, and going up at night is not possible; therefore it is good to think of a pleasant abode.

Souls are remote to the right here; if you consent, I will lead you to them, and they will not be known to you without delight."

"How is that?" was answered. "Would anyone who wanted to go up at night be hindered by others, or would it not be that he could not?"

And good Sordello rubbed his finger on the ground, saying: "See? This line alone you would not cross after the sun has set:

not that anything else, other than the darkness of the night, hindered the upward movement; that entangles the desire with inability.

We could well return down with her and wander around the hillside, while the horizon closes the day.

Then my lord, almost in admiration, said, "Lead me there, then, where you say one can find delight in staying."

We had gone a little way from there, when I noticed that the mountain was diminished, as the valleys diminish it here.

"There," said that shadow, "we will go where the hillside forms its own lap; and there we will await the new day."

Between steep and plain was a winding path, which led us to the side of the lake, where the edge dies more than halfway.

Gold and fine silver, cocoa and white lead, indigo, wood polished and serene, fresh emerald in the hour of its decay,

by the grass and flowers, placed within that bosom, each would be overcome in color, as the lesser is overcome by the greater.

Nature had not merely painted there, but from the sweetness of a thousand scents she created one unknown and indistinct.

'Hail, Queen!' I saw souls sitting singing on the greenery and on the flowers there, who in the valley did not appear from outside.

'Before the faint sun now nestles,' began the Mantuan who had turned us, 'do not wish me to guide you among these.'

From this cliff you will better recognize the gestures and faces of all, than those gathered among them below on the blade.

He who sits highest and pretends to have neglected what he should have done, and who does not move his mouth to the songs of others,

was Emperor Rudolph, who could heal the wounds that have killed Italy, so that it is slow to be revived by others.

The other, who comforts him with his sight, ruled the land where the water rises that Molta in Albia, and Albia in the sea carries it:

He was named Ottacchero, and in swaddling clothes he was far better than his bearded son Vincislaus, who feeds on lust and idleness.

And that little nose, who seems close to counsel with him who has such a benign aspect, died fleeing and disfloring the lily:

Look there how he beats his chest! See the other, who has made a bed on the cheek of his palm, sighing.

Father and father-in-law are the source of France's ill-will: they know its vile and filthy life, and hence comes the grief that so afflicts them.

He who seems so strong and who harmonizes, singing, with him with the manly nose, wore the cord of every valor girded;

and if the youth who sits behind him had remained king after him, his valor would have gone from vessel to vessel,

which cannot be said of the other heirs. James and Frederick hold the kingdoms; no one possesses a better inheritance.

Rarely does human probity rise again through its branches; and this is what He who gives it desires, so that it may be called by Him.

My words also go to the long-nosed Pier, no less than to the other, who sings with him, for which Puglia and Provence already lament.

The plant is so inferior to its seed, that, more than Beatrice and Margaret, Costanza still boasts of her husband.

See the king of the simple life sitting there alone, Henry of England: he has a better outcome in his branches.

He who lowest among these, looking up, is Marquis William, for whom both Alexandria and her war

makes Monferrato and Canavese weep.

Purgatorio · Canto VIII

It was already the hour that turns the desire of seafarers and softens the heart on the day they said farewell to their sweet friends;

and the new pilgrim is stung by love when he hears a distant trumpet that seems to mourn the dying day;

when I began to render hearing vain and to gaze upon one of the souls who had risen, begging with her hand to listen.

She reached out and raised both hands, fixing her eyes toward the east, as if saying to God: "Take care of nothing else."

"Te lucis ante" came from her lips so devoutly and with such sweet notes, that it made me leave my mind;

and then the others followed her sweetly and devoutly throughout the entire hymn, keeping their eyes on the supernal wheels.

Here, reader, sharpen your eyes to the truth, for the veil is now so thin indeed that it is easy to pass through.

I then saw that noble army silently look up, as if waiting, pale and humble;

and I saw two angels emerge from above and descend with two flaming swords, truncated and stripped of their points.

Green as newly-grown leaves, they were in robes, which they trailed behind them, stricken and fanned by green feathers.

One came to stand a little above us, and the other descended to the opposite bank, so that the people remained in the middle.

I could clearly discern their blond heads, but my eye wandered over their faces, like a virtue that is confused by too much.

"Both come from the lap of Mary," said Sordello, "to guard the valley, against the serpent that will soon come."

Whereupon I, not knowing by which path, turned around, and drew close, all frozen, to the faithful shoulders.

And Sordello also: "Now let us descend among the great shades, and we will speak to them; it will be very pleasing for them to see you."

I believe I descended only three steps, and I was below, and I saw one who was looking only at me, as if he wanted to recognize me.

The air had already darkened for a time, but not so dark that between his eyes and mine he did not reveal what he had previously locked.

He turned toward me, and I toward him: gentle judge Nin, how pleased I was when I saw you were not among the wicked!

No kind greeting was silent between us; then he asked: "How long has it been since you came to the foot of the mountain through the distant waters?"

"Oh!" I said to him, "through the sad places I came this morning, and I am in my first life, although by going thus I am gaining the other."

And as soon as my answer was heard, he and Sordello gathered back like people suddenly bewildered.

The one turned to Virgil and the other to someone who was sitting there, crying: "Up, Currado! Come and see what God has willed by his grace."

Then, turning to me: "By that singular gratitude you owe to him who so hides his first love, for there is no ford there,

when you are beyond the wide waves, tell my Giovanna to call for me there where the innocent are answered.

I do not believe her mother loves me anymore, since she changed the white bandages, which it is fitting that, miserable one, she still longs for.

Through her it is very easy to understand how long the fire of love lasts in a woman, if the eye or touch does not often kindle it.

The viper that Melanesi camps will not make her a burial as beautiful as the Gallura rooster would have done.

Thus he spoke, marked by the stamp, in his aspect, of that righteous zeal that moderately burns in the heart.

My greedy eyes went only to the sky, only there where the stars are slowest, like a wheel closest to its stem.

And my leader: "Son, what are you looking up there?" And I to him: "At those three torches that burn the entire pole on this side."

Whereupon he said to me: "The four bright stars you saw this morning are low over there, and these have risen where those were."

As he spoke, Sordello drew him to himself, saying: "See our adversary over there"; and he pointed his finger so that he would look there.

On that side where the little valley has no shelter, there was a snake, perhaps the one that gave Eve her bitter food.

Through the grass and flowers came the evil slither, now turning its head and now licking its back like an animal preening itself.

I did not see, and therefore cannot say, how the celestial hawks moved; but I clearly saw both the one and the other move.

Hearing the air cleft by its green wings, the serpent fled, and the angels turned, flying back to their posts alike.

The shadow that had gathered before the judge when he called, through all that assault was not at all freed from my gaze.

"If the lamp that leads you upward finds in your will as much wax as is needed to reach the highest lustre,"

she began, "if you know true news of Val di Magra or a nearby region, tell me, who was once great there.

I was called Currado Malaspina; I am not the ancient one, but I descended from him; I brought to my people the love that is refined here."

"Oh!" I said to him, "I have never been through your lands; but where does one live throughout Europe that they are not known?

The fame that your house honors proclaims the lords and the region, so that anyone who has not yet been there knows of it;

and I swear to you, if I go above, that your honored people will not be disgraced by the value of their purse and sword.

Use and nature so favor her that, while the world turns its evil head, she alone goes straight and scorns the evil path.

And he: "Now go; lest the sun turn seven times upon the bed that the Ram covers and straddles with all four feet,

for this courteous opinion will be nailed in the middle of your head with more nails than from another's speech,

if the course of judgment is not stopped."

Purgatorio · Canto IX

The concubine of ancient Tithonus was already blanching on the eastern balcony, outside the arms of her sweet friend;

her brow was shining with gems, set in the shape of the cold animal that strikes people with its tail;

And night, of the steps with which it ascends, had taken two in the place where we were, and the third was already lowering its wings;

when I, who had with me that of Adam, overcome by sleep, bowed down on the grass where all five of us were already sitting.

At the hour when the swallow begins its sad laments near morning, perhaps in memory of its first woes,

and when our mind, a pilgrim more from the flesh and less gripped by thoughts, is almost divine in its visions,

in a dream I seemed to see an eagle suspended in the sky with golden feathers, its wings outstretched and ready to descend;

and I seemed to be there where Ganymede's followers were abandoned, when he was snatched from the highest consistory.

I thought to myself: 'Perhaps this one strikes here only out of habit, and perhaps she disdains to carry us up on her feet from another place.'

Then it seemed to me that, having wheeled a little, she descended like a terrible lightning bolt and snatched me up to the fire.

There it seemed that she and I were burning; and the imagined fire burned so fiercely that sleep must have broken.

Just as Achilles awoke, rolling his awakened eyes around and not knowing where he was,

when his mother stole him sleeping from Chiron to Scyros in her arms, there from where the Greeks later departed him;

I shook myself, as sleep fled from my face, and I became pale, as does a man who, frightened, freezes.

My only comfort was beside me, and the sun was already more than two hours high, and my face was turned toward the sea.

"Do not fear," said my lord; "be confident, for we are on the right track; do not press, but loosen all your strength.

You have now reached purgatory: see there the cliff that closes it all around; see the entrance there where it seems cut off.

Just now, in the dawn that precedes the day, when your soul was sleeping within, above the flowers that adorn it down there,

a woman came and said: "I am Lucia; let me take this sleeping man; then I will help him on his way."

Sordel remained, and the other gentle forms; she took you, and as soon as the day was clear, she came up; and I followed in her footsteps.

Here she rested, but first her beautiful eyes showed me that open entrance; then she and sleep went together.

Like a man who is assured by doubt and who turns his fear into comfort, when the truth is revealed to him,

I changed; and when my leader saw me without concern, he moved up the cliff, and I backed away toward the height.

Reader, you see well how I raise my subject, and therefore do not marvel if I reinforce it with more art.

We approached, and were at a place where at first it seemed to me to be broken, just like a crack that divides a wall,

I saw a door, and three steps below to go up to it, of different colors, and a doorkeeper who still said nothing.

And as I opened my eyes more and more, I saw him sitting on the supreme step, so much so that I could not bear it;

and he had a naked sword in his hand, which reflected the rays so toward us that I often turned my face in vain.

"Tell us down there: what do you want?" he began to say, "where is the escort? See that coming up does not disturb you."

"Lady of heaven, aware of these things," my master replied to him, "just now told us: 'Go there: there is the door.'"

"And she advances your steps in good," the courteous doorkeeper began again: "Come then forward to our steps."

There we came; And the first stair, white marble, was so polished and smooth that I saw myself reflected in it as I appear.

The second was colored more than perspex, a rough and scorched stone, cracked lengthwise and crosswise.

The third, which was massive above, seemed to me to be porphyry, as flaming as blood gushing from a vein.

On this one, the angel of God had both feet, sitting on the threshold that seemed to me like a diamond stone.

My guide willingly led me up the three steps, saying, "Humbly ask him to release the lock."

I devoutly threw myself at the holy feet; I begged for mercy and that he would open it for me, but first I struck myself three times in the chest.

He drew seven Ps on my forehead with the point of his sword, and said, "See that you wash these wounds, when you are inside."

Ashes, or earth that is dug up dry, were of the same color with his clothing; and from underneath he took two keys.

One was gold and the other was silver; first with the white one and then with the yellow one he locked the door so that I was content.

"If one of these keys fails to turn straight through the lock," he said to us, "this door will not open.

The one is more precious; but the other requires too much art and ingenuity before it can be unlocked, because it is the one that unties the knot.

I hold them to be Pier; and he told me that I err rather in opening it than in keeping it closed, so long as people will fall at my feet."

Then he pushed the door to the sacred gate, saying: "Enter; but I warn you that he who looks behind returns from outside."

And when the corners of that sacred palace, which are of metal and resonant and strong, were twisted on their hinges,

Tarpea did not roar so much, nor did she appear so harsh, when good Metellus was taken from her, for which she remained emaciated.
