for will, if it does not will, is not quenched, but acts as nature does to fire, if a thousand times violence twists it.

Therefore, whether it bends much or little, force follows; and so these souls, being able to flee to the holy place.

If their will had been whole, as it held Lorenzo on the steps, and made Muzio stern to his hand,

it would have pushed them back along the path by which they were drawn, as they were freed; but such firm will is too rare.

And because of these words, if you have gathered them as you should, the argument that would have annoyed you many times is gone.

But now another step crosses before your eyes, one that you would not be able to escape by yourself: before that you would be weary.

I have certainly put it into your mind that a blessed soul cannot lie, because it is always close to the first truth;

and then you could hear from Piccarda that Costanza held her affection for the veil; so that she seems to contradict me here.

Many times already, brother, it has happened that, to escape danger, one has done against one's will what was not fitting;

just as Almeon, who, at his father's entreaty, killed his own mother, to avoid losing pity, became merciless.

At this point I want you to consider that force and will are mixed together, and they make it so that offenses cannot be excused.

Absolute will does not consent to harm; but it consents only insofar as it fears, if it withdraws, falling into greater anguish.

Therefore, when Piccarda squeezes that, she understands the absolute will, and I the other; so that we speak truth together.

Such was the surging of the holy stream that issued from the source whence all truth flows; such a one and the other desire were brought to peace.

"O love of the first lover, O goddess," I said afterwards, "whose speech inundates and warms me so, that it enlivens me more and more,

my affection is not so deep that it suffices to render you grace for grace; but let He who sees and can respond to this.

I see clearly that our intellect is never satisfied unless it is illumined by the truth, from which no truth extends.

It rests upon it, like a beast on a gleaming rock, as soon as it has reached it; and it can reach it; otherwise, every desire would be frustrated.

Therefore, doubt springs up like a shoot at the foot of truth; and it is nature that pushes us to the summit from neck to neck.

This invites me, this assures me with reverence, lady, to ask you about another truth that is obscure to me.

I want to know if man can satisfy your unfulfilled desires with other goods that do not seem to you to be worthless.

Beatrice looked at me with eyes filled with sparks of love so divine that, overcome, my strength gave way,

and I almost lost myself with downcast eyes.

Paradiso · Canto V

"If I blaze at you in the heat of love beyond the measure seen on earth, so that I surpass the power of your face,

do not marvel, for this comes from perfect vision, which, as it apprehends, so moves its foot toward the good apprehended.

I see clearly how the eternal light already shines in your intellect, which, when seen, alone and always kindles love;

and if your love seduces something else, it is only some trace of that, poorly recognized, that shines through there.

You wish to know if with other service, for less than a vow, one can render the soul so secure from joy.

So began Beatrice this song; and like a man who does not break his speech, she continued the sacred process thus:

"The greatest gift that God in his generosity made in creating, and most conformed to his goodness, and that which he most appreciates,

was freedom of will; with which intelligent creatures, and all and alone, were and are endowed.

Now it will seem to you, if you argue from this, the high value of the vow, if it is so made that God consents when you consent;

For, in establishing the pact between God and man, a victim is made of this treasure, just as I say; and it is made with its action.

So what can be given as compensation? If you believe you can use well what you have offered, I want to do good work with an ill-gotten gain.

You are now certain of the greatest point; but since Holy Church dispenses this, which seems contrary to the truth I have revealed to you,

you must still sit at table a little, because the rigid food you have taken still requires help in your dispensing.

Open your mind to what I reveal to you and fix it there; for without retaining, having understood does not constitute knowledge.

Two things are consonant with the essence of this sacrifice: one is what it is made of; the other is the appropriateness.

The latter is never erased unless observed; and about it so precisely is spoken of above:

Therefore the Hebrews were compelled to offer, even if some offerings were exchanged, as you must know.

The other, which is open to you as a matter, may well be such that there is no mistake if it is exchanged for another matter.

But let no burden be transferred to his shoulder at his own discretion, without the vaulting of both the white and the yellow keys;

and consider every exchange foolish, unless the thing left in the surprise, like the four in the six, is collected.

Therefore whatever weighs so much in its value that it tips every scale, cannot be satisfied with any other expense.

Let not mortals take the vow for gossip; be faithful, and do not be sceptical in doing so, like Jephthah at his first bribe;

It was more fitting to say, 'I did evil,' than to do worse by keeping it; and so foolish can you find the great Duke of the Greeks,

where Iphigenia wept over his beautiful face, and made fools and wise men weep for himself, hearing talk of such a learned man.

Be more serious, Christians, in moving forward: do not be like a feather before every wind, and do not believe that every water can wash you.

You have the New and the Old Testament, and the Shepherd of the Church to guide you; let this suffice for your salvation.

If evil greed cries out to you otherwise, be men, and not foolish sheep, so that the Jew among you will not laugh at you!

Do not be like a lamb that leaves its mother's milk, and, simple and lascivious, fights with itself at its own pleasure!

Thus Beatrice to me as I write; then she turned all longing to that part where the world is most alive.

Her silence and the change in her countenance silenced my eager mind, which already had new questions before it;

and like an arrow that strikes its mark before the string is quiet, so we raced into the second realm.

There I saw my lady so happy, as if she had entered the light of that heaven, that the planet became more luminous.

And if the star changed and smiled, what did I do, who by my nature am changeable in all ways!

As in a calm and pure fishpond the fish are drawn to whatever comes from outside, so that they consider it their food,

so I saw more than a thousand splendors drawn toward us, and in each was heard: "Behold he who will increase our loves."

And as each one approached us, the shade was seen full of joy in the bright lightning that issued from it.

Think, reader, if what is begun here did not proceed, how much more anguished longing you would have to know;

and for yourself you will see how I longed to hear from these men their conditions, as they were manifest to me.

"O well-born one, to whom grace is granted to see the thrones of eternal triumph before the war is abandoned,

we are enkindled by the light that spreads throughout the heavens; and therefore, if you wish to clarify yourself about us, you may satisfy yourself at your pleasure."

Thus was it said to me by one of those pious spirits; and by Beatrice: "Say, say with certainty, and believe as in gods."

"I see clearly how you nestle in your own light, and that you draw it from your eyes, because it sparkles as you laugh;

but I know not who you are, nor why you have, worthy soul, the rank of the sphere that veils itself from mortals with other people's rays."

This I spoke directly to the light that had first spoken to me; whereupon it became brighter far than it was.

Just as the sun, which hides itself from too much light, just as the heat has corroded the tempers of the thick vapors,

for greater joy, the holy figure thus hid itself from me within its ray; and thus, closed and closed, it answered me

in the manner that the following canto sings.

Paradiso · Canto VI

"After Constantine turned his eagle against the course of the sky, which it followed behind the ancient one that Lavina took,

for a hundred and a hundred years and more the bird of God remained at the edge of Europe, near the mountains from which he first emerged;

and under the shadow of his sacred wings he governed the world there from hand to hand, and, thus changing, he reached mine.

Caesar I was and am Justinian, who, by the will of the first love I feel, removed from within the laws the excessive and the vain.

And before I was attentive to the work, I believed that one nature was no longer in Christ, and with that faith I was content;

But blessed Agapitus, who was the supreme shepherd, directed me to sincere faith with his words.

I believed him; and what was in his faith I now see as clearly as you see every contradiction, both false and true.

As soon as I set foot with the Church, God was pleased by his grace to inspire me with the lofty work, and I gave myself entirely to it;

and to my Belisarius I commended the arms, to which the right hand of heaven was so joined that it was a sign that I should rest.

Now here is my answer to the first question; but its condition compels me to follow up with some addition,

so that you may see with what reason those who move against the sacrosanct sign are those who appropriate it and those who oppose it.

See how much virtue has made it worthy of reverence; and it began from the hour that Pallas died to give him the kingdom.

You know that he made his home in Alba for three hundred years and more, until the end when the three still fought for him.

And you know that from the woe of the Sabine women to the grief of Lucretia he did in seven kings, conquering the neighboring peoples all around.

You know what he did, carried by the illustrious Romans against Brennus, against Pyrrhus, against the other princes and colleges;

whereby Torquatus and Quinctius, who was named by the neglected Cirrus, the Decii and the Fabii gained the fame I willingly mirror.

He crushed the pride of the Arabs who, following Hannibal, crossed the Alpine rocks, the Po, of which you lament.

Under him, young men Scipio and Pompey triumphed; and to that hill beneath which you were born it seemed bitter.

Then, near the time when all heaven wanted to restore the world to its own serene state, Caesar, by Rome's will, took it.

And what he did from the Var to the Rhine, he saw Isara and Hera, and he saw the Seine and every valley that fills the Rhone.

What he did after he left Ravenna and leaped the Rubicon was such a flight that neither tongue nor pen could follow it.

Toward Spain he turned his host, then toward Durazzo, and struck Pharsalia so that the heat of the Nile was felt with grief.

Anthandros and Simeonta, from which he set out, he saw again, and there where Hector nestles; and then he shook himself badly for Ptolemy.

From there he descended, flashing, to Iuba; whence he turned toward your west, where he heard the Pompeian trumpet.

Brutus and Cassius barked in hell for what he did with the next messenger, and Modena and Perugia were grieved.

Wretched Cleopatra still weeps for him, who, fleeing before him, took sudden and black death from the snake.

With him he ran to the ruby ​​shore; with him he placed the world in such peace that his shrine was closed to Janus.

But what the sign that makes me speak had first made and then was wrought for the mortal realm that is beneath it,

becomes apparently small and obscure, if one looks at it in the hands of the third Caesar with clear eyes and pure affection;

For the living justice that inspires me granted him, in the hands of him whom I speak, the glory of taking vengeance on his wrath.

Now marvel at what I tell you: then with Titus he ran to take vengeance for the vengeance of ancient sin.

And when the Lombard tooth bit the Holy Church, Charlemagne, victorious, under its wings, succored her.

Now you can judge those whom I accused above and their faults, which are the cause of all your ills.

One opposes the yellow lilies to the public sign, and the other appropriates it for a private one, so that it is hard to see who is most at fault.

Let the Ghibellines practice, let them practice their art under another sign, for he who separates justice from it always follows it badly;

and let not this new Charles and his Guelphs strike it down, but fear the claws that tore the fleece of a loftier lion.

Many times have sons wept for their father's sin, and let no one believe that God exchanges weapons for his lilies!

This little star is adorned with the good spirits who have been active so that honor and fame may succeed it:

and when desires rest there, thus straying, it is fitting that the rays of true love rest less brightly above.

But in measuring our wages against their merit lies a part of our joy, because we see them neither less nor greater.

Therefore, living justice sweetens our affection so that it can never be turned to any iniquity.

Diverse voices make sweet notes; Thus diverse seats in our life bring sweet harmony among these wheels.

And within this present pearl shines the light of Romeo, whose great and beautiful deeds were disliked.

But the Provençals who fought against him did not laugh; and therefore he who takes harm from the good deeds of others is ill-advised.

Ramondo Beringhiere had four daughters, each a queen,
and this was done to him by
Romeo, a humble and foreign man.

And then he moved his crooked words to demand an account from this just man, who assigned him seven and five for ten,

then he departed poor and old; and if the world knew the heart he had, begging his life piece by piece,

it praises him greatly, and would praise him even more.

Paradiso · Canto VII

"Hosanna, holy God of Sabaoth, your most illustrious clarity, your happy fires, your malacòth!"

So, turning to his note, I saw that substance singing, upon which a double light gathers;

and it and the others moved to its dance, and like swift sparks they veiled themselves from me in sudden distance.

I hesitated and said to myself, "Tell her, tell her!" "Tell her," I said, "to my lady who quenches my thirst with her sweet drops."

But that reverence that possesses all of me, even for Be and for Ice, bowed me like a man who is asleep.

Beatrice endured me for a short time and began, beaming at me with a smile that would make a man happy in the fire:

"According to my infallible judgment, how just vengeance was justly punished has put you in thought;

but I will quickly untangle your mind; and you listen, for my words will bring great judgment to your attention.

By not suffering virtue that seeks to restrain its brave, that man who was never born, by damning himself, damned all his offspring;

where the human race lay infirm for many centuries in great error, until it pleased the Word of God to descend

where nature, which had been extended from its Maker, united to himself in person with the sole act of his eternal love.

Now look carefully at what is now being said: this nature, united to its Maker, as it was created, was sincere and good;

but of itself it was banished from Paradise, because it turned from the path of truth and its life.

The punishment, then, that the cross inflicted, if measured by the nature assumed, never stung so justly;

and so nothing was so injurious, considering the person who suffered, in whom that nature was contracted.

Therefore from one act different things came: that one death pleased God and the Jews; For her the earth trembled and the heavens opened.

It should no longer seem harsh to you, when it is said that just vengeance was later avenged by a just court.

But I now see your mind constricted from thought to thought within a knot, from which it awaits with great desire to unravel.

You say: "I discern well what I hear; but why God wanted only this method for our redemption is hidden from me."

This decree, brother, lies buried in the eyes of everyone whose mind is not matured in the flame of love.

Truly, since one gazes at this sign often and discerns little, I will say why this method was more worthy.

The divine goodness, which from itself dispels all envy, burning within itself, sparkles so that it displays the eternal beauties.

What distills from her without half has no end, because its imprint does not move when she seals.

What rains from her without half is entirely free, because it is not subject to the power of new things.

The more it conforms to her, the more it pleases her; for the holy ardor that radiates from everything is most lively in that which is most similar.

The human creature benefits from all these gifts, and if one is lacking, its nobility must fall.

Sin alone is what frees it and makes it dissimilar to the supreme good, for it is little tarnished by its light;

and it never returns to its dignity unless it fills, where sin empties, with just punishments against evil delights.

Your nature, when it sinned completely in its seed, was removed from these dignities, as from paradise;

nor could it be recovered, if you look carefully, by any means, without passing through one of these fords:

Either God alone, out of His courtesy, had dismissed it, or man had satisfied his own folly by himself.

Now cast your eye into the abyss of the eternal counsel, fixed as closely as you can on my speech.

Man could never satisfy within his limits, because he could not go down by humility and obedience,

what by disobeying he intended to go up; and this is the reason why man was opened to the possibility of satisfying by himself.

Therefore, it was fitting for God to repair man's entire life by His own means—I mean by one, or by both.

But because a work is more pleasing to the doer the more it represents the goodness of the heart from which it came,

the divine goodness that imprints the world was content to proceed by all its ways to raise us up.

Nor was or will be, between the last night and the first day, so lofty or so magnificent a process, either by one or the other:

for God was more generous in giving himself to make man sufficient to raise himself, than if he had only dismissed himself;

and all other means were insufficient to justice, if the Son of God had not been humbled to become incarnate.

Now, to satisfy your every desire, I return to explain to you in some place, so that you may see there as I do.

You say: "I see water, I see fire, air, and earth, and all their mixtures, coming to corruption and lasting a short time;

and these things were created; therefore, if what is said were true, they should be safe from corruption."

The angels, brother, and the sincere land in which you are, can be said to be created, just as they are, in their entire being;

but the foods you have named and those things that are made of them are informed by created power.

The matter they possess was created; the informing power was created in these stars that revolve around them.

The soul of every animal and of plants of powerful complexion draws the ray and the motion of the holy lights;

but your life without intermediary breathes the highest beneficence, and makes it so enamoured of itself that it ever desires it.

And from this you can also argue your resurrection, if you consider how human flesh was formed at the time

when the first parents formed both of us."

Paradiso · Canto VIII

The world in its peril used to believe that the beautiful Cyprin radiated mad love, turned in the third epicycle;

wherefore the ancient people, in their ancient error, not only honored her with sacrifice and votive cry;

but they honored Dione and Cupid, the former as her mother, the latter as her son, and said that he sat on Dido's lap;

And from her, from whom I began, they took the name of the star that the sun gazes upon now from its cup, now from its brow.

I did not realize I was ascending into it; but my lady, whom I saw grow more beautiful, gave me strong faith that I was within it.

And as a spark is seen in a flame, and as a voice is discerned in a voice, when one is still and another comes and goes,

I saw in that light other lamps moving in a circle, more or less current, in the manner, I believe, of their internal visions.

From a cold cloud no winds, whether visible or not, descended so vigorously that they did not seem impeded and slow

to anyone who had seen those divine lights come to us, abandoning the circle first begun in the high Seraphim;

and within those who appeared further ahead, 'Hosanna' sounded so loud that I was never without longing to hear it again.

Then one of them drew closer to us and began alone: ​​"All are ready to please you, so that you may rejoice in us.

We turn with the celestial princes in one circle and one gyre and one thirst, to whom you once said of the world:

'You who move the third heaven with understanding'; and they are so full of love that, to please you, a little quiet would not be less sweet."

After my eyes had offered themselves reverently to my lady, and she had made them content and certain of herself,

they turned to the light that had promised so much, and "Ah, who are you?" was my voice imprinted with great affection.

And how much more and more did I see her become, for the new joy that increased, when I spoke, to her joys!

So she said to me: "The world had only a short time for me; and if it had been longer, much evil would have happened, which would not have been.

My joy keeps hidden from you, which shines around me and hides me like an animal swathed in its silk.

You loved me well, and you had good reasons; for if I had been below, I would have shown you my love more than the leaves.

That left bank that is washed by the Rhone after it mixes with the Sorgue awaited me as its lord in time,

and that horn of Ausonia that encompasses Bari and Gaeta and Catona, from where the Tronto and Verde rivers flow into the sea.

Already the crown of that land which the Danube washes after it abandons the German shores shone on my forehead.

And beautiful Trinacria, which looms between Pachynus and Peloro, above the gulf that receives the greatest vexation from Eurus,

not by Typhoeus but by rising sulphur, would still have waited for its kings, born to me of Charles and Rudolph,

if evil lordship, which always grieves subject peoples, had not moved Palermo to cry: "Die, die!"

And if my brother had foreseen this, the avaricious poverty of Catalonia would already have fled, so as not to offend them;

for truly provision must be made for him, or for someone else, so that his loaded boat is no longer burdened.

His nature, which descended from generous thrift, would need such a military force that he would not care to put in the ark.

"Because I believe that the high joy that your words instill in me, my lord, where all good things begin and end,

is seen through you as I see it, is more pleasing to me; and this too I hold dear because you discern it by gazing upon God.

You have made me happy, and so make me clear, since, by speaking, you have moved me to doubt how sweet seed can be made bitter."

This I said to him; and he to me: "If I can show you the truth, you will keep your gaze on what you ask as you keep your back.

The good that turns and satisfies the entire kingdom you explore makes its providence its virtue in these great bodies.

And not only are natures provided for in the mind that is perfect in itself, but they too, along with their salvation:

Therefore, whatever this bow shoots, when directed, falls to a foreseen end, as if something were directed to its target.

If this were not the case, the heaven you travel would produce its effects so that they would not be arts, but ruins;

and this cannot be, unless the intellects that move these stars are lacking, and the First One, which has not perfected them, is lacking.

Do you wish this truth to become more blanched for you?" And I: "Not at all; for I see it impossible that nature, in what is necessary, tires."

Whereupon he again: "Now tell me: would it be worse for man on earth if he were not a citizen?" "Yes," I replied; "and here I ask no reason."

"And can it be, if down below one does not live differently for different duties? No, if your master writes to you well."

So he deduced up to this point; then he concluded: "Therefore the roots of your effects must be different:

for one is born Solon and another Xerxes, another Melchizedek and another he who, flying through the air, lost his son.

Circular nature, which is a seal on mortal wax, practices its art well, but does not distinguish one home from another.

Hence it comes to pass that Esau, by seed, departs from Jacob; and Quirinus comes from such a vile father that he surrenders to Mars.

Nature, once created, would always follow its path similar to that of its begetters, if divine providence did not prevail.

Now what was behind you is before you: but so that you know that it benefits me, I want you to be clothed with a corollary.

Nature, if fortune finds it discordant with itself, like every other seed outside its region, always makes a bad trial.

And if the world down there would pay attention to the foundation that nature lays, following it, its people would be good.

But you turn to religion one who is born to gird himself with the sword, and make king of one who is of speech;

wherefore your path is astray."

Paradiso · Canto IX

After your Charles, beautiful Clemency, had enlightened me, he told me of the deceptions his offspring would suffer;

but he said: "Be silent and let the years pass"; so that I can say nothing except that just weeping will come in the wake of your misfortunes.

And already the life of that holy light had turned toward the Sun that fills it, like that good that is so great for all things.

Ah, deceived souls and impious creatures, who turn your hearts away from such good, straightening your temples in vanity!

And behold, another of those splendors turned toward me, and its desire to please me was signified by its brightness from without.

The eyes of Beatrice, which were fixed upon me as before, were fixed with dear assent to my desire.

"Ah, quickly compensate my will, blessed spirit," I said, "and prove to me that I can reflect in you what I think!"

Then the light, still new to me, from its depths, from which it had previously sung, continued as one that benefits from doing good:

"In that part of the depraved Italian land that lies between the Rialto and the fountains of Brenta and Piava,

a hill rises, and does not rise very high, there from which a torch once descended that made a great assault on the region.

From a root, both she and I were born: Cunizza was my name, and here I shine because the light of this star overcame me;

but I happily indulge myself in the cause of my fate, and it does not annoy me; which perhaps would seem strong to your vulgar.

Of this lustrous and dear joy of our heaven, which is closest to me, great fame remained; and before it dies,

this hundredth year is still five: see if the excellent man should act so that he relinquishes another life to the first.

And the present crowd that blocks the Tagliamento and the Adige does not think of this, nor does it yet repent for being beaten;

but soon Padua will change the water that bathes Vincenza to the marsh, because the people are cruel to their duty;

and where the Sile and Cagnano are joined, one lords it over and walks with his head held high, so that the spider's web is already being snatched up for him.

Feltro will still weep for the fault of its wicked shepherd, which will be so shameful that no one has ever entered Malta like it.

The vat would be too large to accommodate the blood of Ferrara, and weary would be he who weighed it ounce by ounce,

which this courteous priest will give to show his support; and such gifts are suited to the way of life of the land.

Up there are mirrors, you call them Thrones, from which God shines upon us in judgment; so that these words seem good to us."

Here he fell silent; and he made it seem to me that he was turning elsewhere, by the wheel on which he placed himself as he was in front.

The other joy, which I had already known as something dear, appeared to me like a fine balm on which the sun strikes.

For joy up there, radiance is acquired, just as laughter here; but below, the shadow outside darkens, as the mind is sad.

"God sees all, and your vision is infused," I said, "blessed spirit, so that no desire for itself can be futile for you.

So your voice, which always amuses the sky with the song of those pious fires that make the cradle of six wings,

why does it not satisfy my desires? I would not have listened to your question, if I could understand myself as you do."

"The greatest valley in which water spreads," his words then began, "outside of that sea that garlands the earth,

between discordant shores it goes so far against the sun that it makes meridian where the horizon first accustoms to be.

I was a shoreline of that valley between the Ebro and the Macra, which divides the Genoese from the Tuscan by a short journey.

Almost at the west and in a garden lies Buggea and the land from which I was born, which made its harbor already warm with its blood.

Folco, those people to whom my name was known, told me; and this sky imprints itself on me, as I did on him;

for the daughter of Belus no longer burned, annoying both Sychaeus and Creusa, than on me, until it was suitable for the skin;

Nor that Rhodope who was deluded by Demophon, nor Alcides when he had locked Iole in his heart.

But here she does not repent, but laughs, not at the guilt, which does not return to mind, but at the valor she ordered and provided.

Here she admires the art that adorns such affection, and discerns the good by which the world above returns that which is below.

But so that you may carry with you all your full desires that were born in this sphere, I must proceed further.

You wish to know who is in this light that here near me sparkles like a ray of sunshine in clear water.

Now know that within there Rahab is at peace; and joined to our order, hers is sealed in the highest degree.

From this heaven, where the shadow cast by your world falls, before any other soul was taken up by the triumph of Christ.

It was fitting to leave her as a palm in some heaven for the high victory that was won with both palms,

because she favored the first glory of Joshua in the Holy Land, whose memory touches the pope little.

Your city, which is the plant of him who first turned his back on his creator and whose envy is so lamented,

produces and spreads the accursed flower that has led the sheep and lambs astray, because it has made a wolf of the shepherd.

For this reason the Gospel and the great doctors are abandoned, and only the Decretals are studied, so that it appears on their edges.

The pope and the cardinals intend this; Their thoughts do not go to Nazareth, where Gabriel spread his wings.

But the Vatican and the other select parts of Rome, which have been a cemetery for the soldiery that Peter followed,

soon be free from the evil one."

Paradiso · Canto X

Looking at his Son with the Love that eternally inspires both, the first and ineffable Power

made everything in mind and place revolve with such order that whoever gazes upon it cannot be without tasting it.

Raise then, reader, your gaze with me to the high wheels, straight to that place where one motion strikes the other;

and there begin to dream of the art of that master who loves it so deeply that his eye never leaves it.

See how from there the oblique circle that bears the planets branches out, to satisfy the world that calls them.

For if their path were not crooked, much virtue in heaven would be in vain, and almost every power down here would be dead;

and if the departure were more or less distant from the right, much would be lacking both above and below the worldly order.

Now remain, reader, on your bench, thinking back on what you enjoy, if you wish to be happy rather than weary.

I have placed you before me: now feed yourself for yourself; for that matter for which I am made a scribe turns all my care to itself.

Nature's greatest minister, who imprints the world with the value of heaven and measures time with its light,

joined with that part which is remembered above, was turning through the coils in which he always presents himself most quickly;

and I was with him; but I did not notice the ascent, except as a man notices, or rather the first thought, of his coming.

It is Beatrice who sees herself from good to better, so suddenly that her action is not delayed.

How luminous must have been that which was within the sun where I entered, not by color, but by apparent light!

For I call upon genius, art, and practice, I would not say that it was ever imagined; but one can believe it, and one desires to see it.

And if our imaginations are so low, it is no wonder; for above the sun there was no eye that gazed.

Such was the fourth family of the high Father there, who always satisfies her, showing how he breathes and how he is a daughter.

And Beatrice began: "Thank, thank the Sun of the angels, who has raised you to this sensible world by his grace."

Never was the heart of a mortal so drawn to devotion and so ready to surrender to God with all its gratitude,

as I did at those words; and all my love was so focused on him that he eclipsed Beatrice in oblivion.

She was not displeased; but she laughed so much that the splendor of her laughing eyes divided my mind, united in many things.

I have seen many living and victorious lightning bolts center us and form a crown around themselves, sweeter in voice than dazzling in sight:

So we sometimes see Latona's daughter encircle, when the air is pregnant, so that it holds the thread that makes the circle.

In the court of heaven, from which I return, are found many jewels, dear and beautiful, so precious that they cannot be taken from the kingdom;

and the song of those lights was one of those; whoever does not soar as to fly up there, awaits the news from the silence there.

Then, thus singing, those burning suns had circled around us three times, like stars near the fixed poles,

they seemed to me like women, not released from the dance, but silently standing still, listening until the nine notes have been gathered.

And within one I heard it begin: "When the ray of grace, which kindles true love and then grows by loving,

redoubled in you, shines so brightly that it leads you up that ladder where no one descends without ascending;

whoever denies you the wine from his vial because of your thirst, is only as free as water that does not descend into the sea.

You wish to know from what plants this garland is adorned, which the beautiful lady who strengthens you in heaven gazes upon.

I was one of the lambs of the holy flock that Dominic leads on the path where one grows well if one does not wander.

This one, closest to me on my right, was my brother and teacher, and he is Alberto from Cologne, and I am Thomas Aquinas.

If you wish to be certain of all the others, follow my words, and turn your gaze upward through the blessed garland.

That other flame comes from the smile of Gratian, who helped both places so that it pleases in Paradise.

The other who adorns our choir next door was that Peter who, with the poor woman, offered his treasure to Holy Church.

The fifth light, which is most beautiful among us, breathes with such love that the whole world down there thirsts for news of it:

within is the lofty mind that was placed in such profound knowledge that, if the truth is true, no second rose to see so much.

Next, you see the light of that candle that down in the flesh saw the angelic nature and ministry most deeply.

In the other small light smiles that advocate of Christian times whose Latin Augustine provided himself.

Now if you wander your mind's eye from light to light following my praises, you are already thirsting for the eighth.

To see all good within, the holy soul rejoices, which the deceitful world makes manifest to those who hear her well.

The body from which she was banished lies down in Cieldauro; and she came from martyrdom and exile to this peace.

Behold, blazing beyond, the ardent spirit of Isidore, of Bede, and of Richard, who in contemplation was more than a man.

This, from which your regard returns to me, is the light of a spirit who, amidst grave thoughts, seemed slow to die:

It is the eternal light of Siger, who, reading in the Vico de li Strami, syllogized envious truths.

Then, like a clock that calls us at the hour when God's bride rises to call her husband to love her,

pulling and urging both sides, ringing with such sweet notes that the well-disposed spirit is swept away by love;

so I saw the glorious wheel move and give voice to voice in such a temper and sweetness that it cannot be known

except where joy is forever found.

Paradiso · Canto XI

O foolish care of mortals, how defective are those syllogisms that make you beat your wings below!

Some followed law, some aphorisms, some the priesthood, some reigned by force or sophistry,

some theft, some civil business, some absorbed in the delights of the flesh, some abandoned themselves to idleness,

when, freed from all these things, I was so gloriously welcomed with Beatrice up into heaven.

After each had returned to the point of the circle from which he had previously stood, he stopped, as if at a candelabra.

And I heard within that light that had spoken to me before, smiling, beginning, growing more radiant:

"Just as I shine with its ray, so, gazing into the eternal light, I learn the causes of your thoughts.

You doubt, and you want my words to be sought in such open and expansive language that they may reach your ears,

where before I said: 'Whoever grows fat,' and there I said: 'The second was not born'; and here it is necessary that I distinguish them clearly.

Providence, which governs the world with that counsel in which every created aspect is vanquished before it sinks to the bottom,

so that the bride of him who loudly wedded her with blessed blood might go toward her beloved,

safe in herself and even more faithful to him, ordained two princes in her favor, who would be her guides here and there.

One was all seraphic in ardor; the other, through wisdom, was a splendor of cherubic light on earth.

Of one I will speak, since of both one speaks in praise, whatever one takes, because their works were for one purpose.

Between Tupino and the water that descends from the hill chosen by blessed Ubaldo, a fertile slope of a high mountain hangs,

where Perugia feels the cold and heat of Porta Sole; and behind it, Nocera and Gualdo weep under their heavy yoke.

From this hillside, where it breaks its sharpest, a sun was born into the world, as this one sometimes does from the Ganges.

So whoever speaks of that place should not say Ascesi, for that would be too short, but Orient, if one really wants to use the word.

He was not yet far from the garden when he began to make the earth feel some comfort from his great virtue;

for for a certain woman, as a youth, he ran to war with his father, from whom, as with death, no one unlocks the door of pleasure;

and before her spiritual court and with his father he became united with her; thereafter, day by day, he loved her more deeply.

She, deprived of her first husband, remained for eleven hundred years and more despised and obscure, until he came to him without an invitation;

Nor was it any use to hear that he who had struck fear into the whole world found her safe with Amyclas, at the sound of his voice;

nor was it any use to be steadfast or ferocious, so that, where Mary remained below, she wept with Christ on the cross.

But lest I proceed too secretly, take Francis and Poverty as these lovers now in my diffused speech.

Their harmony and their joyful countenances, love and wonder and sweet gaze, were the cause of holy thoughts;

so much so that the venerable Bernard took off his shoes first, and ran after such peace, and, running, seemed to him to be slow.

Oh unknown riches! Oh fertile good! Giles takes off his shoes, Silvester takes off his shoes following the groom, so pleases the bride.

Then goes that father and that teacher with his wife and that family who were already tied to the humble noose.

Nor did cowardice of heart weigh down his brows because he was the son of Pietro Bernardone, nor because he seemed marvelously scorned;

but royally he revealed his harsh intention to Innocent, and from him received the first seal on his faith.

After the poor people grew behind him, whose wonderful life would be better sung in the glory of heaven,

the holy desire of this archimandrite was redeemed by Honorius with a second crown by the Eternal Spirit.

And then, thirsting for martyrdom, in the presence of the proud Sultan, he preached Christ and the others who followed him,

and to find the people too bitter for conversion and not to remain in vain, he returned to the fruit of the Italian grass,

on the rugged rock between the Tiber and the Arno he took from Christ the last seal that his limbs had borne for two years.

When it pleased Him who had bestowed such good upon him to raise him up to the reward he deserved in becoming a coward,

he commended his dearest lady to his brothers, as to just heirs, and commanded them to love her faithfully;

and from her bosom his illustrious soul wished to move, returning to its kingdom, and for his body he desired no other bier.

Consider now who he was, who was a worthy colleague in keeping Peter's bark on the high seas by a straight path;

and this was our patriarch; so that whoever follows him, as he commands, may discern that he is laden with good merchandise.

But his flock has become so greedy for new food that it cannot help but be scattered over various leaps;

And the farther his sheep wander and wander from him, the more empty they return to the sheepfold of milk.

They are indeed among those who fear harm and cling to the shepherd; but they are so few that little cloth is available for their cloaks.

Now, if my words are not hoarse, if your listening has been attentive, if you recall what is said to your mind,

your desire will be partly satisfied, for you will see the tree from which it is splintered, and you will see the correction that argues

"Where one grows well, if one does not wander."

Paradiso · Canto XII

As soon as the blessed flame took the last word to speak, the holy mill began to whirl;

and in its circle it did not completely turn before another circle enclosed it, and motion after motion and song after song it gathered;

A song that so conquers our muses, our serene ones in those sweet pipes, as it refuses the first splendor.

As two parallel and concolorous bows turn through a tender cloud, when Juno iubetes her handmaiden,

born from that within that without, in the manner of the speech of that lovely one whom love consumed like sun vapors,

and make the people here be presaged, by the pact that God made with Noah, of the world that will never again be flooded:

So the two garlands of those everlasting roses turn around us, and so the outer one responds to the inner one.

After the jubilation and the other great celebration, both of singing and of the blazing light with joyful and gentle light,

at the same time and wanting to calm down, just like the eyes that must both close and rise at the pleasure that moves them;

from the heart of one of the new lights a voice came, which made me seem like the needle of the star as I turned to its place;

and it began: "The love that makes me beautiful draws me to speak of the other leader by whom mine is spoken of so well.

It is fitting that where one is, the other be drawn: so that, as they fought for one, so their glory shines together.

The army of Christ, which had cost so dearly to rearm, moved slowly, hesitantly, and infrequently behind the standard,

when the Emperor, who always reigns, provided for the army, which was in doubt, by grace alone, not because it was worthy;

and, as is said, he aided his bride with two champions, to whose deeds and words the erring people rallied.

In that region where the sweet Zephyr rises to open the new leaves with which Europe is seen clothed,

not far from the crashing waves behind which, because of its long rage, the sun sometimes hides from every man,

sits fortunate Calaroga under the protection of the great shield where the lion subdues and subdues:

within it was born the loving lover of the Christian faith, the holy athlete, kind to his own and cruel to his enemies;

and as soon as she was created, her mind was so filled with living virtue that, in her mother, it became a prophet.

After the espousals were consummated at the sacred font between him and Faith, where they were endowed with mutual salvation,

the lady who gave her consent for him, saw in her sleep the wondrous fruit that was to come from him and his heirs;

and so that it was as it was in construction, the spirit was moved to name it by the possessive of which it was all.

Dominic was called; and I speak of him as of the farmer whom Christ chose for his garden to help him.

He seemed truly a messenger and a servant of Christ: for the first love that was manifest in him was for the first counsel Christ gave.

Often he was found silent and awake on the ground by his nurse, as if saying: "I have come for this."

Oh, his father, truly Felice! Oh, his mother, truly Giovanna, if, interpreted, it is worth as it is said!

Not for the world, for which he now toils after Ostense and Taddeo, but for the love of the true manna,

in a short time he became a great teacher; so much so that he set about circling the vineyard that soon turns white if the vinedresser is guilty.

And from the chair that was once more benign to the poor and just, not for its sake, but for the sake of Him who sits, who errs,

not to dispense two or three for six, not the formerly vacant fortune, not tithes, which are the paupers of God,

he asked, but against the erring world, permission to fight for the seed of which twenty-four plants swathe you.

Then, with doctrine and will together, with the apostolic office he moved like a torrent that presses a deep vein;

and he struck the heretical undergrowth with his impetus, most vigorously where the resistance was greatest.

From him were then made various streams that water the Catholic garden, so that its shrubs stand more alive.

If such was the one wheel of the chariot in which the Holy Church defended herself and won her civil battle,

the excellence of the other should be clear to you, of which Thomas was so courteous upon my arrival.

But the orbit that formed the highest part of its circumference is derelict, so that mold has grown where the crust once was.

His family, which moved straight with feet in its footprints, is so turned that what is ahead casts what is behind;

and soon the harvest of the bad cultivation will be seen, when the darnel will complain that its ark has been taken from it.

Truly I say, whoever searches our volume page by page will still find a page where he would read "I am what I am used to";

But it will not be from Casal or Acquasparta, where such come to writing, that one flees and another constrains it.

I am the life of Bonaventure of Bagnoregio, who in great offices always postponed the sinister care.

Illuminato and Augustin are here, who were among the first barefooted poor who in the halter became friends of God.

Hugh of San Vittore is here with them, and Pietro Mangiadore and Pietro Spano, who already shines in twelve little books;

Nathan the prophet and Metropolitan Chrysostom and Anselm and that Donatus who deigned to put his hand to the first art.

Rabanus is here, and beside me shines the Calabrese abbot Giovacchino, gifted with a prophetic spirit.

The fiery courtesy of Fra Tommaso and his discreet Latin moved me to salute such a champion;

and this company moved with me."

Paradiso · Canto XIII

Let him who understands well what I saw now—and hold the image, while I speak, like a firm rock—

imagine fifteen stars that in different regions enliven the sky with such serenity that it surpasses every companion of the air;

let him imagine that chariot for which the bosom of our heaven is sufficient both night and day, so that at the turning of the wheel it does not falter;

let him imagine the mouth of that horn that begins at the tip of the stem around which the first wheel goes,

having made of itself two signs in the sky, as the daughter of Minos made when she felt the chill of death;

and one having its rays within the other, and both turning so that one went first and the other after;

and it will almost have the shadow of the true constellation and of the double dance that circled the point where I was:

since it is as far beyond our custom as the heaven that surpasses all others moves beyond the motion of the Chiana.

There was sung not of Bacchus, not of Paean, but of three persons in divine nature, and in one person both that and the human.

It completed its singing and its turning, and those holy lights attended to us, congratulating itself from care to care.

The silence in the harmonious gods was then broken by the light in which the wondrous life of God's poor one, narrated, smokes,

and said: "When one straw is threshed, when its seed is already laid, sweet love invites me to thresh the other.

You believe that in the breast from which the rib was drawn to form the beautiful cheek whose palate costs all the world,

and in that which, pierced by the lance, both first and then so satisfied that it outweighs all sin,

insofar as human nature is permitted to have light, it was all infused with that value that created both;

and therefore consider what I said above, when I narrated that the good that is enclosed in the fifth light did not have the second.

Now open your eyes to what I answer you, and you will see your belief and my speech in truth become like a center in a circle.

That which does not die and that which can die is nothing but the splendor of that idea that our Lord gives birth to, in loving;

For that living light, which radiates so from its shining source that it is not separated from it nor from the love that intertwines with them,

through its goodness gathers its rays, as if mirrored, into nine subsistences, remaining eternally one.

Then it descends to the ultimate powers, from act to act, becoming so much that it no longer makes any more than brief contingencies;

and I understand these contingencies to be the generated things that the heavens produce, with and without seed, by moving.

The wax of these and he who guides it is not of the same order; and therefore under the ideal sign it shines more and less.

Hence it happens that the same wood, according to its species, bears better and worse fruit; and you are born with different geniuses.

If the wax were precisely deduced and the heavens were in its supreme virtue, the light of the seal would appear complete;

But nature always gives it incomplete, working likewise to the artist whose hand trembles at the habit of art.

Therefore, if ardent love disposes and marks the clear vision of the first virtue, all perfection is acquired there.

Thus was the earth once made worthy of all animal perfection; thus was the pregnant Virgin made;

so that I commend your opinion, that human nature never was nor will be as it was in those two persons.

Now, if I did not proceed further, your words would begin: "So, how was this one without appearance?"

But that what does not appear may appear well, consider who he was, and the reason that moved him, when it was said, "Ask."

I have not spoken so that you cannot clearly see that he was a king, who asked for wisdom so that he might be a sufficient king;

not to know the number of the motors up here, or whether they ever made necessity with contingent necessity;

it is not whether to give the first motion, or whether a triangle can be made from a half-circle so that it does not have a right angle.

Therefore, if you note what I said and this, royal prudence is that uneven vision on which the arrow of my intention strikes;

and if at the "surse" you direct your clear eyes, you will see that you have respect only for kings, who are many, and good are rare.

With this distinction, take my saying; and so it can stand with what you believe of the first father and our Beloved.

And let this always be lead at your feet, to make you move slowly like a weary man, both to the yes and the no that you do not see:

For he is among the lowest fools who without distinction affirms and denies in one as well as in another passage;

because he often finds that current opinion bends in a false direction, and then affection binds the intellect.

He who fishes for truth and lacks skill leaves farther away from the shore, because he does not return as he started.

And of this there are clear proofs in the world, Parmenides, Melissus, and Brissus, and many others who went and did not know where;

so did Sabellius and Arius, and those fools who were like swords to the Scriptures in making straight faces crooked.

Let not people, yet, be too sure of their judgments, like one who estimates the grain in the field before it is ripe;

for all winter I have seen the thorn appear first rigid and fierce, then bearing the rose on its top;

and I have once seen a vessel rush straight and swift through the sea along its entire course, finally perishing at the entrance to the mouth.

Do not let Lady Berta and Ser Martino, just because they see one stealing, another offering, believe they are within the divine council;

for one can rise, another can fall.

Paradiso · Canto XIV

From the center to the circle, and from the circle to the center, water moves in a round vessel, according as it is struck outside or inside:

In my mind this I say suddenly occurred to me, as the glorious life of Thomas was passed over in silence,

because of the similarity that arose between his speech and that of Beatrice, who was pleased to begin thus after him:

"This man needs, and he tells you neither with his voice nor yet in thought, to go to the root of another truth.

Tell me if the light that blossoms in your substance will remain with you eternally, as it is now;

and if it remains, say how, after you are made visible again, it can be so that the sight does not annoy you.

Just as, moved and drawn by greater joy, those who go on the wheel once raise their voices and cheer their actions,

so, at prompt and devout prayer, the holy circles show new joy in the return and in the familiar gaze.

He who laments that one must die here to live above has not seen here the refreshment of eternal torment.

That one and two and three that always lives and reigns in three and two and one, uncircumscribed, and circumscribes all,

was sung three times by each of those spirits with such melody that it would be just enough for every merit.

And I heard in the brightest light of the smallest circle a modest voice, perhaps like that of the angel to Mary,

answer: "As long as the feast of paradise lasts, so long will our love shine around this garment.

Its brightness follows the ardor; the ardor the vision, and that is as great as it has grace above its worth.

As the glorious and holy flesh is clothed, our person will be more pleasing for being whole;

Because that which the Supreme Good gives us with its free light, a light that conditions our seeing, will increase;

therefore the vision must increase, the ardor that is kindled by it must increase, the ray that comes from it must increase.

But just as coal gives off flame, and with its vivid whiteness overcomes it, so that its appearance defends itself;

so this lightning that already surrounds us will be overcome in appearance by the flesh that covers the earth all day;

nor will it be able to tire us with so much light: for the organs of the body will be strong for all that can delight in it.

Both choirs seemed so sudden and alert to me in saying "Amme!" that they clearly showed longing for the dead bodies:

perhaps not only for them, but for the mothers, the fathers, and the others who were dear before they became eternal flames.

And behold, around, a lustre of equal clarity was born above what was there, like a horizon that brightens.

And just as at the rising of early evening new appearances begin in the sky, so that the sight seems and does not seem real,

it seemed to me there that new existences were beginning to be seen, and were circling outside the other two circumferences.

Oh, the true sparkle of the Holy Spirit! how sudden and burning it became to my eyes, which, vanquished, could not bear it!

But Beatrice appeared to me so beautiful and smiling that among those visions I must leave aside the thought of following it.

Then my eyes began to rise again, and I saw myself translated alone with my lady into higher health.

I clearly perceived that I was more elevated, because of the fiery smile of the star, which seemed to me redder than usual.

With all my heart and with that speech that is one in all, I offered a holocaust to God, as befitted the new grace.

And the ardor of the sacrifice had not yet exhausted my breast, when I recognized that that liturgy had been accepted and auspicious;

for with such brightness and such splendor appeared to me within two rays, that I said: "O Helios, who so adorns them!"

As if, distinct from greater and lesser lights, the Galaxy shines white between the poles of the world, so that it makes the wise doubt;

those rays, so constellated in the depths of Mars, made the venerable sign that joins quadrants in a circle.

Here my memory overcomes my intellect; for that cross shone with Christ, so that I cannot find a worthy example;

but he who takes up his cross and follows Christ will still excuse me for what I lament, seeing Christ flash in that dawn.

From horn to horn and between the top and the bottom, lights move, brightly shining as they meet and pass:

thus here are seen, straight and crooked, swift and slow, renewing sight, the minutiae of bodies, long and short,

moving along the ray from which the shadow is sometimes streaked, which, for its defense, people acquire with ingenuity and art.

And as a jig and a harp, strung with many strings, make a sweet tinkle to one who cannot hear the note,

so from the lights that appeared to me there, a melody gathered through the cross that enraptured me, without understanding the hymn.

I clearly realized that it was of high praise, because to me came "Rise again" and "Conquer" as to one who neither understands nor hears.

I was so in love there that until then nothing had bound me with such sweet victories.

Perhaps my words seem too bold, postponing the pleasure of those beautiful eyes, where my desire, gazing, finds rest;

but he who realizes that the living seals of all beauty reach higher, and that I had not turned to them there,

can excuse me for what I accuse myself of, in order to excuse myself, and see that I speak the truth: for the holy pleasure is not disclosed here,

because, ascending, it becomes more sincere.

Paradiso · Canto XV

A benign will, in which love that rightly breathes is always dissolved, as greed does in the wicked,

put silence on that sweet lyre, and caused the holy strings that the right hand of heaven loosens and pulls to rest.

How can those souls be deaf to just prayers, who, to make me want to beg them, were united in silence?

It is true that he who, for love of something that does not last eternally, strips himself of that love, grieves without end.

As through the calm and pure serene skies, now a fire runs suddenly, moving eyes that were secure,

and seems like a star that changes place, except that from the side from which it is lit, nothing is lost, and it lasts but a short time:

just as from the horn that extends to the right at the foot of that cross, a star from the constellation that shines there ran;

nor did the gem depart from its ribbon, but ran along the radial line, like fire behind alabaster.

So piously did the shade of Anchises linger, if faith be deserved by our greater muse, when he perceived his son in Elysium.

"O my blood, O superinfused grace God, like you whose son I have never known?"

So that light: whereupon I gazed upon it; then I turned my face to my lady, and was astonished both here and there;

for within her eyes burned such a smile that I thought with mine I touched the depths of my glory and my paradise.

Then, joyfully hearing and seeing, my spirit reached its origin, things that I had not understood, so profoundly did it speak;

Nor was it hidden from me by choice, but by necessity, for its concept was set beyond the bounds of mortals.

And when the bow of the ardent passion was so vented that speech descended toward the mark of our intellect,

the first thing that was heard by me, "Blessed be you," was "Triune and One, who are so courteous to my seed!"

And it continued: "A grateful and distant fast, drawn from reading the great volume where white and brown never change,

you have resolved, son, within this light in which I speak to you, thanks to her who clothed you in plumage for the high flight.

You believe that your thought comes to me from the first, just as from the one, if it is recognized, the five and the six shine;

And therefore, what I am and why I seem more joyful to you, do not ask me than anyone else in this gay crowd.

You believe the truth; for the lesser and the greater of this life gaze into the mirror where, before they think, they cast their thoughts;

but so that the sacred love in which I watch with perpetual vision and which thirsts for sweet desire may be better fulfilled,

may your voice, sure, bold, and joyful, sound the will, sound the desire, to which my answer is already decreed!

I turned to Beatrice, and I heard her before I spoke, and she smiled at me with a nod that made my will grow wings.

Then I began thus: "Affection and wisdom, as soon as the first equality appeared to you, became of the same weight for each of you,

because the sun that illuminated and burned you, with heat and light, is so equal that all similarities are scant.

But in mortals, desire and reason, for the reason manifest to you, are differently feathered in wings;

wherefore I, who am mortal, feel this inequality, and therefore I give thanks only with my heart for the paternal celebration.

I truly beseech you, living topaz, to enliven this precious joy, that you may make me satiated with your name."

"O my leaf, in which I delighted while still waiting, I was your root": this was my beginning, answering.

Then he said to me: "He from whom your kinship is called, and who for a hundred years and more has circled the mountain to the first ridge,

was my son and your great-grandfather: it is fitting that you shorten their long toil with your works.

Florence within the ancient circle, from which she still takes the tercet and the ninth, lived in peace, sober and modest.

She had no chain, no crown, no gathered skirts, no belt that was visible beyond her person.

At birth, the daughter did not yet cause fear to her father, for time and dowry did not flee from measure here and there.

She had no empty family homes; Sardanapalus had not yet arrived to show what can be done in a room.

Montemalo was not yet surpassed by your Uccellatoio, which, as it is surpassed in the ascent, so it will be in the descent.

I saw Bellincion Berti go girded with leather and bone, and his lady come from the mirror without a painted face;

and I saw the Nerli and the del Vecchio content with their skin uncovered, and their women with their spindle and plume.

Oh fortunate ones! each was certain of her burial, and as yet nothing was deserted in France in her bed.

One was watching over the cradle, and, consoling, used the language that first amuses fathers and mothers;

the other, pulling her hair from her distaff, was telling stories to her family of the Trojans, of Fiesole, and of Rome.

A Cianghella, a Lapo Salterello, would then have been considered as marvelous as Cincinnatus and Corniglia would be now.

To such a peaceful, such a beautiful life of citizens, to such a faithful citizenship, to such a sweet hostelry,

Maria gave me, called with loud cries; and in your ancient Baptistery I was together a Christian and Cacciaguida.

Moronto was my brother and Eliseo; my lady came to me from the Pado Valley, and from there your nickname came.

Then I followed Emperor Currado; and he encircled me with his soldiers, so much did I deserve for good deeds.

Following him I went to meet the iniquity of that law whose people usurp, through the fault of the shepherds, your justice.

There I was liberated from that foul people by the deceitful world, whose love defiles many souls;

and I came from martyrdom to this peace."

Paradiso · Canto XVI

O little nobility of our blood, if you make people glory in you down here where our affection languishes,

it will never be a wonderful thing to me: for there where desire is not twisted, I mean in heaven, I gloried in it.

You are indeed a cloak that quickly shortens: so that, if it is not added from day to day, time goes by with its forces.

From the 'you' that first offered itself in Rome, in which its family least perseveres, my words began again;

whereupon Beatrice, who was a little free, laughing, seemed like the one who coughed at the first written fault of Ginevra.

I began: "You are my father; you give me all the boldness to speak; you lift me up so that I am more than I.

Through so many streams my mind is filled with joy, which makes itself happy because it can sustain itself without breaking.

Tell me then, my dear firstborn, who were your ancestors and what were the years that were marked in your childhood;

tell me how large the sheepfold of San Giovanni was then, and who were the people there worthy of the highest seats.

As a coal comes to life in flame at the blowing of the winds, so I saw that light shine at my blandishments;

and as it grew more beautiful in my eyes, so with a sweeter and gentler voice, but not with this modern speech,

it said to me: "Since that day when 'Ave' was said at the birth when my mother, who is now a saint, was relieved of me who was heavy,

this fire has come to his Leo five hundred and fifty-three times to rekindle beneath his soles.

My ancestors and I were born in the place where once stood the last sixth of that which your annual game runs.

Let it be enough to hear this of my ancestors: who they were and where they came here, it is more fitting to keep silent than to speak honestly.

All those who at that time were there capable of bearing arms, between Mars and the Baptist, were a fifth of those now alive.

But the citizenry, now mixed with Campi, Certaldo, and Fegghine, is seen pure in the last artist.

Oh, how much better it would be to be near those people I speak of, and to have your border at Galluzzo and Trespiano,

than to have them inside and endure the stench of the peasant of Aguglione, of that man from Signa, who already has his eye sharpened for barter!

If the most depraved people in the world had not been Caesar's neighbors, but kind as a mother to her son,

such is the Florentine deed, both in change and trade, that he would have turned to Simifonti, where his grandfather went in search of him;

Montemurlo would still be the Conti's; The Cerchi would be in the Acone parish, and perhaps the Buondelmonti in Valdigrieve.

The confusion of people has always been the source of the city's ills, just as the food you put aside is the source of yours;

and a blind bull falls quicker than a blind lamb; and often one sword cuts more and better than five.

If you look at Luni and Orbisaglia as they have gone, and how Chiusi and Sinigaglia are following them,

hearing how the clans are disintegrating will not seem new or shocking to you, since cities have an end.

All your affairs have their death, just as you do; but it is hidden in some that lasts a long time, and lives are short.

And as the moon's turning of the sky covers and uncovers the shores without pause, so does Fortune with Florence:

Therefore what I will say of the noble Florentines, whose fame is hidden in time, should not seem a wondrous thing.

I saw the Ughi, and I saw the Catellini, Filippi, Greci, Ormanni, and Alberichi, already in decline, illustrious citizens;

and I saw those as great as ancient, with him of la Sannella, him of l'Arca, and Soldanieri, Ardinghi, and Bostichi.

Above the gate that is now burdened with a new crime of such weight that it will soon be a disaster for the ship,

were the Ravignani, from which Count Guido disembarked, and whoever has since taken the name of the noble Bellincione.

The man from La Pressa already knew how to rule, and Galigaio had already gilded the hilt and pommel in his house.

The column of Vaio was already great, Sacchetti, Giuochi, Fifanti, Barucci, Galli, and those who blush for the bushel.

The lineage from which the Calfucci sprang was already large, and already the Sizii and Arrigucci were drawn to the curule.

Oh, what I saw of those who are undone by their pride! And the balls of gold flourished Florence in all its great deeds.

So did the fathers of those who, whenever your church is vacant, grow fat by staying in the consistory.

The haughty race that pursues those who flee, and those who show their teeth or purses, like a lamb, is appeased,

already came up, but of small people; so much so that Ubertin Donato was not pleased, who later was made their relative by his father-in-law.

Caponsacco had already descended from Fiesole into the market, and already Giuda and Infangato were good citizens.

I will tell you something incredible and true: the small circle was entered through a gate named after those of La Pera.

Everyone who bears the beautiful emblem of the great baron whose name and honor the feast of Thomas cheers,

from him received military service and privilege; although today he who drapes it with the insignia gathers with the people.

There were already Gualterotti and Importuni; And Borgo would be even quieter, if new neighbors were fasting.

The house from which your mourning arose, because of the just disdain that killed you and put an end to your happy life,

was honored, it and its companions: O Buondelmonte, how badly you avoided her wedding for the comforts of others!

Many would be happy, who are sad, if God had granted you to Ema the first time you came to the city.

But it was fitting for that bare stone that guards the bridge that Florence made a victim in her final peace.

With these people, and with others with them, I saw Florence in such repose that she had no reason to weep.

With these people I saw their people so glorious and just, that the lily was never placed backward on a spear,

nor made vermilion by division."

Paradiso · Canto XVII

As he who still makes fathers scanty for their sons came to Clymenè to ascertain what he had heard before him;

such was I, and such was I perceived both by Beatrice and by the holy lamp that had previously changed its position for me.

Therefore, my lady, "Send forth the flame of your desire," she said to me, "so that it may emerge clearly marked from the inner stamp:

not that our knowledge may increase through your speech, but that you may accustom yourself to express your thirst, so that man may mix with you."

"O dear plant of mine, who so inspire you, that, as earthly minds see that two obtuse points cannot fit into a triangle,

so see contingent things before they exist in themselves, gazing at the point to which all times are present;

While I was joined to Virgil on the mountain that heals souls and descending into the dead world,

he spoke to me weighty words about my future life, although I feel quite impervious to the blows of fortune;

so that my desire would be content to understand what fortune is approaching me: for a foreseen arrow comes more slowly."

Thus I spoke to that same light that had first spoken to me; and as Beatrice willed, my desire was confessed.

Nor through the confusion in which the mad people were already entangled before the Lamb of God who took away their sins was slain,

but in clear words and precise Latin that paternal love, hidden and apparent in its own smile, responded:

"The contingency, which extends not beyond the notebook of your matter, is all painted in the eternal sight;

necessity, however, takes hold of you only as from the face in which a ship is mirrored as it descends in a torrent.

From then on, just as sweet harmony from an organ reaches my ear, so the time that is preparing for you comes to me.

As Hippolytus left Athens through the merciless and perfidious story, so must you leave Florence.

This is desired and this is already sought, and it will soon be done for whoever thinks of it there where Christ is traded daily.

Guilt will follow the offended party in a cry, as it usually does; but vengeance will bear witness to the truth that dispenses it.

You will abandon everything you cherish most; and this is the arrow that the bow of exile shoots first.

You will experience how salty another's bread tastes, and how hard the path is to ascend and descend another's stairs.

And what will weigh most heavily on your shoulders will be the wicked and foolish company with which you will fall into this valley;

which will turn against you, all ungrateful, all mad and impious; but, shortly thereafter, it, not you, will have its temples reddened by it.

His bestiality will be proved by his trial; so it will be good for you to have made yourself a part of it.

Your first refuge and your first shelter will be the courtesy of the great Lombard who carries the holy bird up the ladder;

who will have such benign regard for you that, between the two of you, what is slowest among others will come first in asking and doing.

With him you will see him who, at his birth, was so impressed by this strong star that his deeds will be notable.

People are not yet aware of this because of his young age, for only nine years have these wheels revolved around him;

but before the Gascon deceives the lofty Henry, sparks of his virtue will appear in caring neither for silver nor for cares.

His magnificence will still be known, so that his enemies will not be able to keep their tongues silent.

Await him and his benefits; Many people will be transformed through him, changing the conditions of the rich and the beggars;

and you will carry it written in his mind, and you will not tell it"; and he said things incredible to those who were present.

Then he added: "Son, these are the glosses of what was told you; behold the snares that are hidden behind a few circles.

But I do not want you to envy your neighbors, since your future life will be far beyond the punishment of their perfidiousness."

After the holy soul, silently, showed herself ready to weave the woof into the web I had handed her,

I began, like one who, in doubt, longs for advice from one who sees, wills rightly, and loves:

"I see clearly, my father, how time spurs me on, to deal me a blow that is heaviest to those who most abandon themselves;

wherefore it is good that I arm myself with foresight, so that, if a place dearer to me is taken from me, I may not lose the others for my songs.

Down through the endlessly bitter world, and through the mountain from whose beautiful summit my lady's eyes rose,

and then through the heavens, from light to light, I have learned what, if I repeat it, will taste like strong citrus to many;

and if I am a timid friend of truth, I fear losing my life among those who will call this time ancient."

The light in which my treasure, whom I found there, smiled first glittered, like a golden mirror in a ray of sunlight;

then it replied: "A dark conscience, either from its own shame or from another's, will surely feel your harsh words.

But nevertheless, having removed every lie, make your entire vision manifest; and let it scratch where the itch is.

For if your voice is unpleasant at first, it will leave vital nourishment afterward, once it has digested.

This cry of yours will be like the wind that strikes the highest peaks most; and this is no small reason for honor.

But in these wheels, on the mountain and in the dolorous valley, only the souls known by fame are shown to you,

that the soul of him who hears does not rest, nor does it hold firm faith for an example whose root is unknown and hidden,

nor for any argument that does not appear.

Paradiso · Canto XVIII

That blessed mirror already enjoyed only its word, and I savored mine, tempering the bitter with sweetness;

and that lady who led me to God said: "Change your thoughts; consider that I am near him who unburdens every wrong."

I turned to the loving sound of my comfort; and what I then saw love in those holy eyes, I abandon here:

not because I distrust my own speech, but because my mind cannot reflect so much upon itself unless another guides it.

So much can I say of that moment, that, gazing at her, my affection was freed from all other desire,

until the eternal pleasure, which directly shone upon Beatrice, from her beautiful face contented me with the second look.

Overcoming me with the light of a smile, she said to me: "Turn and listen; for Paradise is not only in my eyes."

Just as affection is sometimes seen here in the sight, if it is so strong that the whole soul is taken from it,

so in the blaze of the holy lightning, to which I turned, I recognized in it the desire to speak to me still for a while.

He began: "On this fifth threshold of the tree that lives from the top and always bears fruit and never loses a leaf,

blessed are the spirits who, before they reached heaven, gave forth a loud voice, so that every muse would be filled with them.

Therefore look at the horns of the cross: he whom I will name will there perform the act that his swift fire makes in a cloud."

I saw a light drawn from the cross by the name of Joshua, as he did; nor was the word known to me until the deed.

And at the name of the lofty Macabeus I saw another move, whirling, and joy was the whip of the pale.

Thus through Charlemagne and through Roland my attentive gaze followed two of them, as an eye follows its falcon in flight.

Then my sight was drawn by that cross to William, Richard, Duke Gottfried, and Robert Guiscard.

Then, among the other lights, stirring and mixed, the soul that had spoken to me showed itself to be an artist among the singers of heaven.

I turned to my right side to see in Beatrice my duty, whether in speech or in action, marked;

and I saw her eyes so pure, so joyful, that her appearance surpassed the others and the last solemnity.

And as, by feeling greater delight in doing good, man realizes day by day that his virtue advances,

so I realized that my circling of the sky had increased its arc together, seeing that miracle more adorned.

And as it is to be transformed, in a brief space of time, into a white lady, when her face is freed from the burden of shame,
