such was it in my eyes, when I was turned, by the candor of the tempered sixth star, which had gathered me within itself.

I saw in that jovial torch the sparkle of love that was there, marking our speech in my eyes.

And as birds rising from the river, as if congratulating their pastures, make of themselves now round, now another flock,

so within the lights holy creatures, fluttering, sang, and made now D, now I, now L in their figures.

First, singing, they moved to its note; then, becoming one of these signs, they stopped a little and fell silent.

O divine Pegasus, who makes geniuses glorious and makes them long-lived, and with you cities and kingdoms,

illumine me with yourself, so that I may reveal their figures as I have conceived them: may your power appear in these brief verses!

So let seven vowels and consonants be shown five times; and I noted the parts as they seemed to me to be said.

"DILIGITE JUSTITIAM" was first the verb and noun of the entire painting; "QUI JUDICATIS TERRAM" was then separated.

Then they remained arranged in the m of the fifth word, so that Jupiter seemed silver there distinguished by gold.

And I saw other lights descend where the top of the M was, and there they rest, singing, I believe, the good that moves them.

Then, as innumerable sparks arise from the striking of burning logs, by which fools are wont to seek hope,

thereafter more than a thousand lights seemed to rise and rise, some more, some less, as the sun that lights them allotted them;

and each, calmed in its place, I saw the head and neck of an eagle represented by that distinct fire.

He who paints there has no one to guide him; but he guides, and from him is remembered that virtue which is form for the nests.

The other bliss, which seemed content before being attached to the M, followed the imprint with little movement.

O sweet star, how many gems have shown me that our justice is an effect of the heaven you bejewel!

Therefore I pray the mind in which your motion and your virtue begin, to look where the smoke that vitiates your ray comes from;

so that once again it may be angry at buying and selling within the temple that was walled with signs and martyrs.

O militia of heaven, whom I contemplate, adore for those who are on earth, all led astray by the evil example!

Once it was customary to wage war with swords; but now it is done by taking, now here, now there, the bread that the pious Father keeps from no one.

But you who write only to erase, consider that Peter and Paul, who died for the vineyard you ruin, are still alive.

Well can you say: "I have so firm a desire for him who wanted to live alone and who was drawn by leaps to martyrdom,

that I know neither the fisherman nor Polo."

Paradiso · Canto XIX

The beautiful image that made the entwined souls joyful in sweet fruition appeared before me with outstretched wings;

each faucet seemed to have a ray of sunlight burning so brightly that it refracted it into my eyes.

And what I must now portray has never been spoken, nor written down, nor has it ever been grasped by imagination;

for I saw and even heard the beak speak, and the voice sound both "I" and "mine," when both "we" and "our" were in the concept.

And he began: "Because I am just and pious, I am here exalted to that glory which cannot be overcome by desire;

and on earth I left my memory so formed that the wicked people there praise it, but do not follow the story.

Thus a single heat from many embers is felt, as from many loves only a single sound came from that image.

Whereupon I said: "O perpetual flowers of eternal joy, who make all your fragrances seem to me to be but one,

breathe, dissolve for me the great fast that has kept me hungry for so long, finding no food on earth.

I know well that, if divine justice makes another realm its mirror in heaven, it does not see yours with a veil.

You know how attentively I prepare myself to listen; you know what is the doubt that has kept me fasting for so long."

Like a falcon emerging from its cap, it moves its head and applauds with its wings, showing off its will and making itself beautiful,

I saw that sign, which was interwoven with praise of divine grace, appear, with songs such as those who rejoice above know.

Then it began: "He who turned the sixth to the edge of the world, and within it discerned so much that was hidden and manifest,

could not make his power so impressed upon the entire universe that his word did not remain in infinite excess.

And this makes it certain that the first proud one, who was the summit of all creation, through not waiting for light, fell immature;

and from this it appears that every lesser nature is a meager receptacle for that good which has no end and measures itself within itself.

Therefore your vision, which must be one of the rays of the mind with which all things are filled,

cannot by its nature be so powerful as to discern its origin far beyond what appears to it.

Therefore, the vision that your world receives, like an eye through the sea, penetrates eternal justice;

for although from the shore it sees the bottom, it does not see it in the open sea; and yet it is there, but it conceals the depths.

There is no light unless it comes from the serene sky that is never disturbed; rather, it is darkness or the shadow of the flesh or its poison.

The lair that hid living justice has long been opened to you, and why you questioned so much;

for you said: "A man is born on the banks of the Indus, and there is no one there who speaks of Christ, no one who reads, no one who writes;

and all his good wills and deeds are, as far as human reason can see, without sin in life or in sermons.

He dies unbaptized and without faith: where is this justice that condemns him? Where is his guilt, if he does not believe?"

Now who are you, who wishes to sit on a throne, to judge from a thousand miles away with the shortsightedness of a span?

Certainly, to him who grows thin with me, if the Scripture were not above you, there would be wonder to be in doubt.

Oh earthly animals! Oh coarse minds! The first will, which is good in itself, which is the supreme good, has never moved.

So much is just as it is suited to it: no good created thing draws it to itself, but it, by radiating, causes it.

As the stork turns over the nest after it has fed its young, and gazes at it like one who has been fed;

such became the blessed image, which moved its wings, driven by so many counsels, and raised its brows.

Whipping, it sang, and said: "As my notes are to you, who do not understand them, such is the eternal judgment to you mortals."

Then those bright fires of the Holy Spirit were stilled, even in the sign that the Romans made reverend to the world.

He began again: "No one who did not believe in Christ ever ascended to this kingdom, neither before nor after he was nailed to the cross.

But see: many cry 'Christ, Christ!' who will be far less inclined to judge him than those who do not know Christ;

and such Christians will the Ethiopian damn when the two colleges separate, one eternally rich and the other hopeless.

What can the Persians say to your kings? When will they see that open volume in which all his disparagements are written?

There will be seen, among Albert's works, the one that will soon set the pen to work, so that the kingdom of Prague will be deserted.

There will be seen the grief that, by counterfeiting the coin, he who will die from the blow of his skin upon the Seine will be induced.

There will be seen the thirsty pride that drives the Scots and the English mad, so that they cannot bear to reach their goal.

There will be seen the lust and the soft living of the Spanish and Bohemian, who never knew or wanted valor.

There will be seen the goodness of Giotto of Jerusalem marked with an i, when the opposite would mark an m.

There will be seen the avarice and cowardice of him who guards the island of fire, where Anchises ended his long age;

and to make clear how little he is, his writing will be truncated letters, which will make much sense in a small place.

And to everyone the filthy deeds of the beard and the brother, who have stamped such a noble nation and two crowns, will seem.

And those of Portugal and Norway will be recognized there, and those of Rascia who have seen the Venetian coin badly.

Oh blessed Hungary, if she no longer lets herself be mistreated! and blessed Navarre, if she were to arm herself with the mountain that surrounds her!

And everyone must believe that, as a pledge of this, Nicosia and Famagusta already lament and quarrel for their beast,

who does not depart from the side of the others.

Paradiso · Canto XX

When he who lights up the whole world from our hemisphere descends so that the day is consumed on every side,

the sky, which is first lit by him alone, suddenly regains its brightness through many lights, in which one shines;

And this act of heaven came to my mind, as the sign of the world and its leaders in the blessed beak was silent;

because all those living lights, shining ever brighter, began to sing songs, faint and fleeting from my memory.

O sweet love, who cloaks yourself in laughter, how ardent you seemed in those flares, which had breathed only holy thoughts!

After the dear and lucid lapilli, with which I saw the sixth light bejeweled, silenced the angelic blasts,

I seemed to hear the murmur of a river flowing clearly down from stone to stone, revealing the richness of its summit.

And just as the sound of the lyre takes shape around its neck, and just as the wind that penetrates the hole of the pipe,

so, having removed the need for delay, the murmur of the eagle rose up its neck as if it were a lie.

A voice was made there, and from there it issued from its beak in the form of words, such as the heart awaited where I wrote them.

"The part of me that sees and suffers the sun in the mortal eagles," I began, "must now be looked at steadily,

because of the fires by which I form myself, those that make the eye in my head sparkle, are the highest of all their degrees.

He who shines in the midst as the pupil was the singer of the Holy Spirit, who translated the ark from village to village:

now he knows the merit of his song, insofar as it was the effect of his counsel, for the reward is equal.

Of the five that circle my brow, the one closest to my goat consoled the widow for her son:

Now he knows how dearly it costs not to follow Christ, through the experience of this sweet life and of the opposite one.

And he who follows in the circumference of which I speak, through the supernal arch, delayed death through true penance:

Now he knows that eternal judgment is not changed, when a worthy prayer is offered down there for today.

The other who follows, with the laws and with me, under good intentions that bore bad fruit, became a Greek to yield to the shepherd:

Now he knows that evil deduced from his good deeds is not harmful to him, even if the world is destroyed there.

And he whom you see in the sloping arch was William, whom that land mourns that mourns Charles and Frederick alive:

Now he knows how heaven falls in love with the just king, and by the face of his splendor makes him still visible.

Who would believe down in the wandering world that Ripheus of Troy in this circle was the fifth of the holy lights?

Now he knows much of what the world cannot see of divine grace, although his sight cannot discern the depths.

Like a lark that first wanders through the air singing, and then falls silent, content with the ultimate sweetness that satiates it,

such seemed to me the image of the imprint of eternal pleasure, by whose desire each thing becomes what it is.

And although I was there, in my doubt, like glass against the color that dresses him, I had no time to wait in silence,

but from his mouth, "What things are these?" he pressed me with the force of his weight; whereupon I saw great feasts of sparkle.

Then, with eyes more alight, the blessed sign answered me, so as not to keep me in suspense:

"I see that you believe these things because I say them, but you do not see how; so that, if they are believed, they are hidden.

You act like one who understands the thing well by name, but cannot see its quiescence unless another promises it.

The kingdom of heaven suffers violence from ardent love and living hope, which conquers the divine will:

not as man overcomes man, but conquers it because it wants to be conquered, and, conquered, conquers with its benevolence.

The first life of the eyelid and the fifth makes you marvel, because you see the region of the angels depicted.

From their bodies, not Gentiles, as you believe, emerge, but Christians, in firm faith, that of the walkers and that of the footsteps.

For one from hell, where one never returns to good will, returned to the bones; and this was the reward of living hope:

of living hope, which placed power in the prayers made to God to raise her, so that her will might be moved.

The glorious soul of which we speak, having returned to the flesh, where it had been but a short time, believed in Him who could help it;

and believing, it was inflamed with such a fire of true love that in the second death it was worthy to come to this game.

The other, by grace that trickles from a fountain so deep that no creature ever peered to the first wave,

directed all its love down there; whereby, from grace to grace, God opened its eyes to our future redemption.

Therefore he believed in it, and from then on no longer tolerated the stench of paganism; and he rebukes the perverse people for it.

Those three women were for his baptism, whom you saw on the right wheel, more than a thousand years before baptizing.

O predestination, how remote is your root from those aspects that do not see the whole of the first cause!

And you, mortals, hold fast to judgment: for we, who see God, do not yet know all the elect;

and it is sweet to be so deprived of it, because our good is refined in this good, that what God wills, and what we will.

Thus from that divine image, to clarify my short sight, was given to me sweet medicine.

And as a good singer makes a good harpist follow the flick of the string, by which the song gains greater pleasure,

so, while he spoke, he reminds me that I saw the two blessed lights, just as the blinking of eyes harmonizes,

moving the flames with the words.

Paradiso · Canto XXI

My eyes were already fixed on my lady's face, and my mind with them, and I had withdrawn from all other intents.

And she did not smile; but "If I were to laugh," she began to me, "you would become like Semele when she turned to ashes:

for my beauty, which, as you have seen, glows more brightly the higher one ascends along the stairs of the eternal palace,

if it were not tempered, shines so brightly that your mortal power, in its splendor, would be a leaf that falls to a throne.

We have risen to the seventh splendor, which now shines beneath the breast of the burning Lion, mingled with his power below.

Fix your mind behind your eyes, and make of those mirrors the figure that will appear to you in this mirror."

Whoever knew what was the pasture of my face in that blissful aspect when I was transferred to another care,

would know how grateful it was for me to obey my celestial escort, balancing one side with the other.

Within the crystal that the name carries, encircling the world, of its dear leader under whom all malice lay dead,

golden in color, from which a ray shines, I saw a ladder erected so high that my light could not follow it.

I also saw such splendor descending down the steps that I thought every light that appears in the sky was diffused from there.

And just as, by natural custom, the poles, at the beginning of the day, move together to warm their cold plumage;

then some go away without returning, others turn back from whence they started, and others, circling, make their home;

It seemed to me that there was such a thing there in that flash that came together, as soon as it struck a certain point.

And what was closest to us became so clear that I said, thinking: "I clearly see the love you indicate to me.

But she, for whom I await the how and when of speaking and of keeping silent, remains; for which I, against my desire, do well not to ask."

Therefore she, who saw my silence in the sight of him who sees all, said to me: "Resolve your burning desire."

And I began: "My reward does not make me worthy of your answer; but by her who grants me the asking,

blessed life, who remain hidden within your joy, make known to me the reason that has brought you so close to me;

and tell me why the sweet symphony of paradise is silent on this wheel, which sounds so devoutly below.

"You have mortal hearing as your sight," he replied to me; "so here there is no singing because Beatrice has not laughed.

Down the steps of the holy staircase I descended only to celebrate you with words and with the light that envelops me;

nor did love make me more eager, for more and more love burns up here, as the flame shows you.

But the high charity, which makes us ready servants to the council that governs the world, casts lots here as you observe."

"I see well," I said, "sacred lamp, how free love in this court suffices to follow eternal providence;

But this is what seems difficult to discern, because you were predestined alone among your consorts for this office."

Nor did I come to the last word before the light made its center in its midst, whirling like a swift millstone;

then the love within it responded: "Divine light shines upon me, penetrating through this in which I invent myself,

whose virtue, joined with my sight, lifts me so high above myself that I see the supreme essence from which it is milked.

Hence comes the joy from which I blaze; because to my sight, as far as it is clear, I match the brightness of the flame.

But that soul in heaven which is most enlightened, that seraph whose eye is most fixed on God, does not satisfy your question,

because what you ask penetrates so deeply into the abyss of the eternal statute that it is separated from all created sight.

And to the mortal world, when you return, report this, so that it may no longer presume to move its feet to such a point.

The mind, which shines here, smokes on earth; hence consider how it can do down there what it could not because heaven assumes it.

His words so prescribed to me that I abandoned the question and withdrew to humbly ask who he was.

"Between two shores of Italy, rocks rise, and not far from your homeland, so that the thrones sound much lower,

and they form a hump called Catria, beneath which is consecrated a hermitage, usually dedicated to worship alone."

Thus I began the third sermon; and then, continuing, he said: "Here in the service of God he made me so firm,

that even with food of olive liquor I easily passed through heat and cold, content in contemplative thoughts.

That cloister used to yield fruitful service to these heavens; and now it has become empty, so that it must soon be revealed.

In that place I was Peter Damian, and Peter the Sinner was in the house of Our Lady on the shore of Hadrian.

Little mortal life remained to me when I was called and drawn to that cap, which always changes from bad to worse.

Cephas came, and the great vessel of the Holy Spirit came, lean and barefoot, taking food from every inn.

Now they want here and there someone to support the modern shepherds and someone to lead them, so heavy are they, and someone to lift them from behind.

They cover their palfreys with their cloaks, so that two beasts go under one skin: oh patience, that endures so much!

At this voice I saw more flames descend step by step and turn, and each turn made them more beautiful.

Around it they came and stopped, and gave a cry of such a loud sound that it could not be matched here;

nor did I hear it, so the thunder overcame me.

Paradiso · Canto XXII

Overwhelmed with amazement, I turned to my guide, like a child who always runs to where he most trusts;

and he, like a mother who quickly helps her pale and longing son with her voice, which usually disposes him well,

said to me: "Do you not know that you are in heaven? And do you not know that heaven is all holy, and what is done there comes from good zeal?

How the song would have transformed you, and I, laughing, can you now imagine, since the cry has moved you so;

in which, if you had understood his prayers, you would already know the vengeance you will see before you die.

The sword up here cuts neither quickly nor slowly, but at the will of him who awaits it, longing or fearing.

But now turn your attention to others; for you will see many illustrious spirits, if, as I say, you restore your gaze."

As it pleased her, I returned my eyes, and saw a hundred spherules that together were becoming more beautiful with mutual rays.

I stood like one who represses the edge of desire within himself, and does not dare to ask, so much is he afraid of too much;

and I moved the largest and most luminous of those daisies forward, to make my desire content with itself.

Then I heard within her: "If you could see how I feel the charity that burns between us, your thoughts would be expressed.

But so that, by waiting, you do not delay towards the high goal, I will give you an answer to the thought that so regards you.

That mountain on whose slope Cassino stands was once frequented on its summit by deceived and ill-disposed people;

and I am he who first bore there the name of him who brought to earth the truth that so exalts us;

and such grace shone upon me that I withdrew the surrounding villages from the wicked culture that seduced the world.

These other fires were all contemplating men, lit by that heat that makes flowers and holy fruits grow.

Here is Maccario, here is Romoaldo, here are my friars who within the cloisters rested their feet and held their hearts steadfast.

And I to him: "The affection you show me in speaking, and the good looks I see and notice in all your ardors,

have so expanded my trust in me, as the sun does the rose when it opens to the extent of its power.

Therefore I beg you, and you, father, assure me if I can obtain such grace that I may see you with an uncovered image."

To which he: "Brother, your high desire will be fulfilled on the final sphere, where all the others and mine are fulfilled.

There every longing is perfect, mature, and whole; in that alone is every part where it always was,

because it is not in place and does not become crowded; and our stairway reaches up to it, where it thus steals from your sight.

Up there the patriarch Jacob saw it offer the highest portion, when it appeared to him so laden with angels.

But, to ascend it, no one now lifts his feet from the ground, and my rule remains to the detriment of the papers.

The walls that used to be built as abbeys are caves, and the cowls are sacks full of rotten flour.

But no usury is taken so grievously against the pleasure of God as that fruit which makes the hearts of monks so foolish;

for whatever the Church looks upon, it all belongs to the people who ask for God; not to parents or anything worse.

The flesh of mortals is so soft that a good beginning is not enough, from the sprouting of the oak to the ripening of the acorn.

Peter began without gold or silver, and I with prayer and fasting, and Francis humbly began his convent;

and if you look at the beginning of each, then look back to where it has gone, you will see the white turned brown.

Truly Jordan turned further back, and the sea fled, when God willed, more wonderful to see than help here.

Thus he spoke to me, and then he returned to his college, and the college gathered together; then, like a whirlwind, all swirled upward.

The sweet lady, following them, urged me with a single nod up that ladder, so her power conquered my nature;

nor ever down here, where one ascends and descends naturally, was there such a swift motion that could equal my wing.

If I ever return, reader, to that devout triumph for which I often weep for my sins and beat my breast,

you would not have drawn and placed your finger in the fire when I saw the sign that follows Taurus and was within it.

O glorious stars, O light pregnant with great virtue, from which I recognize all my genius, whatever it may be,

with you was born and hidden within you he who is the father of all mortal life, when I first felt the Tuscan air;

and then, when I was granted grace to enter the high wheel that turns you, your region was allotted to me.

Now my soul devoutly sighs for you, to acquire virtue for the strong step that draws it toward itself.

"You are so close to ultimate salvation," Beatrice began, "that you must have your eyes clear and sharp;

and therefore, before you enter it further, look down and see how much world I have already made beneath your feet;

so that your heart, as much as it can, may joyfully present itself to the triumphant crowd that joyfully comes through this circular ethereal world.

I returned my gaze through all the seven spheres, and I saw this globe such that I smiled at its vile appearance;

and I approve of that counsel as better than that which is less; and whoever thinks of anything else can be called truly upright.

I saw the daughter of Leto incense without that shadow that was the reason I once believed her rare and dense.

The sight of your son, Hyperion, I endured there, and I saw how Maia and Dione move around and near him.

Then appeared to me the tempering of Jove between the father and the son; and then it became clear to me the variation they make where;

and all seven showed me how great they are, how swift they are, and how far away they are.

The flowerbed that makes us so ferocious, turning with the eternal Twins, appeared to me, from the hills to the mouths;

then I turned my eyes to their beautiful eyes.

Paradiso · Canto XXIII

Like the bird, among the beloved leaves, perched on the nest of its sweet young during the night that hides things from us,

that, to see the longed-for faces and to find the food to feed them, in which heavy labors are pleasing to it,

anticipates the time in an open foliage, and with ardent affection awaits the sun, intently watching only for the dawn to break;

Thus my lady stood erect and attentive, turned toward the region beneath which the sun shows less haste:

so that, seeing her suspended and wandering, I became like one who, longing for something else, desires it, and is satisfied by hope.

But little time passed between one and the other when, of my waiting, I speak, and of seeing the sky grow brighter and brighter;

and Beatrice said: "Behold the ranks of Christ's triumph and all the fruit gathered from the revolving of these spheres!"

It seemed to me that her face was all ablaze, and her eyes were so full of joy that I must pass by without purpose.

As Trivia laughs in the serene full moons among the eternal nymphs who paint the sky throughout its gulfs,

I saw above thousands of lamps a single sun that lit them all, as ours does our visions above;

and through the living light the shining substance shone so clearly in my face that I could not bear it.

Oh Beatrice, sweet and dear guide! She said to me: "What overwhelms you is virtue from which nothing can be repaired.

Here is the wisdom and the power that opened the paths between heaven and earth, for which there was once such long longing."

As fire breaks free from a cloud to expand so that it cannot contain, and outside its nature falls to the ground,

my mind, thus, among those bees, grew larger, emerged from itself, and knows not what to remember.

"Open your eyes and see what I am; you have seen things that have made you powerful enough to sustain my laughter."

I was like one who feels the lingering of a forgotten vision and who tries in vain to bring it back to mind,

when I heard this proposition, worthy of so much gratitude that it is never lost from the book that reviews the past.

If now all those languages ​​were sounded that Polyhymnia and her sisters made richer with their sweetest milk,

to help me, it would not come close to the thousandth of the truth, singing of the holy smile and how much the holy aspect made mere;

and so, picturing Paradise, one must skip the sacred poem, like one who finds his path cut off.

But whoever ponders the weighty theme and the mortal shoulder that burdens it would not blame him if he trembles beneath it:

It is no match for a small boat that the bold prow cleaves, nor for a pilot who is careful to himself.

"Why does my face so enamore you that you do not turn to the beautiful garden that blooms under the rays of Christ?

There is the rose in which the divine Word became flesh; there are the lilies whose fragrance took the good path."

So Beatrice; and I, who was entirely ready for her counsels, again surrendered to the battle of the feeble eyelids.

As to a ray of sunshine, which pure shines through a broken cloud, my eyes once saw a meadow of flowers, covered in shadow;

I saw thus greater crowds of splendors, struck from above by burning rays, without seeing the beginning of lightning.

O benign virtue that so imprints them, you exalted yourself above, to grant me room for eyes that were not powerful enough for you.

The name of the beautiful flower that I always invoke, morning and evening, constrained my soul entirely to perceive the greater fire;

and as both lights depicted to me the which and the magnitude of the living star that conquers up there as it conquers down here,

a torch descended into the sky, formed in a circle like a crown, and encircled her and revolved around her.

Whatever sweeter melody sounds down here and draws the soul closer, would seem like a cloud that, when torn, thunders,

compared to the sound of that lyre that crowned the beautiful sapphire with which the clearest sky is sapphireed.

"I am angelic love, who revolves the high joy that breathes from the womb that was the home of our desire;

and I will revolve, lady of heaven, while you follow your son, and make the supreme sphere more radiant because he enters there."

Thus the circling melody was sealed, and all the other lights made the name of Mary resound.

The royal mantle of all the volumes of the world, which most fervently and most enlivens in the breath of God and in customs,

had its inner shore so distant above us that its appearance, where I was, was not yet apparent:

therefore my eyes were not able to follow the crowned flame that rose near its seed.

And like a little child who stretches his arms toward his mother, after having taken the milk, because of the soul that is inflamed even from without;

each of those whitenesses stretched upward with its summit, so that the high affection they had for Mary was evident to me.

Then they remained there in my presence, "Queen, hide yourself!" singing so sweetly that the delight never left me.

Oh, how much abundance is suffocated in those rich coffers that were once sowing good things down here!

Here one lives and enjoys the treasure that was acquired by weeping in exile in Babylon, where the gold was left behind.

Here, under the high Son of God and Mary, triumphs in his victory, and with the ancient and the new council,

he who holds the keys to such glory.

Paradiso · Canto XXIV

"O fellowship chosen for the great supper of the blessed Lamb, who feeds you so that your desire is always satisfied,

if by the grace of God he delights in what falls from your table, before death prescribes time,

consider his immense affection and pour it out a little: you always drink from the fountain from which comes what he thinks."

Thus Beatrice; and those joyful souls became spheres upon fixed poles, flaming, at times, like comets.

And as circles made of clockwork revolve so that the first one, to whoever pays attention, seems quiet, and the last one flying;

so those carols, dancing differently, made me appreciate her richness, swift and slow.

From the one I most fondly noted, I saw issue a fire so happy, that it left no one there of greater clarity;

and three times she circled around Beatrice with a song so divine, that my imagination cannot recall it.

Therefore my pen skips and I do not write it: for our imagination, not to mention our speech, is too bright for such folds.

"O my holy sister, who prays so devoutly to us, by your ardent love, free me from that beautiful sphere."

Then, stopped, the blessed fire directed its spirit to my lady, who spoke as I have said.

And she: "O eternal light of the great man to whom Our Lord left the keys, which he brought down, I gaze upon this joy,

try this one with light and heavy points, as you please, about the faith, for which you traveled across the sea.

If he loves well and hopes and believes well, it is not hidden from you, because your face is there where everything is seen painted;

but since this kingdom has made citizens for the true faith, to glorify it, it is right that I speak of it to him."

Just as the bachelor arms himself and does not speak until the master proposes the question, to approve it, not to conclude it,

so I armed myself with every argument while she spoke, to be ready for such a querent and such a profession.

"Tell me, good Christian, make yourself known: what is faith?" Whereupon I raised my head to that light from which this breathed;

then I turned to Beatrice, and she made ready appearances for me to pour forth the water from my inner fountain.

"May the Grace that grants me to confess," I began, "from the high first pillar, make my concepts well expressed."

And I continued: "As the true pen wrote to us, Father, of your dear friar who with you put Rome on the right track,

faith is the substance of things hoped for and the proof of things not seen; and this seems to me to be his quidity."

Then I heard: "You hear rightly, if you understand well why he placed it among the substances, and then among the arguments."

And I followed: "The profound things that grant me their appearance here are so hidden from the eyes down there,

that their being exists only in belief, upon which the high hope is founded; and therefore it takes on the meaning of substance.

And from this belief we must reason, without having another view: therefore it has the meaning of argument."

Then I heard: "If whatever is acquired below through doctrine were thus understood, there would be no place there for the intellect of a sophist."

Thus he breathed his last with that burning love; then he added: "The alloy and weight of this coin have already passed far beyond;

But tell me if you have it in your purse." To which I replied: "Yes, I have it, so bright and so round that nothing in its stamp becomes obscured."

Then he emerged from the profound light that shone there: "This dear joy on which all virtue is founded,

where did it come to you?" And I: "The broad plutonium of the Holy Spirit, which is diffused over the old and the new skins,

is a syllogism that has concluded it for me so acutely, that against it all demonstration seems obtuse to me."

Then I heard: "The old and the new proposition that thus concludes you, why do you take it for divine speech?"

And I: "The proof that reveals the truth to me are the works that have followed, for which nature never heats iron nor strikes anvil."

I was answered: "Tell me, who assures you that those works were real? The very One who wants to prove himself, not another, swears it to you."

"If the world turned to Christianity," I said, "without miracles, this one is such that the others are not a hundred:

since you entered the field, poor and hungry, to sow the good plant that was once a vine and now has become a bramble."

This finished, the high, holy court resounded through the spheres with a "Let us praise God" in the melody that is sung up there.

And that baron, who had already led me from branch to branch, examining, until we were approaching the last leaves,

began again: "Grace, who mingled with your mind, opened your mouth up to this point as it should have been opened,

so that I approve what emerged from it; but now it is necessary to express what you believe, and why it offered itself to your belief."

"O holy father, and spirit, who see what you believed so that you conquered younger feet toward the tomb,"

I began, "you want me to manifest here the form of my ready belief, and you also asked the reason for it.

And I answer: I believe in one God, alone and eternal, who moves all heaven, not motion, with love and desire;

and for this belief I have not only physical and metaphysical proof, but also the truth that rains down from here

through Moses, through the prophets and the psalms, through the Gospel, and through you who wrote later that the ardent Spirit made you souls;

and I believe in three eternal persons, and these I believe to be one essence, so one and so triune, that it suffers the union of 'I am' and 'this.'

Of the profound divine condition that I now touch, the evangelical doctrine seals my mind many times.

This is the beginning, this is the spark that then expands into a living flame, and like a star in heaven, sparkles within me.

As the lord, who hears what pleases him, embraces his servant, congratulating him for the news, as soon as he falls silent;

so, blessing me in song, the apostolic light, at whose command

I had said, "So pleased him in speaking!", encircled me three times, as I fell silent!

Paradiso · Canto XXV

If ever it seems to me that the sacred poem to which both heaven and earth have set their hands, so that for many years they have made me a beast,

may vanquish the cruelty that bars me from the beautiful sheepfold where I slept as a lamb, enemy of the wolves that wage war against it;

now with another voice, with another fleece I will return as a poet, and at the font of my baptism I will take up my cap;

Because I entered into the faith that makes souls count for God, and then Peter turned my head for it.

Then a light moved toward us from that sphere whence came forth the first fruits of his vicars that Christ left;

and my lady, filled with joy, said to me: "Look, look: behold the baron for whom Galicia is being visited down there."

Just as when a dove lands near its companion, one spreads affection to the other, circling and murmuring;

so I saw one great and glorious prince being welcomed by the other, praising the food that is being eaten up there.

But when the congratulations were over, each one silently stood with me, so enflamed that it overcame my face.

Then, laughing, Beatrice said: "Illustrious life, for which the breadth of our basilica was written,

make the hope resound in this height: you know that you imagine it as often as Jesus most caressed the three."

"Lift your head and be sure: that what comes up here from the mortal world must mature in our rays."

This second comfort of the fire came to me; whereupon I raised my eyes to the mountains that had first bent them with excessive weight.

"Since our Emperor, by his grace, wishes you to confront him, even death, in the most secret hall with his counts,

so that, having seen the truth of this court, the hope that down there so enamours, in you and in others, may strengthen it,

tell what it is, tell how your mind is adorned with it, and say where it came to you." Thus the second light followed again.

And that pious one who guided the feathers of my wings to such a lofty flight thus anticipated my answer:

"The Church Militant has no son with greater hope, as is written in the Sun that shines upon our entire flock.

Therefore, he is granted permission to come from Egypt to Jerusalem to see, rather than be required to serve in the army.

The other two points, which are asked not for knowledge, but so that he may relate how much this virtue pleases you,

I leave to him, for they will not be strong or boastful to him. Let him answer this, and may the grace of God bear it with him."

Like a student who readily and freely follows a teacher in what he knows, so that his goodness may be hidden,

"Hope," I said, "is a certain expectation of future glory, which produces divine grace and previous merit.

This light comes to me from many stars; but he distilled it in my heart first, who was the supreme singer of the supreme leader.

"Let those who know your name hope in you," he says in his theody: "and who does not know if he has my faith?

You distilled in me, with his distillation, then in my pistol; so that I am full, and I pour your rain back into others."

While I was speaking, within the living bosom of that fire a sudden and frequent flash trembled like a flash.

Then he breathed: "The love with which I still burn toward the virtue that followed me to the palm and to the exit of the field,

wants me to breathe in you who delight in her; and I am grateful that you say what hope promises you."

And I: "The new and ancient writings place the sign, and it points it out to me, of the souls that God has made friends.

Isaiah says that each one in her own land will be clothed in a double garment: and her land is this sweet life;

and your brother is far more digestible, where he speaks of the white robes, this revelation reveals to us."

And first, near the end of these words, "Hope in you" was heard above us; to which all the carols responded.

Then a light brightened between them, so that if Cancer had such a crystal, winter would be a month of a single day.

And as a joyful virgin rises and goes and enters the dance, only to honor the novice, not for any fault,

so I saw the bright splendor come to the two who were turning to the note befitting their ardent love.

There she stood in song and on the wheel; and my lady held her gaze upon them, just like a silent and motionless bride.

"This is he who lay on the breast of our pelican, and this was chosen from the cross for the great office."

My lady thus; but her gaze no longer moved her attention after his words.

As he who gazes and dares to see the sun eclipse a little, who, by seeing, becomes blind;

such I became at that final fire while it was said: "Why do you dazzle yourself to see something that has no place here?

On earth is earth, my body, and it will be so much there with the others that our number is equal to the eternal purpose.

With the two stoles in the blessed cloister are the two sole lights that ascended; and this you will bring into your world."

At this voice the inflamed circle calmed, along with the sweet mingling that was made in the sound of the triune spirit,

just as, to cease toil or risk, the oars, previously reverberating in the water, all rest at the sound of a whistle.

Oh, how I was moved in my mind when I turned to see Beatrice, for I could not see, although I was

near her, and in the happy world!

Paradiso · Canto XXVI

While I was doubting because of my dulled face, from the bright flame that extinguished it came a breath that made me attentive,

saying: "While you recover from the sight that has been consumed in me, it is well that by reasoning you compensate for it.

Begin then; and say where your soul is fixed, and reason that the sight in you is lost and not dead:

because the lady who leads you through this heavenly region has in her gaze the power that the hand of Ananias had."

I said: "As she pleases, may remedy come, soon or late, to the eyes that were outside when she entered with the fire that always burns me.

The good that makes this court content, Alpha and O is all the writing that Love reads to me, either lightly or forcefully."

That same voice that had taken away my fear of the sudden dazzlement, put me to the trouble of reasoning again;

and it said: "Certainly you must clear your sieve more narrowly: you must tell who aimed your bow at such a target."

And I: "By philosophical arguments and by the authority that comes from there, such love must impress itself upon me:

for good, insofar as good, as is understood, kindles love, and all the more the more it contains goodness within itself.

Therefore, to the essence where there is such an advantage that every good found outside of it is nothing but a light of its ray,

more than in any other, the mind of each one who seeks the truth on which this proof is founded must be moved by love.

Let him who demonstrates to me the first love of all sempiternal substances proclaim such truth to my intellect.

Let him proclaim the voice of the true author, who says to Moses, speaking of himself: 'I will make you see every value.'

Let him proclaim to me, too, beginning the loud prophecy that proclaims the secret from here below above every other proclamation.

And I heard: 'Through the human intellect and through authority in harmony with it, guard the sovereignty of your loves toward God.

But tell me also if you feel other strings pulling you toward him, so that you may play with how many teeth this love bites you."

The holy intention of Christ's eagle was not latent; rather, I realized where it wanted to lead my profession.

So I began again: "All those bites that can turn the heart to God have converged on my charity:

for the existence of the world and my existence, the death he endured so that I might live, and what every faithful person like me hopes for,

with the aforementioned living knowledge, have drawn me from the sea of ​​crooked love, and placed me on the shore of the right one.

The leaves with which the entire garden of the eternal gardener is filled, I love as much as good is brought to them by him."

As I fell silent, a sweet song resounded through the sky, and my lady said with the others: "Holy, holy, holy!"

And as the spirit of vision is roused by a sharp light, running to the splendor that goes from skirt to skirt,

and the awakened one abhors what it sees, so sudden wakefulness is numb until appreciation comes to its aid;

so Beatrice drove every speck from my eyes with the ray of hers, which shone from more than a thousand miles away:

wherefore better than before I saw later; and almost astonished, I asked about a fourth light I saw between us.

And my lady: "Within those rays, its Maker longs for the soul before the first virtue ever created."

Like a leaf that bends its tip in the passing wind, and then rises by its own power that sublimates it,

I stood there, amazed, as she spoke, and then a burning desire to speak reassured me.

And I began: "O apple that was only a ripe product, O ancient father to whom every wife is daughter and son,

Devoted as I can, I beg you to speak to me: you see my desire, and to hear you quickly I do not speak it."

Sometimes a covered animal quarrels, so that affection must appear by the following of its desire;

and similarly the primal soul made me see through the cover how joyfully it came to please me.

Then he breathed: "Without having been offered to me by you, I discern your desire better than you do anything more certain to you;

because I see it in the true mirror that makes itself comparable to other things, and nothing makes itself comparable.

You wish to hear how long God placed me in the lofty garden, where she placed you on such a long ladder,

and how much delight it brought to my eyes, and the very cause of my great disdain, and the language I used and made.

Now, my son, it was not the tasting of the wood itself that caused such exile, but only the passing of the mark.

Therefore, whence your lady, Virgil, moved, I desired only four thousand three hundred and two volumes of this council;

And I saw him return to all the lights of his path nine hundred and thirty times, while I was on earth.

The language I spoke was completely extinguished before Nimrod's people were attentive to the inconsumable work:

since no effect ever rationed, for the human pleasure that renews following the sky, was ever lasting.

It is a natural work that man speaks; but thus or thus, nature leaves you to do as it pleases you.

Before I descended to the infernal anguish, I was called on earth by the supreme good from which comes the joy that swathes me;

and then He called Himself: and this is fitting, for the custom of mortals is like a leaf on a branch, which goes away and another comes.

On the mountain that rises highest from the waves, I was, with a life pure and dishonest, from the first hour to the second,

as the sun changes its quarter, the sixth hour.

Paradiso · Canto XXVII

"To the Father, to the Son, to the Holy Spirit," it began, "glory!" all Paradise, so that the sweet song intoxicated me.

What I saw seemed to me a laughter of the universe, so that my intoxication entered through hearing and sight.

Oh joy! Oh ineffable joy! Oh life whole of love and peace! Oh secure riches without desire!

Before my eyes the four torches were burning, and the one that came first began to grow brighter,

and its appearance became such as Jupiter would become if he and Mars were birds and changed feathers.

Provence, which there distributes vice and office, had placed silence on all sides in the blessed choir,

when I heard: "If I change color, do not marvel, for, as I speak, you will see all these change color.

He who usurps my place on earth, my place, my place, which is vacant in the presence of the Son of God,

has made my cemetery a cesspool of blood and stench; where the wicked man who fell from above is calmed down there.

Then I saw the whole sky covered with that color that the adverse sun paints in the evening and the morning.

And like a chaste lady who remains confident in herself, and yet, hearing of another's failings, becomes timid,

so Beatrice's appearance changed; and such an eclipse, I believe, occurred in heaven when she suffered the supreme power.

Then her words continued, with a voice so transformed by herself that her appearance no longer changed:

"The bride of Christ was not raised with my blood, with that of Linus, with that of Cletus, to be used for the purchase of gold;

but for the purchase of this happy life, Sixtus, Pius, Calixtus, and Urban shed their blood after much mourning.

It was not our intention that one side of the Christian people should sit on the right hand of our successors, and one side on the other;

nor that the keys granted to me should become a sign on a banner to fight against the baptized;

nor that I should be a seal for sold and lying privileges, which I often blush and blaze with.

Ravenous wolves are seen up here in the guise of shepherds throughout all the pastures: O defense of God, why do you lie?

The Caorsini and Guaschi prepare to drink of our blood: O good beginning, to what vile end must you fall!

But the high Providence, which with Scipio defended the glory of the world in Rome, will soon come to its aid, as I conceive;

and you, son, who through mortal weight will return again, open your mouth, and do not hide what I do not hide.

Just as frozen vapors shower down our air when the horn of the goat of heaven touches the sun,

so above I saw the ethereal adorn itself and shower with triumphant vapors that had made our sojourn there.

My sight followed his features, and continued until the middle, through the depths, was taken away from him by the passing of the most advanced.

Then the lady, who saw me freed from waiting above, said to me: "Fix your face and look how you have turned."

From the hour I had first gazed, I saw myself moved along the entire arc that makes the primeval climate from its middle to its end;

so that beyond Gade I saw Ulysses' mad passage, and on this side, near the shore where Europa became sweetly burdened.

And the site of this flowerbed was more visible to me; but the sun was proceeding under my feet in a more distant sign.

My enamoured mind, which always consorted with my lady, burned more than ever to return my eyes to her;

and if nature or art created pastures to catch the eyes, to have the mind, in human flesh or in her paintings,

all gathered together, they would seem nothing compared to the divine pleasure that shone upon me when I turned to her smiling face.

And the power that gazed upon me tore me from Leda's beautiful nest and drove me into the swiftest heaven.

Its most living and sublime parts are so uniform that I cannot say which Beatrice chose for me.

But she, who saw my desire, began, laughing so joyfully that God seemed to rejoice in her face:

"The nature of the world, which quiets the center and moves all else around, begins here as from its goal;

and this heaven has no other where than the divine mind, in which the love that turns it and the power that pours forth are kindled.

It encompasses light and love within one circle, as this does the others; and that precinct alone is understood by him who encircles it.

Its motion is not distinct from anything else, but the others are measured by this, as ten is by a half and a fifth;

and how time holds its roots in such a body and its leaves in the others, can now be made clear to you.

O greed, which sinks mortals so beneath you that no one has the power to lift his eyes from your waves!

Will flourishes well in men; but the constant rain turns true wives into stumps.

Faith and innocence are discovered only in infants; then each flees before its cheeks are covered.

One, still stammering, fasts, who then devours, with unbound tongue, any food under any moon;

and one, stammering, loves and listens to his mother, who, with complete speech, then longs to see her buried.

Thus the white skin turns black at the first glance of the beautiful daughter of him who brings morning and leaves evening.

You, lest you marvel, consider that on earth there is no one to govern; hence the human family goes so astray.

But before January is completely overwintered by the hundredth that is neglected down there, these supernal circles will shine so brightly,

that the fortune that is so longed for will turn its breasts where the prows are, so that the class will run straight;

and true fruit will come after the flower.

Paradiso · Canto XXVIII

After the truth was revealed to me, to the present life of wretched mortals, that which my mind marvels at,

as in a mirror he sees the flame of a glass, who lights up behind it before he has it in sight or in thought,

and turns to see if the glass tells him the truth, and sees that it accords with it as a note with its meter;

so my memory recalls what I did gazing into the beautiful eyes from which Love made the cord to seize me.

And as I turned and mine were touched by what appears in that volume, whenever one gazes closely at its circle,

I saw a point that radiated a light so keen that the face it inflames must close because of its strong acuity;

And whatever star seems smaller here would seem the moon, placed with it as star is placed with star.

Perhaps as close as the light that paints it appears to surround it when the vapor that carries it is thickest,

Distant around the point, a circle of fire was whirling so swiftly that it would have overcome the motion that most quickly encircles the world;

and this was circumscribed by another, and that by the third, and the third by the fourth, and then by the fifth by the fourth, and then by the sixth by the fifth.

Above followed the seventh, already spread out so wide that the entire messenger of Juno would have been too weak to contain it.

So did the eighth and the ninth; and each moved more slowly, according as it was further from the first in number;

and that one had the most sincere flame, the one least distant from the pure spark, I believe, because it is more true than it.

My lady, who saw me deeply in suspense, said: "On that point depends the heavens and all nature.

Look at that circle which is most closely connected to it; and know that its motion is so swift because of the fiery love that pierces it."

And I to her: "If the world were arranged in the order I see in those wheels, what is proposed to me would have satisfied me;

but in the sensible world one can see the vaults as all the more divine, the more remote they are from the center.

Therefore, if my desire is to find its end in this marvelous and angelic temple whose only boundary is love and light,

I must also hear how the example and the exemplar do not go together, for I contemplate this in vain for myself."

"If your fingers are not sufficient for this knot, it is no wonder: so firm, not to try, is it made!"

Thus my lady; then she said: "Take what I will tell you, if you want to satiate yourself; and around it, thin yourself out.

The bodily circles are wide and limber according to the greater or lesser virtue that extends through all their parts.

Greater goodness means greater health; greater health means greater body, if its parts are equally complete.

Therefore, this one who takes all the other universe with him corresponds to the circle he loves most and knows most:

Therefore, if you base your measure on virtue, not on the appearance of the substances that appear round to you,

you will see a wondrous consequence of greater to greater and less to less, in each heaven, according to his intelligence.

Just as the hemisphere of the air remains splendid and serene when Boreas blows from that cheek where it is sweetest,

so that the turmoil that previously disturbed it is purged and resolved, so that the heavens smile with the beauties of each of its forms;

so I did, after my lady provided me with her clear answer, and the truth was seen like a star in heaven.

And after her words were finished, boiling iron sparkles no differently than the circles sparkle.

Its fire followed every spark; and there were so many that their number was more numerous than the doubling of the chessboards.

I heard chorus after chorus cheering the fixed point that holds them to their places, and always will, where they always were.

And she who saw the doubtful thoughts in my mind said: "The first circles have shown you Seraphs and Cherubim.

So swiftly do their vines follow, to resemble the point as much as they can; and they can as much as they are sublime in seeing.

Those other loves that surround them are called Thrones of the divine aspect, whereby the first ternary ends;

and you must know that all delight in the depths of their vision in the truth wherein every intellect rests.

From this we can see how blessedness is founded on the act of seeing, not on that which loves, which then follows;

and the measure of seeing is a reward, which grace and good will give birth to: thus we proceed from step to step.

The other ternary, which thus sprouts in this everlasting spring that nocturnal Aries does not strip,

perpetually sings 'Hosanna' with three melodies, which sound in three orders of joy from which it is internalized.

In this hierarchy are the other goddesses: first the Dominions, and then the Virtues; the third order is that of Podestades.

Then in the two penultimate triumphs, Principalities and Archangels revolve; the last is all of Angelic games.

These orders are all admired from above, and from below they conquer so that all are drawn and all draw toward God.

And Dionysius set himself to contemplate these orders with such longing that he named and distinguished them, as I do.

But Gregory then separated from him; whereupon, as soon as he opened his eyes in this heaven, he laughed to himself.

And if so much secret truth was uttered by a mortal on earth, I do not want him to marvel: for he who saw it up here revealed it to him

with much else of the truth of these circles."

Paradiso · Canto XXIX

When both sons of Latona, covered by the Ram and the Scales, together form the horizon,

as far as from the point where the apex rises to the point where both, changing hemispheres, lift themselves from that circle,

so far, with her face painted with laughter, Beatrice fell silent, gazing fixedly at the point that had vanquished me.

Then he began: "I say, and do not ask, what you wish to hear, for I have seen it there where every ubi and every quando is pointed.

Not to gain any good for itself, which cannot be, but so that its splendor might, shining, say 'I submit,'

in its eternity of time, outside of all else, as it pleased, eternal love opened itself in new love.

Nor did it first lie almost torpid; for neither before nor after proceeded the discourse of God upon these waters.

Form and matter, joined and pure, emerged into being without fault, like three arrows from a three-stringed bow.

And just as in glass, amber, or crystal a ray shines so brightly that there is no interval between its coming and its being,

so the threefold effect of its Lord radiated forth into its being, all at once, without distinction at its origin.

Order and construction were concretly created in the substances; and they were the summit in the world in which pure act was produced;

pure power held the first part; in the middle it held power with such act that it can never be divided.

Jerome wrote to you for centuries about the angels created before the other world was created;

but this truth is written on many pages by the writers of the Holy Spirit, and you will perceive it if you look carefully;

and reason also sees it somewhat, which would not grant that the movers without its perfection were so great.

Now you know where and when these loves were created and how: so that already three ardors are quenched in your desire.

Nor will they, in counting, reach the twentieth as quickly as a part of the angels disturbed the subject of your nourishment.

The other remained, and began this art that you discern, with such delight that it never departs from its circling.

The beginning of the fall was the accursed pride of him whom you saw constrained by all the burdens of the world.

Those you see here were modest in recognizing themselves from the goodness that had made them so ready to understand:

their sights were exalted by illuminating grace and by their merit, so that they have firm and full will;

and I do not want you to doubt, but be certain, that receiving grace is meritorious according to the affection that is open to it.

Now you can contemplate much about this consistory, if my words are understood, without other help.

But since on earth in your schools it is read that the angelic nature is such that it understands, remembers, and wills,

I will say more, so that you may see the pure truth that is confused down there, equivocating in such a reading.

These substances, once they were joyful in the face of God, did not turn their gaze from it, from which nothing is hidden.

Therefore, they have no vision cut off by a new object, and therefore they must not remember with divided thought.

So down there, not sleeping, one dreams, believing and disbelieving to speak the truth; but in the one there is greater guilt and greater shame.

You do not go down a path philosophizing: so transports you are the love of appearance and its thought!

And even this up here is treated with less disdain than when the divine Scripture is postponed or when it is distorted.

One does not consider how much blood it costs to spread it in the world and how much pleasure it brings to those who humbly approach it.

To appear, everyone strives and makes his own inventions; and these are passed over by the preachers and the Gospel is silent.

One says that the moon was turned during the Passion of Christ and was interposed, so that the light of the sun was not shown below;

and he is right, for the light was hidden by itself: therefore, to the Spaniards and the Indians, as to the Jews, such an eclipse answered.

Florence does not have as many Lapi and Bindi as such fables are shouted here and there in the pulpit every year:

so that the sheep, who do not know, return from the pasture fed on the wind, and not seeing it is no excuse.

Christ did not say to his first convent: "Go and preach nonsense to the world," but he gave them a true foundation;

and that sounded so much in his cheeks, that he fought with shield and spear to kindle faith in the Gospel.

Now they go preaching with jokes and jokes, and as long as they laugh well, they puff out their hoods and ask for no more.

But such a bird nests in its beak that, if the common people saw it, they would see the forgiveness in which it confides:

Thus such foolishness has grown on earth that, without proof from any witness, every promise would be made.

On this, the swine Saint Anthony fattens, and many others who are even more swinish, paying with unstamped money.

But since we have digressed too far, let us now turn our eyes to the straight road, so that the path may shorten with time.

This nature grows so far in number that never was mortal speech or concept capable of so much;

And if you look at what is revealed through Daniel, you will see that a certain number is hidden in its thousands.

The first light, which radiates all, is received in as many ways as there are splendors to one who appears to him.

Therefore, since the act of conception is followed by affection, the sweetness of love is diversely fervent and warm within it.

See now the exalted and the breadth of the eternal value, since it has been made so many mirrors in which it is broken,

one remaining within itself as if before."

Paradiso · Canto XXX

Perhaps half a thousand miles away the sixth hour is burning, and this world already lowers its shadow almost to a level bed,

when the mid-heaven, deep within us, begins to grow so that some star loses its visibility down to this depth;

And as the sun's brightest handmaiden advances ever further, so the heaven closes in from sight to sight, even to the most beautiful.

Just as the triumph that always gleams around the point that vanquished me, seeming enclosed by that which it encloses,

little by little faded from my sight: so that I turned my eyes to Beatrice, seeing nothing, and love forced me.

If all that has been said of her thus far were summed up in one single eulogy, this tale would be too short to provide.

The beauty I saw transcends not only beyond us, but I certainly believe that its Creator alone enjoys it entirely.

By this passage I admit I am more conquered than ever before by any point of her theme, whether comic or tragic:

for, like the sun on a face that trembles most, so the memory of her sweet smile diminishes my mind from myself.

From the first day I saw her face in this life, until this sight, I have not been able to follow my song precisely;

but now I must cease pursuing her beauty, in poetry, as every artist does his last.

Such as I leave to a greater extent than that of my tuba, which concludes its arduous subject,

with the gesture and voice of a nimble leader, he began again: "We have emerged from the greater body into the heaven that is pure light:

intellectual light, full of love; love of true good, full of joy; joy that transcends all sweetness.

Here you will see both armies of paradise, and one in those aspects that you will see at the final judgment."

As a sudden flash that dispels the visual spirits, so that it deprives the eye of its ability to see stronger objects,

so a living light shone around me, and left me wrapped in such a veil of its splendor that nothing appeared to me.

"Always the love that quiets this heaven welcomes into itself with such salvation, to make the candle ready for its flame."

No sooner had these brief words come to me than I realized I was rising above my own strength;

and I was rekindled by a new sight, such that no light is so pure that my eyes could not defend themselves;

and I saw a light in the form of a river, glowing with splendor, between two banks painted in a wondrous springtime.

From this river came living sparks, and on every side they settled in the flowers, like rubies encircling gold;

then, as if intoxicated by the scents, they sank back into the miraculous gush, and as one entered, another issued forth.

"The high desire that now inflames and urges you, to have knowledge of what you see, pleases me the more the more it swells;

but you must drink of this water before such thirst is quenched within you": thus said the sun of my eyes to me.

He also added: "The river and the topazes that flow in and out and the laughter of the grass are shadowy prefaces of their truth.

Not that these things are harsh in themselves; but it is a defect on your part, that you have not yet seen such proud things."

There is no infant who so suddenly turns his face toward the milk, if he wakes much later than usual,

as I did, to make even better mirrors of my eyes, leaning toward the wave that flows so that I may improve there;

And as the gutter of my eyelids drank of it, so it seemed to me that its length had become round.

Then, like people who have been under masks, who appear different than before, if they shed the appearance into which they disappeared,

so the flowers and sparks changed for me into greater festivities, so that I saw both courts of heaven manifest.

O splendor of God, through whom I saw the high triumph of the true kingdom, give me the strength to say how I saw it!

There is a light up there that the Creator makes visible to that creature who only in seeing him finds its peace.

It extends itself in a circular shape, so that its circumference would be too large a girdle for the sun.

All its appearance becomes a ray reflected at the summit of the primeval mobile, which then takes on life and power.

And as a hill reflects its reflection in the water at its base, as if to see itself adorned, when it is full of greenery and flowers,

so, rising above the light all around, I saw reflected in more than a thousand thresholds all that has returned from us up there.

And if the lowest step gathers in itself such great light, how great is the breadth of this rose in its outermost leaves!

My vision was not lost in the expanse and the height, but entirely absorbed the quantity and the quality of that joy.

Near and far, there, neither add nor take away: for where God governs without means, natural law matters nothing.

In the yellow of the everlasting rose, which fades and expands and smells the scent of praise for the ever-wintry sun,

like one who is silent and wants to speak, Beatrice drew me and said: "Look how great is the convent of the white stoles!

See how our city revolves; see our seats so full, that few people desire us anymore.

And in that great chair where you keep your eyes because of the crown already placed there, before you dine at this wedding,

will sit the soul, which will be below in August, of high Henry, who will come to straighten Italy before she is ready.

The blind greed that bewitches you has done similar things to the little boy who dies of hunger and chases away his nurse.

And he will be prefect in the divine forum then, one who will not go with him on the same path, openly or covertly.

But soon afterward he will be suffered by God in the holy office; for he will be expelled there where Simon the Magician is, by his merit,

and he will make the man from Alagna enter deeper.

Paradiso · Canto XXXI

Thus, in the form of a pure rose, the holy militia that Christ espoused in his blood appeared to me;

but the other, which, flying, sees and sings the glory of him who enamoured her and the goodness that made her so great,

like a flock of bees that once adorn themselves with flowers and then return to where their labors are flavored,

descended into the great flower adorned with so many leaves, and then ascended to where their love always abides.

Their faces were all of living flame and their wings of gold, and the other so white that no snow reaches that limit.

When they descended into the flower, from bank to bank they offered the peace and ardor they acquired by fanning their sides.

Nor did the interposition of such a flying multitude between the above and the flower impede the sight and the splendor:

for the divine light penetrates the universe as it deserves, so that nothing can stand in its way.

This secure and joyful kingdom, frequent in ancient and modern peoples, had all its sight and love in one place.

O triune light, that, sparkling in a single star at their sight, so satisfies them! Look down here at our storm!

If the barbarians, coming from that region that every day covers Helice, revolving with her son whom she loves,

seeing Rome and its arduous work, were amazed when Lateran went above mortal things;

I, who had come from the human to the divine, from time to the eternal, and from Florence to a just and healthy people,

of what wonder must have been accomplished! Certainly, between it and the joy, I felt compelled not to hear and to remain silent.

And like a pilgrim who, gazing at the temple of his vow, is taking recreation, and hopes already to tell how it was,

Walking through the living light, I led my eyes along the steps, now up, now down, now recirculating.

I saw faces bent on charity, adorned with the light of others and its smile, and gestures adorned with every dignity.

I had already completely understood the general form of paradise, but nowhere had I yet fixed my gaze;

and I turned with rekindled desire to ask my lady about things that had in suspense in my mind.

I understood one thing, and she answered me another: I thought I saw Beatrice, and I saw a breast dressed in the glorious folk.

A benign joy was diffused through my eyes and breasts, in a pious attitude befitting a tender father.

And "Where is she?" I immediately said. To which he: "Beatrice moved me from my place to fulfill your desire;

and if you look up into the third circle from the highest rank, you will see her again on the throne that her merits have granted her."

Without answering, I raised my eyes and saw her forming a crown for herself, reflecting the eternal rays from herself.

From that region which thunders highest, no mortal eye is so far distant, no one who abandons himself to the sea lowest,

as there from Beatrice my sight; but it did me no harm, for her image did not descend to me by a mixed medium.

"O Lady in whom my hope lives, and who suffered for my salvation to leave your traces in hell,

of so many things as I have seen, from your power and your goodness I recognize the grace and the virtue.

You have drawn me from slavery to freedom by all those ways, by all the means you had the power to do so.

Keep your magnificence in me, so that my soul, which you have made healthy, may, pleasing to you, disengage itself from the body."

So I prayed; and she, as far away as she seemed, smiled and looked at me; then she returned to the eternal fountain.

And the saint said: "So that you may perfectly complete your journey, to which prayer and holy love have sent me,

fly with your eyes through this garden; for seeing it will better equip your gaze to ascend through the divine ray.

And the Queen of Heaven, for whom I burn with love, will grant us every grace, because I am her faithful Bernard."

What man is there who perhaps comes from Croatia to see our Veronica, who, because of her ancient hunger, is never satisfied,

but says in his thoughts, as soon as he appears: 'My Lord Jesus Christ, true God, was your likeness once made like this?'

Such was I, gazing at the lively charity of him who, contemplating in this world, tasted that peace.

"Son of grace, this joyful being," he began, "will not be known to you, keeping your eyes only down here;

but gaze up the circles to the most distant, so that you may see seated the queen to whom this kingdom is subject and devoted."

I raised my eyes; and as in the morning the eastern part of the horizon surpasses that where the sun sets,

so, as if going with my eyes from valley to mountain, I saw a part at the edge surpass in light all the other front.

And as there, where one waits for the pole that Phaeton misguided, it flames more, and on this side and that the light grows dim,

so that peaceful oriaflame in the center was kindled, and on every side its flame was equally slackened;

and in the middle of it, with spread wings, I saw more than a thousand rejoicing angels, each distinguished by its brilliance and art.

I saw a beauty laughing at their games and at their songs, a beauty that was a joy in the eyes of all the other saints;

and if I had as much wealth in speaking as I had in imagining, I would not dare even attempt to describe her delight.

Bernard, when he saw my eyes fixed and attentive in her warm glow, turned his own to her with such affection,

that he made mine more ardent to gaze.

Paradiso · Canto XXXII

Affectionate for her pleasure, that contemplative one assumed the free office of teacher, and began these holy words:

"The wound that Mary closed and anointed, she who is so beautiful at her feet, is she who opened it and who pricked it.

In the order of the third seats, Rachel sits below her with Beatrice, as you see.

Sarah and Rebecca, Judith, and she who was the second wife of the singer who, in pain of his sin, said, "Have mercy on me,"

you can see them descending from threshold to threshold, as I, who in my own name, go down the rose from leaf to leaf.

And from the seventh step down, as far as it goes, come the Hebrews, dividing all the flower's tresses;

because, according to the gaze that faith in Christ cast, these are the wall from which the sacred stairs depart.

On this side, where the flower is ripe with all its leaves, sit those who believed in the coming Christ;

on the other side, where the semicircles are cut with hollows, stand those who had faces for Christ when he came.

And just as on this side the glorious seat of the Lady of Heaven and the other seats below it make such a selection,

so against that of the great John, who always holy endured desert and martyrdom, and then hell for two years;

and below him, in the same way, sorted out Francis, Benedict, and Augustine, and others from here on down, from circle to circle.

Now behold the high divine providence: for both aspects of faith will equally fill this garden.

And know that from the step down that marks the midway point between the two discretions, one sits not through one's own merit,

but through the merit of others, under certain conditions: for all these are spirits listened to before they had true choices.

You can perceive this clearly by their faces and even by their childish voices, if you look at them well and listen to them.

Now you doubt, and doubting, you will; but I will loosen the strong bond with which subtle thoughts bind you.

Within the vastness of this realm, no casual moment can exist, except like sadness, thirst, or hunger:

for by eternal law everything you see is established, so that the ring on your finger rightly responds to it;

and therefore this people, destined for true life, is not without cause within itself more or less excellent here.

The king by whom this kingdom rests in such love and such delight that no will can greater cause,

creating all minds in his joyful aspect, endows them with grace differently at his pleasure; and let the effect suffice here.

And this is clearly and expressly noted in Holy Scripture in those twins who were moved by their mother's anger.

Therefore, according to the color of their hair, the highest light of such grace must be worthily adorned.

Therefore, without mercy to their custom, they are placed in different degrees, differing only in their original acumen.

In recent centuries, along with innocence, the faith of parents alone was sufficient for salvation;

after the first ages were completed, males had to acquire virtue from the innocent feathers of circumcision;
