but after the time of grace came, without the perfect baptism of Christ, such innocence was retained down there.

Look now at the face that most resembles Christ, for its brightness alone can prepare you to see Christ.

I saw such joy rain down upon her, carried in the holy minds created to soar through that height,

that although I had seen it before, it did not suspend me with such admiration, nor showed me such a countenance of God;

and that love that first descended there, singing 'Ave, Maria, full of grace,' spread its wings before her.

The blessed court responded to the divine chant from all sides, so that every sight became more serene.

"O holy Father, who endures for me to be down here, leaving the sweet place where you sit by eternal destiny,

who is that angel who gazes so playfully into the eyes of our queen, so enamoured that he seems to be of fire?"

So I again turned to the teaching of him who adorned Mary as the morning star of the sun.

And he to me: "All the courage and grace that can be in an angel and in a soul is in him; and so we wish it to be,

because he is the one who bore the palm down to Mary, when the Son of God turned to take up our body.

But come now with your eyes, as I continue speaking, and note the great fathers of this most just and pious empire.

Those two who sit up there, happier for being closest to Augusta, are like two roots of this rose:

He who sits on her left is the father, through whose bold taste the human race tastes so bitter;

On the right you see that ancient father of Holy Church, to whom Christ entrusted the keys of this lovely flower.

And he who saw all the hard times, before he died, of the beautiful bride he acquired with lance and hammer,

sits along him, and along the other rests that ruler under whom the ungrateful, fickle, and reluctant people lived on manna.

Opposite Peter you see Anna sitting, so content to gaze upon her daughter that she does not move her eye to sing hosannas;

And opposite the eldest father of the family sits Lucia, who moved your lady when you lowered your brows to ruin.

But since time flies and lulls you to sleep, we will make a stop here, like a good tailor who makes a skirt from cloth of whatever fabric he has;

and we will direct our eyes to our first love, so that, looking toward it, we may penetrate as far as possible through its splendor.

Truly, nor do you perhaps retreat, moving your wings, believing you are surpassing yourself; praying for grace must be obtained

from her who can help you; and you will follow me with affection, so that your heart does not depart from my words.

And he began this holy prayer:

Paradiso · Canto XXXIII

"Virgin Mother, daughter of your son, humble and exalted above all other creatures, fixed goal of eternal counsel,

you are she who so ennobled human nature that its creator did not disdain to become its creation.

In your womb, love was rekindled, by whose heat this flower thus germinated in eternal peace.

Here you are for us the noonday torch of charity, and down among mortals, you are a living fountain of hope.

Lady, you are so great and so powerful, that he who desires grace and does not turn to you, his longing wants to fly without wings.

Your kindness not only helps those who ask, but often freely anticipates their asking.

In you, mercy, in you, pity, in you, magnificence, in you is gathered whatever goodness there is in any creature.

Now this one, who from the lowest depths of the universe to this very day has seen the spiritual lives one by one,

begs you, by grace, for such virtue that with his eyes he may rise higher toward ultimate salvation.

And I, who never burned more for my own sight than I do for his, offer you all my prayers, and I pray that they may not be scanty,

that you may dispel every cloud of his mortality with your prayers, so that the supreme pleasure may be revealed to him.

I also pray you, queen, who can do what you wish, that, after so much seeing, you preserve his affections healthy.

May your guard conquer human movements: see Beatrice with how many blessed ones close their hands to you because of my prayers!

The eyes, beloved and venerated by God, fixed on the orator, showed us how grateful our devout prayers are to her;

then they turned to the eternal light, into which it should not be believed that such a clear eye could be sent by any creature.

And I, who was approaching the end of all desires, as I should, the ardor of desire within me was extinguished.

Bernardo beckoned to me and smiled for me to look up; but I was already as he wished:

for my sight, growing pure, penetrated ever deeper into the ray of the high light that is true in itself.

From then on, my vision was greater than speech shows, which yields to such a sight, and memory yields to such outrage.

As is he who dreaming sees, that after the dream the imprinted passion remains, and the other does not return to the mind,

such am I, for my vision almost entirely ceases, and still distils in my heart the sweetness that was born from it.

So the snow is unsealed by the sun; Thus the Sibyl's words were lost in the wind among the light leaves.

O supreme light, so far removed from mortal thoughts, restore to my mind a little of what you appeared to me,

and make my tongue so powerful that it may leave a single spark of your glory to the people to come;

for by returning a little to my memory and by resounding a little in these verses, more will be conceived of your victory.

I believe, from the keenness I endured from the living ray, that I would be lost if my eyes had been turned from it.

And it reminds me that I was more daring to endure because of this, so much so that my gaze reached infinite value.

Oh abundant grace, by which I presumed to fix my gaze on the eternal light, so much so that I consumed my sight there!

In its depths I saw that within, bound by love in a volume, lies that which is spread out throughout the universe:

substances and accidents and their habits, as it were, fused together, so that what I speak is a simple light.

I believe I saw the universal form of this knot, because, saying this, I feel that I enjoy it more broadly.

A single moment is greater lethargy for me than twenty-five centuries at the feat that made Neptune admire the shade of Argos.

Thus my mind, all suspended, gazed fixedly, motionless and attentive, and was ever kindled to gaze.

One becomes such at that light that to turn from it to another aspect is impossible, ever to consent;

because the good, which is the object of the will, is entirely gathered in it, and outside of it, whatever is perfect there is defective.

From now on, my speech will be shorter, even from what I remember, than that of a servant who still wets his tongue at the breast.

Not because there was more than a simple appearance in the living light I gazed at, which is always as it was before;

But as my vision grew stronger as I gazed, a single appearance, as I changed, troubled me.

In the deep and clear subsistence of the high light, three circles appeared to me, each containing three colors;

and one seemed reflected from the other like ire from ire, and the third seemed like fire that breathes equally from here and there.

Oh, how short is the word, and how feeble to my conception! And this, from what I saw, is so great that it is not enough to say "little."

O eternal light, who alone dwells in yourself, who alone understands yourself, and who, intelligible and understanding, loves and smiles upon yourself!

That circulation, so conceived in you, seemed like a reflected light, somewhat circumspected by my eyes,

within itself, with its own color, seemed to me painted with our image: wherefore my face was entirely absorbed in it.

As is the geometrician who fixes himself entirely on measuring the circle, and cannot, in thinking, find the beginning from which he needs it,

such was I at that new sight: I wanted to see how the image suited the circle and how it fits there;

but my own wings were not for this, except that my mind was struck by a flash in which its desire came.

The power of my lofty imagination here failed; but already my desire and will were turning, like a wheel that is moved equally,

the love that moves the sun and the other stars.
